The Exception: Tamattu' Hady and the Basis of Istihsan
Exception for tamattu' hady based on istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the exception for tamattu' hady in the Hanafi school and apply the principle of istihsan to differentiate this ruling from the general qiyas.

Core Idea
For the tamattu' hady, setting out with the animal alone suffices for ihram, due to istihsan, because this hady is a foundational ritual.

This lesson focuses on the unique treatment of the tamattu' hady. While the general rule requires one to actually drive the animal or catch up to it, the tamattu' hady is an exception: setting out with it is enough to enter ihram. The basis for this is istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides qiyas. The reason is that the tamattu' hady is a ritual ordained from the beginning, specific to Makkah, and obligatory as thanks for combining Hajj and Umrah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the exception
For the budnah of tamattu', the person becomes muhrim upon setting out, even without driving the animal.
This is an exception to the general rule that one must drive or catch up.
2
Understand the qiyas (general rule)
The qiyas would treat all types of hady equally: one must actually drive or catch the animal. This is the default ruling for non-tamattu' hady.
The qiyas is based on the analogy with talbiyah mentioned earlier.
3
Recognize the istihsan
Istihsan departs from qiyas because the tamattu' hady is legislated as a ritual from the start (mashru' min al-ibtida') as a rite of Hajj, unlike other hady that become obligatory due to violations.
This is a stronger consideration that overrides the analogy.
4
Note the wisdom
The tamattu' hady is specific to Makkah and obligatory as thanksgiving for combining Hajj and Umrah. Therefore, setting out with it is enough.
Other hady (e.g., penalty) may be obligatory even if one never reaches Makkah, so they require actual action.

Source Text

جس نے بدن خواہ نفلی ہو یا نذر کا یا شکار کی جزا ہوں کو قلادہ ڈالا اور حج کے ارادے سے چل پڑا وہ محرم ہے خواہ تلبیہ پڑھے یا نہ پڑھے
قَالَ وَمَنْ قَلَّدَ بُدَنَةً تَطَوُّعًا أو نَدْرًا أَوْ جَزَاءَ صَيدَا وَشَيْئًا مِنَ الْأَشْيَاءِ وَ تَوَجَّهَ مَعَهَا يُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ فَقَدْ أَحْرَمَ لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَام مَنْ قَلَّدَ بَدَنَةً فَقَدْ أحْرَمَ وَلانَ سَوقَ الْهَدْي فِى مَعْنَى التلييَةِ فِي إِظْهَارِ إِلَّا جَابَةِ لِأَنَّهُ لَا يَفْعَلُهُ إِلَّا مَنْ يُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ أَوِ الْعُمْرَةَ وَإِظْهَارُ الْإِجَابَةِ قَدْ يَكُونُ بِالْفِعْلِ كَمَا يَكُونُ بِالْقَوْلِ فَيَصِيرُ بِهِ مُحْرِ مَا لا تُصَالِ النِّيَّةِ بِفِعْلِ هُوَ مِنْ خَصَائِصِ الْإِحْرَامِ وَ صِفَةُ التَّقْلِيدِ أنْ تَرْبِطَ عَلَى عُنْقِ بَدَنَتِهِ قِطَعَةَ نَعِل أَوْ عَرَوَةَ مُرَادَةٍ أَو لِحَاءَ شَجَرَةٍ
ترجمہ امام محمد نے (جامع صغیر ) میں کہا کہ اور جس شخص نے بدنہ کو تقلید کیا ب نہ خواہ نفی ہو یا نذر کا ہو یا شکار کے جرمانہ کا ہو یا انٹیلومیں سے اور کسی چیز کا ہو ۔ اور بدنہ کے ساتھ خود متوجہ ہو اس حال میں کہ وہ خود حج کا ارادہ کرتا ہے تو اس کا احرام ہو گیا ۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا ہے کہ جس نے بدنہ تقلید کیا وہ محرم ہو گیا اور اس لئے کہ قبولیت کا جواب دینے میں ہدی چلانا تلبیہ کے معنی رکھتا ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ کام وہی شخص کرتا ہے جو حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو اور قبولیت کا اظہار بھی فعل سے ہوتا ہے جیسا کہ قول سے ہوتا ہے بس تقلید سے محرم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ نیت ایسے فعل کے ساتھ متصل ہے جو احرام کے خصائص میں سے ہے۔ اور تقلید کی صورت یہ ہے کہ اپنے بد نہ کی گردن پر جوتی کا ٹکڑایا کی لوٹے کا دستہ یا درخت کی چھال باندھ دے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی بدنہ کے گلے میں قلادہ ڈالا ہ نہ نکلی ہو یائڈ رکا ہو یا گذشتہ کبھی احترام کی حالت میں شکار کرنے کی وجہ سے جر مانہ کا جانور و یادم تمت وغیرہ ہو اور شیخین کے ارادے سے اپنے بد نہ کے ساتھ مکہ المکرمہ کی طرف روانہ بھی ہو گیا، تو یہ محرم ہو گیا ، زبان سے تلبیہ کہا ہو یا نہ کہا ہو۔ پہلی دلیل تو رسول خدا صلى الله عليه وسلم کا ارشاد ہے ۔ مَن قَلدَ بُدَنَةً فَقَدْ أَحْرَمَ . دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ دعا ، ابراہیم کی قبولیت کا جواب دینے میں بدی چلانا، تلبیت معنی میں ہے۔ کیونکہ سوتی بدی کا عمل وہی کرتا ہے جو حج یا عمرہ کا ارادہ رکھتا ہو۔ قبولیت کا اظہار چونکہ جس طرح قول یعنی تلبیہ سے ہوتا ہے اس طرح فعل یعنی سوق بدی سے بھی ہوتا ہے اس لئے یہ شخص سوق بدی سے محرم ہو جائے گا۔ کیونکہ نیت حج ایسے فعل کے ساتھ متصل ہو گئی ہے جو فعل احرام کی خصوصیات میں سے ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ تقلید کی صورت یہ ہے کہ بدنہ کے گلے میں جوتے کا ٹکڑا یا لوٹے کا دستہ یا درخت کی چھال ڈال دی جائے۔ جس نے بدنہ کو قلادہ ڈالا اور اس کو بھیج دیا خود نہیں گیا تو وہ محرم نہیں ہے
فَإِنْ قَلَّدَهَا وَبَعَثَ بِهَا وَلَمْ يَسُقُهَا لَمْ يَصِرُ مُحْرِمًا لِمَارُوِيَ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ كُنْتُ أَفْتِلُ قَلَائِدَهَدَى رَسُولِ فَبَعَثَ بِهَا وَأَقَامَ فِى أَهْلِهِ حَلَا لَا فَإِنْ تَوَجَّهَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَصِرُ مُحْرِمًا حَتَّى يَلْحَقَهَا لِأَنَّ عِنْدَ التَّوَجَهِ إِذَا لَم يَكُن بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ هَدَى يَسُوقُهُ لَمْ يُوجَدُ مِنْهُ إِلَّا مُجَرَّدُ النّيَةِ وَبِمُجَرِّدِ النّيَةِ لَا يَصِيرُ مُحرَّمًا فَإِذَا أُدْرَكَهَا وَسَاقَهَا أَوْ أَدْرَكَهَا فَقَدْ اقْتَرَنَتْ نِيَّتُهُ بِعَمَلٍ هُوَ مِنْ خَصَائِصِ الْإِحْرَامِ فَيَصِيرُ مُحْرِمًا كَمَا لَوْ سَا فَهَا فِي الْابْتِدَاءِ قَالَ إِلَّا فِي بُدُنَةِ الْمُتَعَةِ فَإِنَّهُ مُحْرِمْ حِيْنَ تَوَجَّهَ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا نَوَى الإِحْرَامَ وَهذَا اِسْتِحْسَانَ وَجهُ الْقِيَاسِ فِيهِ مَادَ كَرُنَا وَوَجهُ الاسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ هَذَا الْهَدْيَ مَشْرُوعٌ عَلَى الْإِبْتِدَاءِ نُسَكًا مِنْ مَناسِكِ الْحَقِّ وَضْعًا لِأَنَّهُ يَخْتَصُّ بِمَكَّةَ وَيَجِبُ شُكْرَ اللجَمع بَيْنَ أدَاءِ النُّسُكَيْنِ وَغَيْرَهُ قَدْ يَجِبُ بِالْجَنايَةِ وَإِنَّ لَمْ يَصِلُ إِلَى مَكَّةَ فَلِهذَا اكْتُفِي فِيهِ بِالتَّوَجُهِ وَفِي غَيْرِهِ تَوُقِّفَ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْفِعْلَ
ترجمہ پس اگر اس نے بدنہ کو قلادہ پہنایا اور اس کو بھیجا لیکن خود نہیں چلایا تو وہ محرم نہ ہوگا کیونکہ حضرت عائشہ سے مروی ہے۔ انہوں نے کہا کہ میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بدی کے قلاده گردن بند ) کو ملتی تھی پھر آپ نے بدی کو بھیج دیا اور خود اپنے اہل میں بحالت حلال ٹھہرے رہے پھر اگر اس کے بعد خود بھی متوجہ ہوا تو محرم نہ ہوگا۔ یہاں تک کہ بدی کے جانور میں جا کر مل جائے ۔ کیونکہ روانہ ہونے کے وقت جبکہ اس کے روبرو ہدی نہ ہو کہ اس کو چلائے تو اس کی طرف سے سوائے نیت کے کچھ نہیں پایا گیا۔ اور محض نیست سے محرم نہیں ہوتا۔ پھر جب ہدی کو پایا اور اس کو چلایا یا ہدی کو فقط پالیا تو اس کی نیت ایسے عمل کے ساتھ مقترن ہو گئی جو احرام کے خصائص میں سے ہے لہذا محرم ہو جائے گا۔ جیسے اگر ابتداء میں ہدی کو چلایا کہا مگر متعہ کے بدلہ میں اس لئے کہ یہ روانہ ہوتے ہی محرم ہو جائے گا۔ مراد یہ ہے کہ جب احرام کی نیت کی ہو اور یہ استحسان ہے اور قیاس کی وجہ اس میں وہ ہے جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ یہ ہدی ابتداء مناسک حج میں سے ایک نسک بنا کر شریعت نے وضع کی ہے۔ کیونکہ یہ ہدی مکہ کے ساتھ مختص ہے اور دونسک ( حج و عمرہ) جمع کرنے پر بطور شکرانہ واجب ہے اور بدی تمتع کے علاوہ کبھی جنایت کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتی ہے۔ اگر چہ مکہ کو نہ پہنچے اسی وجہ سے ہدی تمتع میں توجہ پر اکتفاء کیا اور ہدی متعہ کے علاوہ میں حقیقت فعل پر موقوف ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے ہدی کے جانور کو قلادہ پہنا کر مکتہ المکرمہ کی طرف بھیج دیا لیکن اس کو بذات خود نہیں بنایا تو وہ اس سے محرم نہ ہوگا۔ دلیل حدیث عائشہ ہے انہوں نے فرمایا کہ میں رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کے بدی کا قلادہ بناتی تھی اور رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم ہدی کے جانور کو بھیج کر خود اپنے گھر بحالت حلال قیام فرماتے تھے اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ محرم ہونے کے لئے فقط ہدی کے جانور کا بھیجنا کافی نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کو خود لے کر جانا ضروری ہے۔ اور اگر ہدی کا جانور بھیجنے کے بعد خود روانہ ہوا تو محض روانہ ہونے سے محرم نہ ہوگا۔ بلکہ محرم اس وقت ہو گا جب ہدی سے جا کر مل جائے۔ کیونکہ اس کے روانہ ہوتے وقت اس کے روبرو کوئی ہدی نہیں جس کو وہ چلائے۔
Whoever marked a budnah, whether voluntary, vowed, or penalty for hunting, and anything, and set out with it intending Hajj, then he has entered ihram. For his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever marks a budnah has entered ihram.' And because driving the hady is like talbiyah in showing acceptance. For no one does it except one who intends Hajj or Umrah. And showing acceptance may be by action as it is by speech. So he becomes muhrim by it due to the connection of intention with an action that is from the characteristics of ihram. And the description of taqlid is that he ties on the neck of his budnah a piece of sandal or the handle of a small vessel or tree bark. Translation: Imam Muhammad said in al-Jami' al-Saghir: And whoever performed taqlid on a budnah, whether voluntary, vowed, or penalty for hunting, and set out with it intending Hajj, then his ihram is established. Because the Prophet said: 'Whoever marks a budnah has entered ihram.' And because driving the hady is like talbiyah in meaning of answering the call. For only one who intends Hajj or Umrah does this act. And showing acceptance may be by action just as by speech. So by taqlid he becomes muhrim. For intention is connected with an action that is from the characteristics of ihram. And the form of taqlid is that he ties on the neck of his budnah a piece of sandal or handle of a small vessel or tree bark. Explanation: If someone puts a necklace on his budnah, whether it is a voluntary budnah, or a vowed one, or an animal for penalty for hunting, or a hady tamattu', and sets out with his budnah towards Makkah intending Hajj, then he becomes muhrim whether he said talbiyah or not. First proof: the hadith. Second proof: Driving the hady is like talbiyah in meaning of responding to the call. Because only one who intends Hajj or Umrah does this act. Since showing acceptance is by action as by speech, this person becomes muhrim by driving the hady. For intention of Hajj is connected with an action that is from the characteristics of ihram. The author of al-Hidayah says: The form of taqlid is to put on the budnah's neck a piece of sandal or handle of a small vessel or tree bark. If one marked the budnah and sent it but did not drive it himself, he is not muhrim. For if he marked it and sent it and did not drive it, he does not become muhrim, due to what is narrated from Aisha that she said: 'I used to twist the necklaces of the hady of the Messenger (peace be upon him), then he sent it and remained with his family in a halal state.' Then if he set out after that, he does not become muhrim until he catches up with it. Because at the time of setting out, when there is no hady before him that he is driving, nothing is found from him except mere intention, and by mere intention he does not become muhrim. Then when he catches up with it and drives it, or catches up with it, his intention becomes connected with an action that is from the characteristics of ihram, so he becomes muhrim, just as if he had driven it from the beginning. He (Imam Muhammad) said: Except in the case of the budnah of tamattu', for he is muhrim at the moment he sets out, meaning if he intends ihram. This is istihsan. The qiyas in it is what we mentioned. The istihsan basis is that this hady is legislated from the beginning as a ritual from the rituals of Hajj, because it is specific to Makkah and is obligatory as thanksgiving for combining two rituals, whereas other hady may be obligatory due to a violation even if one does not reach Makkah. Therefore, in the tamattu' hady, one is content with setting out, while in other types, it depends on actual action. Translation: So if he put the necklace on the budnah and sent it but did not himself drive it, he does not become muhrim, because it is narrated from Aisha that she said: 'I used to twist the necklaces of the hady of the Messenger (peace be upon him), then he sent it and remained with his family in a halal state.' Then if after that he himself set out, he does not become muhrim until he catches up with the animal. Because at the time of setting out, when there is no hady before him that he drives, nothing is found from him except intention, and by mere intention he does not become muhrim. Then when he catches up with it and drives it, or merely catches up with it, his intention becomes connected with an action from the characteristics of ihram, so he becomes muhrim, just as if he had driven it from the beginning. He said: Except for the budnah of tamattu', for he becomes muhrim at the moment of setting out, meaning if he intends ihram. This is istihsan. The qiyas in it is what we mentioned. The istihsan basis is that this hady is legislated from the beginning as a ritual from the rituals of Hajj, because it is specific to Makkah and is obligatory as thanksgiving for combining the two rituals, whereas other hady may become obligatory due to violation even if one does not reach Makkah. Therefore, in the tamattu' hady, setting out alone suffices, and in other types it depends on actual action. Explanation: If someone puts a necklace on his hady and sends it to Makkah but does not personally accompany it, he does not become muhrim. The proof is the hadith of Aisha: she used to make necklaces for the hady of the Prophet, and he would send it while staying at home in a halal state. This shows that sending the animal alone is not sufficient for ihram; one must personally take it. And if he sets out after sending it, he does not become muhrim merely by setting out; rather, he becomes muhrim when he catches up with the hady. Because at the time of his setting out, there is no hady before him to drive.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on entering ihram through the act of taqlid (marking) a sacrificial animal. The text begins by stating the general ruling: whoever performs taqlid on a budnah (sacrificial animal) and sets out with it intending Hajj becomes muhrim, even if he does not recite talbiyah. The proof is the hadith: 'Whoever marks a budnah has entered ihram.' A secondary proof is that driving the hady (sacrificial animal) is similar to saying talbiyah in that both express acceptance of the call to Hajj. The author then describes the method of taqlid: tying a piece of sandal, a loop of a small vessel, or tree bark on the animal's neck. Next, the text discusses a sub-case: if one marks the animal and sends it to Makkah without personally accompanying it, he does not become muhrim. This is supported by the practice of the Prophet as narrated by Aisha. If after sending it he sets out, he remains halal until he catches up with the animal and drives it (or merely catches up), because before that he only had intention without an action specific to ihram. An exception is made for the hady of tamattu' (Hajj performed after Umrah): in that case, one becomes muhrim upon setting out with the animal, even without driving it. This is based on istihsan (juristic preference) because the tamattu' hady is a ritual from the beginning, specific to Makkah and obligatory as thanks for combining Hajj and Umrah. In contrast, other types of hady (e.g., penalty for hunting) are contingent on reaching Makkah, so the mere setting out does not suffice. The qiyas (analogy) would treat all hady equally, but istihsan differentiates the tamattu' hady due to its nature as a foundational ritual.

Key Terms
متعہ (tamattu'): Performing Umrah during Hajj season, then Hajj in the same year with a sacrifice
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference departing from qiyas for a stronger reason
ہدی (hady): Sacrificial animal sent to the Haram

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for the exception for tamattu' hady?
A) Explicit hadith
B) Analogy with talbiyah
C) Istihsan
D) Consensus

Key Takeaway
For the tamattu' hady, setting out alone suffices for ihram due to istihsan, as this hady is a foundational ritual of Hajj.

Sending Hady Ahead with Qiladah Does Not Constitute Ihram
Ruling on sending hady ahead without accompanying it

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that sending a hady with a qiladah does not constitute ihram and identify the condition under which one becomes muhrim when the hady is sent ahead.

Core Idea
Sending the hady alone does not make one muhrim; leading the animal is an essential action for ihram.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a common question: does sending a sacrificial animal ahead to Mecca automatically put you into ihram? The Hanafi school says no, based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ. Let's walk through the ruling and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
What specific act is being ruled upon? Sending a hady with a qiladah (necklace) but without driving it (sawq). The ruling: this does not make the person a muhrim.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Aisha (RA) that she used to twist the qalaid of the Prophet's hady, and he would send it while remaining halal (non-muhrim) with his family.
The hadith is cited as evidence that sending alone does not entail ihram.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the hadith prove the ruling? The Prophet's action shows that sending the hady, even with taqlid, does not by itself make one muhrim. He remained in a non-muhrim state until he personally went forth and presumably led the animal.
The specific phrase 'wa aqama fi ahlihi halalan' (he stayed with his family as a non-muhrim) is the key evidence.
4
Note the exception: setting out and catching up
If the person later sets out for Hajj, he does not become muhrim until he catches up with the hady (yalhaqaha) and either drives it or simply meets it. At that point, his intention connects with the specific action of leading the hady, and he becomes muhrim.
This is analogous to driving the hady from the beginning.
5
Understand the principle
The underlying principle is that intention alone (mujarrad al-niyyah) is insufficient to enter ihram in this context. A specific action characteristic of ihram (leading the hady) is also required.
This is a Hanafi distinctive position; other madhhabs may hold different views.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ قَلَّدَهَا وَبَعَثَ بِهَا وَلَمْ يَسُقْهَا لَمْ يَصِرْ مُحْرِمًا لِمَا رُوِيَ عَنْ عَائِشَةَ أَنَّهَا قَالَتْ كُنْتُ أَفْتِلُ قَلَائِدَ هَدْيِ رَسُولِ اللَّهِ فَبَعَثَ بِهَا وَأَقَامَ فِي أَهْلِهِ حَلَالاً فَإِنْ تَوَجَّهَ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ لَمْ يَصِرْ مُحْرِمًا حَتَّى يَلْحَقَهَا لِأَنَّ عِنْدَ التَّوَجُّهِ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ بَيْنَ يَدَيْهِ هَدْيٌ يَسُوقُهُ لَمْ يُوجَدْ مِنْهُ إِلَّا مُجَرَّدُ النِّيَّةِ وَبِمُجَرَّدِ النِّيَّةِ لَا يَصِيرُ مُحْرِمًا فَإِذَا أَدْرَكَهَا وَسَاقَهَا أَوْ أَدْرَكَهَا فَقَدْ اقْتَرَنَتْ نِيَّتُهُ بِعَمَلٍ هُوَ مِنْ خَصَائِصِ الْإِحْرَامِ فَيَصِيرُ مُحْرِمًا كَمَا لَوْ سَاقَهَا فِي الِابْتِدَاءِ
If he puts a qiladah on it (the hady) and sends it but does not drive it, he does not become a muhrim due to what is narrated from Aisha that she said: 'I used to twist the qalaid of the hady of the Messenger of Allah, and he sent it while staying with his family as a non-muhrim.' Then if he sets out after that, he does not become a muhrim until he catches up with it because at the time of setting out, if there is no hady before him which he drives, nothing is found from him except mere intention, and by mere intention he does not become a muhrim. When he catches up with it and drives it, or catches up with it, then his intention has become connected with an action that is from the specific characteristics of ihram, so he becomes a muhrim, just as if he had driven it from the beginning.
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
This is a ruling from Al-Hidayah on the conditions for entering ihram through sending a sacrificial animal (hady). The general rule is that merely sending the animal with a qiladah (necklace) does not make one a muhrim. The proof is the hadith of Aisha (RA) that the Prophet (SAW) would send his hady to Mecca while remaining in a non-muhrim state himself. If a person sends the animal and later sets out himself, he remains a non-muhrim until he physically meets the animal and either drives it or simply encounters it, because his intention to become muhrim must be accompanied by an action specific to ihram—namely, leading the hady. Without that action, only intention exists, and intention alone is insufficient to enter ihram. Once he connects with the animal, his intention is coupled with this characteristic act, and he becomes muhrim equivalently to having led it from the start.

Key Terms
تقلید (taqlid): Placing a necklace (qiladah) on the sacrificial animal as a mark that it is a hady.
هدی (hady): The sacrificial animal sent to the Haram for the rites of Hajj.
احرام (ihram): The sacred state into which a Muslim enters for the performance of Hajj or Umrah, with specific prohibitions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Immediately upon setting out
B) When he catches up with the hady
C) When he reaches Mecca
D) When he performs tawaf

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires an action specific to ihram—driving the hady—alongside intention; mere sending does not induce the sacred state.

The Exception for Hady al-Tamattu': Ihram upon Setting Out
Exception for tamattu' hady: ihram upon setting out

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the exception for hady al-tamattu' and explain the istihsan reasoning that overrides qiyas.

Core Idea
For hady al-tamattu', setting out with intention suffices for ihram—istihsan overrides qiyas because it is a Hajj ritual from the start.

In Hajj, when one sends a sacrificial animal ahead, the general rule is that one does not become a muhrim until actually leading the animal. However, Imam Muhammad (RA) in Al-Hidayah states an exception for the hady of tamattu': the person becomes muhrim upon setting out with intention. This ruling is based on istihsan (juristic preference), which overrides the analogical reasoning (qiyas) that would treat it like other hady. Let us examine the legal reasoning behind this exception.

Guided Path
1
State the General Rule
Identify the default rule: for most sacrificial animals sent ahead, one does not enter ihram until actually leading or driving the animal. This is based on qiyas with other hady.
The general rule applies to hady for violations (jinaayah) or other voluntary offerings.
2
Identify the Exception
Note that Imam Muhammad states 'except for the badanah of tamattu''. For this specific hady, setting out (tawajjuh) with the intention of ihram makes the person a muhrim.
The key Arabic terms: 'إِلَّا فِي بُدُنَةِ الْمُتْعَةِ' and 'مُحْرِمٌ حِينَ تَوَجَّهَ'.
3
Understand the Qiyas Objection
Recognize that qiyas would treat tamattu' hady like all others, requiring actual leading. The text acknowledges this as 'wajh al-qiyas'.
Qiyas uses the original case (asl) of other hady and the common illa of sending an animal ahead.
4
Analyze the Istihsan Reasoning
Examine the special nature of tamattu' hady: it is legislated from the beginning as a Hajj ritual, specific to Mecca, and obligatory as gratitude for combining Umrah and Hajj. Therefore, setting out is sufficient.
The illa here is not the act of leading but the ritual nature from inception. Istihsan relies on this stronger reason.
5
Apply the Ruling
In practice: if a person intends Hajj al-Tamattu', sends the hady animal ahead, and sets out with the intention of ihram, he becomes muhrim immediately. No need to wait until actually leading the animal.
This applies only to tamattu' hady, not to violation hady or nafl hady.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ إِلَّا فِي بُدُنَةِ الْمُتْعَةِ فَإِنَّهُ مُحْرِمٌ حِينَ تَوَجَّهَ مَعْنَاهُ إِذَا نَوَى الْإِحْرَامَ وَهَذَا اسْتِحْسَانٌ وَجْهُ الْقِيَاسِ فِيهِ مَا ذَكَرْنَا وَوَجْهُ الِاسْتِحْسَانِ أَنَّ هَذَا الْهَدْيَ مَشْرُوعٌ عَلَى الِابْتِدَاءِ نُسُكًا مِنْ مَنَاسِكِ الْحَجِّ وَضْعًا لِأَنَّهُ يَخْتَصُّ بِمَكَّةَ وَيَجِبُ شُكْرَ الْجَمْعِ بَيْنَ أَدَاءِ النُّسُكَيْنِ وَغَيْرُهُ قَدْ يَجِبُ بِالْجِنَايَةِ وَإِنْ لَمْ يَصِلْ إِلَى مَكَّةَ فَلِهَذَا اكْتُفِيَ فِيهِ بِالتَّوَجُّهِ وَفِي غَيْرِهِ تُوُقِّفَ عَلَى حَقِيقَةِ الْفِعْلِ
He said: Except for the badanah (camel/cow) of tamattu', for indeed he is a muhrim when he sets out, meaning when he intends ihram. And this is istihsan. The aspect of qiyas in it is what we mentioned, and the aspect of istihsan is that this hady is legislated from the beginning as a ritual from the rituals of Hajj by prescription, because it is specific to Mecca and is obligatory as thanksgiving for combining the performance of the two rituals. Other (hady) may become obligatory due to a violation even if one does not reach Mecca. Therefore, setting out was deemed sufficient in this case, while in other cases it is conditioned upon the actual act (of driving).
Source pages p. 376

Commentary
Imam Muhammad (RA) states an exception to the general rule: for the hady of tamattu' (the sacrificial animal offered by one performing Hajj al-Tamattu'), the person becomes a muhrim upon setting out, provided he intends ihram. This is by istihsan (juristic preference). Qiyas would treat it like other hady where actual driving is required, but istihsan considers the special nature of tamattu' hady: it is legislated as a ritual act of Hajj from the start, specific to Mecca, and obligatory as gratitude for combining Umrah and Hajj. Other hady (e.g., for violations) may be due to non-Hajj causes even if one never reaches Mecca. Hence, with tamattu' hady, the mere intention and setting out suffice; with other hady, the actual driving is required.

Key Terms
بدنة المتعة (badanat al-mut'ah): The sacrificial animal obligatory upon one performing Hajj al-Tamattu' as a thank-offering for combining Umrah and Hajj.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas for a stronger reason based on specific evidence or special circumstances.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning from an original case (asl) to a new case (far') based on a common effective cause (illa).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Because it is a violation hady
C) Because it is legislated as a Hajj ritual from the beginning
D) Because the Prophet always did so

Key Takeaway
For hady al-tamattu', setting out with intention suffices for ihram due to istihsan, because it is a Hajj ritual from its inception.

Actions That Do Not Make One Muhrim: Jull, Ish'ar, Taqlid of Sheep
Ruling on acts that are not specific to Hajj and thus do not effect ihram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between acts that effect ihram and those that do not, specifically explaining why jull, ish'ar, and taqlid of sheep do not make one a muhrim, and state the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar.

Core Idea
Only acts exclusive to Hajj rituals effect ihram; covering, marking, and placing a qilada on a sheep do not qualify.

A pilgrim may perform various actions with his sacrificial animal, but not all of them constitute entering the state of ihram. This passage clarifies that covering the animal (tajliyah), slitting its hump (ish'ar), and putting a qilada on a sheep are not considered ihram-inducing acts because they lack exclusivity to Hajj. It also highlights a subtle intra-Hanafi difference regarding the ruling on ish'ar itself.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions
List the actions mentioned: jull (covering), ish'ar (marking), and taqlid of a sheep (placing a qilada). Note that all are done to/for the sacrificial animal.
These actions are performed by someone who intends to offer a hady, not necessarily a pilgrim in ihram.
2
Analyze why each does not effect ihram
For jull: it is for repelling heat, cold, or flies – a practical need, not a Hajj-specific ritual. For ish'ar: disputed but either disliked (Abu Hanifa) or good (Sahibayn) but also done for treatment, so not exclusive. For taqlid of a sheep: not customary, and the sheep is not a tamattu' hady.
The key principle is that only actions particular to Hajj (like talbiyah, wearing ihram garments) effect ihram.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on ish'ar
Abu Hanifa holds ish'ar is makruh and not part of the ritual at all. The Sahibayn consider it hasan but note it may be done for veterinary reasons. Both agree it does not make one muhrim.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) is only in the ruling on ish'ar itself, not on ihram.
4
Confirm the overall ruling
Regardless of the ikhtilaf, none of these three actions make one a muhrim. The mufta bihi is that they do not effect ihram.
This ruling is from zahir al-riwayah and is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ جَلَّلَ بُدْنَةً أَوْ أَشْعَرَهَا أَوْ قَلَّدَ شَاةً لَمْ يَكُنْ مُحْرِمًا لِأَنَّ التَّجْلِيلَ لِدَفْعِ الْحَرِّ وَالْبَرْدِ وَالذُّبَانِ فَلَمْ يَكُنْ مِنْ خَصَائِصِ الْحَجِّ وَالْإِشْعَارُ مَكْرُوهٌ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ فَلَا يَكُونُ مِنَ النُّسُكِ فِي شَيْءٍ وَعِنْدَهُمَا إِنْ كَانَ حَسَنًا فَقَدْ يُفْعَلُ لِلْمُعَالَجَةِ بِخِلَافِ التَّقْلِيدِ لِأَنَّهُ يَخْتَصُّ بِالْهَدْيِ وَتَقْلِيدُ الشَّاةِ غَيْرُ مُعْتَادٍ وَلَيْسَ بِمُتَّعٍ أَيْضًا
If he covers a badanah with a jull, or performs ish'ar on it, or puts a qiladah on a sheep, he is not a muhrim, because covering is for repelling heat, cold, and flies, so it is not from the specific characteristics of Hajj. Ish'ar is disliked (makruh) according to Abu Hanifa, so it is not part of the ritual at all. According to the two (Sahibayn), even if it is good (hasan), it may be done for treatment, unlike taqlid because it is specific to hady, and taqlid of a sheep is not customary and is not a tamattu' either.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage lists three actions that do not render a person a muhrim: covering the animal (tajliyah), making a cut on its hump (ish'ar), and placing a qiladah on a sheep. The reason is that these actions are not exclusive to Hajj rituals; covering is for practical purposes, and ish'ar is also done for veterinary reasons. Then the text highlights an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding ish'ar: Imam Abu Hanifa considers it makruh and thus not part of the Hajj ritual at all. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it hasan (good) but note that it may be done for treatment, so it does not have the specificity of taqlid. Taqlid is specific to hady, but taqlid of a sheep is not customary and is not considered a tamattu' hady. Hence, none of these actions make one a muhrim.

Key Terms
تجلية (tajliyah): Covering the sacrificial animal with a cloth (jull) for protection.
إشعار (ish'ar): Making a cut or slit on the hump of the animal to mark it as a hady.
تقلید الشاة (taqlid al-sha'): Placing a qiladah on a sheep (as opposed to a camel or cow).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) It is disliked (makruh)
C) It is obligatory (wajib)
D) It is forbidden (haram)

Key Takeaway
Covering, marking, and putting a qilada on a sheep do not make one a muhrim because they are not exclusive to Hajj; the intra-Hanafi dispute on ish'ar does not change this outcome.

When Does Sending Hady Make One Muhrim? The Tamattu' Exception
Imam Muhammad's istihsan for tamattu' hady vs. general qiyas

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi general rule and the exception for tamattu' hady, and identify the basis of Imam Muhammad's istihsan.

Core Idea
Sending hady before oneself does not make one muhrim—except for tamattu' hady, where departure with intention suffices by istihsan.

This lesson examines an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the moment a pilgrim enters ihram after sending a sacrificial animal (hady) ahead. While the school's general rule (qiyas) requires physical joining with the animal, Imam Muhammad makes an exception for the tamattu' hady, allowing ihram to take effect upon departure with intention. We will unpack the reasoning behind this exception and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi rule
Identify the standard ruling: sending hady alone does not make one muhrim; one becomes muhrim only when he joins the hady. This is the qiyas.
This is the zahir al-riwayah position.
2
Identify the exceptional case
Note that Imam Muhammad holds a different view for tamattu' hady: the pilgrim becomes muhrim immediately upon departure, provided he intends ihram.
The exception is specific to mut'ah's hady.
3
Recognize the basis of the exception
Imam Muhammad justifies this by istihsan (juristic preference). The illah is that tamattu' hady is an initial act of Hajj, specific to Makkah and obligatory as thanksgiving for combining Hajj and Umrah. Other hady (e.g., for jinayah) are not tied to Makkah.
The distinction lies in the nature of the obligation.
4
Understand the practical consequence
For a mutamatti' pilgrim, departure with intention triggers ihram if hady was sent ahead. For others, they must wait to join the hady.
This affects the validity and timing of ihram.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
امام محمد نے ایک استثنائی صورت بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ تمتع کے بدنہ کے علاوہ کا حکم تو یہ ہے کہ اگر ہدی کو بھیج دیا اور بعد میں خود روانہ ہوا تو روانہ ہونے سے محرم نہ ہوگا یہاں تک کہ بدی کے ساتھ جا کر مل جائے لیکن تمتع کے بدی کا حکم یہ ہے کہ اگر ہدی کو پہلے بھیج دیا اور پھر خود روانہ ہوا تو روانہ ہوتے ہی اس وقت محرم ہو گا جبکہ اس نے احترام کی نیت بھی کی ہو۔ یہ حکم استحسانی ہے ورنہ قیاس وہی ہے جو ہم دوسرے ہدی کے جانوروں میں بیان کر چکے ہیں اور اس کی وجہ بھی بیان کر چکے۔ استحسان کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ تمتع کا بدی از جانب شرع ابتداء افعال حج میں سے ایک فعل ہے۔ فعل حج اس لئے ہے کہ یہ ہلدی مکہ کے ساتھ خاص ہے اور حج اور عمرہ کی دو نعمتوں کو جمع کرنے پر بطور شکرانہ واجب ہے۔ اور ہدی تجمیع کے علاوہ بھی جنایت کی وجہ سے واجب ہوتا ہے اگر چہ وہ مکہ کو نہ پہنچے یعنی جنایت وغیرہ کی وجہ سے جو ہدی واجب ہے وہ مکہ کی خصوصیات میں سے نہیں ہے پس اس فرق کی وجہ سے تمتع کے بدی میں محض روانہ ہونے پر اکتفاء کیا اور اس کے علاوہ کو حقیقت فعل یعنی سوق بدی پر موقوف رکھا۔
Imam Muhammad stated an exceptional case: The ruling for other than mut'ah's badanah is that if one sends the hady and later proceeds himself, he does not become muhrim upon proceeding until he joins the hady. But the ruling for mut'ah's hady is that if he sends the hady first and then proceeds himself, he becomes muhrim at the moment of proceeding provided he also intends ihram. This ruling is istihsan; otherwise the qiyas is the same as we have stated for other sacrificial animals, and we have already given its reason. The reason for istihsan is that mut'ah's hady is, by divine law, one of the initial acts of Hajj. It is an act of Hajj because it is specific to Makkah and is obligatory as a thanksgiving for combining the two blessings of Hajj and 'Umrah. Whereas hady other than that of tamattu' becomes obligatory due to a transgression (jinayah) even if it does not reach Makkah—i.e., the hady that is obligatory due to jinayah and the like is not among the specificities of Makkah. So due to this difference, for mut'ah's hady, mere departure was deemed sufficient, while for other than it, it was made dependent on the actual act, i.e., driving the hady.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding when a person becomes muhrim (enters the state of ihram) after sending a sacrificial animal (hady) ahead. The general ruling (qiyas) is that sending a hady before oneself does not make one muhrim; one only becomes muhrim when he joins the animal at its location. Imam Muhammad, however, makes an exception for the hady of tamattu' (the sacrificial animal offered by a mutamatti' pilgrim). For this specific hady, if the pilgrim sends it first and then departs with the intention of ihram, he becomes muhrim immediately upon departure. The basis is istihsan (juristic preference): the tamattu' hady is itself a ritual act specific to Makkah and is tied to the combined performance of Hajj and 'Umrah. In contrast, other hady are not specific to Makkah (e.g., those due to violations). Hence, the exception. The text does not mention the views of Abu Hanifa or Abu Yusuf explicitly, but Imam Muhammad's position is presented as a distinct ikhtilaf within the school.

Key Terms
بدی (badanah / hady): Sacrificial animal sent ahead to the Haram, especially for tamattu' or as a penalty.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing 'Umrah and then Hajj in the same journey with a break, requiring a hady.
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference; departing from qiyas to a more suitable ruling due to a stronger reason.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical deduction; the general rule based on an effective cause (illah).
جنایت (jinayah): Transgression during ihram that necessitates a penalty sacrifice.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Muhammad, when does a mutamatti' pilgrim become muhrim if he sends his hady ahead?
A) When he joins the hady
B) Upon departure with intention
C) Only when he reaches Makkah
D) He never becomes muhrim by sending the hady

Key Takeaway
For tamattu' hady alone, departure with intention suffices to enter ihram, by istihsan; all other hady require physical joining with the animal.

Actions on Hady That Do Not Induce Ihram
Ruling on three actions on hady that do not induce ihram, with proof and intra-Hanafi detail.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that covering, ish'ar, and taqlid on a goat do not induce ihram, and explain why based on the specificity of Hajj rituals.

Core Idea
Actions on hady not exclusive to Hajj do not make you muhrim, even with intention.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies a common confusion: performing certain actions on a sacrificial animal does not automatically bring one into the state of ihram. We will explore the ruling for covering a camel, ish'ar, and placing a necklace on a goat, and understand the underlying principle that only acts specific to Hajj can validate the intention of ihram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actions
List the three actions mentioned: jull (covering), ish'ar (cutting hump), taqlid on a goat.
2
Understand the ruling
The ruling is that none of these make one muhrim, even with niyyah.
3
Analyze the reason (talil)
The reason is that these actions are not specific to Hajj; they can be done for other purposes (repelling heat/cold, treatment). Only actions that are khasa'is al-Hajj can carry the intention of ihram.
Note the distinction: ish'ar has intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf but both sides agree it's not specific to Hajj.
4
Examine taqlid limitation
Taqlid is specific to hady, but only for camels/cows, not goats. Hence placing a qiladah on a goat is neither customary nor sunnah and thus does not induce ihram.

کہاں سے متصل ہوئی اور جب نسک حج کے ساتھ نیت متصل نہ ہوئی تو محرم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر چہ اشعار اچھا ہے غیر مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن وہ حج کی خصوصیات میں سے نہیں ہے کیونکہ اشعار کبھی علاج کے واسطے تقلید فعل مختص ہے تو بکری کی گردن میں بھی قلادہ ڈالنے سے محرم ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ اس سے محرم نہیں ہوتا۔ جواب، بکری کا تقلید کرنا یعنی اس کو قلادہ پہنانا نہ معتاد ہے اور نہ سنت سے ثابت ہے بلکہ تقلید فقط بد نہ یعنی اونٹ گائے کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ اس لئے بکری کو قلادہ پہنانے سے محرم نہ ہوگا۔
If one covers a badanah with a jull, or makes ish'ar on it, or places a qiladah on a goat, he is not muhrim, because the jull is for repelling heat, cold, and flies, so it is not among the specificities of Hajj. Translation: And if someone covered a badanah with a jull, or made ish'ar on it (cutting its hump and drawing blood), or placed a qiladah on a goat, he will not be muhrim. Because covering with a jull is sometimes done to ward off heat, cold, and flies, so this action is not among the specificities of Hajj. Explanation: Ish'ar means cutting the hump and drawing blood. The issue: If someone placed a jull on a badanah, or made ish'ar on it (cutting its hump and drawing blood), or placed a qiladah on a goat's neck, in these cases he will not be muhrim, even if he intended ihram. Because covering with a jull is also for warding off heat, cold, and flies, so this action is not among the specificities of Hajj, whereas the intention of ihram is only valid when it is connected to a specific action. The view of Abu Hanifah regarding ish'ar: Ish'ar is makruh according to Abu Hanifah, so it is not part of the ritual at all. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), if ish'ar is good (hasan), it may be done for treatment—unlike taqlid, because it is specific to hady, and taqlid of a goat is not customary nor is it a sunnah. Explanation: The author of Hidayah says: One does not become muhrim by making ish'ar, because ish'ar is makruh according to Imam Abu Hanifah, and something makruh cannot be a ritual act of Hajj. And when ish'ar is not a Hajj ritual, how can the intention of ihram connect with it? And when the intention does not connect with a Hajj ritual, one is not muhrim. According to the two (Sahibayn), although ish'ar is good (non-makruh), it is still not among the specificities of Hajj, because ish'ar is sometimes done for treatment. Thus, according to them too, ish'ar is not a specific act of Hajj, so they also hold that one does not become muhrim. Unlike taqlid, which is specific to hady and is not done for any other purpose. Question: Now the question remains: since taqlid is a specific act, then placing a qiladah on a goat's neck should make one muhrim, but it does not. Answer: Taqlid of a goat (placing a qiladah on it) is neither customary nor established by the Sunnah; rather, taqlid is specific only to badanah – i.e., camels and cows. Therefore, placing a qiladah on a goat does not make one muhrim.
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling about actions performed on a sacrificial animal that do not bring about the state of ihram. The author clarifies that covering a badanah (a camel or cow) with a jull (a cloth), making ish'ar (slitting the hump to draw blood), or placing a qiladah (a necklace) on a goat, does not make one muhrim even if one intends ihram. The reason is that these actions are not exclusive to the Hajj rituals; they can be done for ordinary purposes such as protection from heat, cold, or insects. The intention (niyyah) of ihram is only effective if it is attached to an act that is specific to the Hajj (khasa'is al-Hajj). The passage then delves into an intra-Hanafi difference regarding ish'ar: Imam Abu Hanifah considers ish'ar makruh (disliked), so it cannot be a ritual act. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider ish'ar permissible (hasan) but still not a specific Hajj act because it can be done for medical reasons. In contrast, taqlid (placing a qiladah) is a specific act for hady animals, but only for camels and cows, not for goats. Hence, taqlid on a goat does not make one muhrim because it is neither customary nor sunnah. This distinction ensures that only actions unequivocally tied to the Hajj ritual (like driving the hady with the intention of ihram) induce the state of ihram.

Key Terms
اشعار (ish'ar): Cutting the hump of a camel or cow to draw blood, as a mark for the sacrificial animal.
تقلید (taqlid): Placing a qiladah (necklace) around the neck of a sacrificial animal to mark it as hady.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the goat is not a valid hady animal
B) Because taqlid is only specific to camels and cows, and is not customary for goats
C) Because the intention was not present
D) Because the goat was not driven

Key Takeaway
Only acts that are specific to Hajj (khasa'is al-Hajj) can carry the intention of ihram; covering, ish'ar, and taqlid on a goat are not such acts.

The Hanafi Definition of Badanah: Camels and Cows
Resolving the definition of badanah between Hanafi and Shafi'i schools

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the scope of 'badanah' and explain the linguistic and hadith-based proofs against the Shafi'i view.

Core Idea
Bad anah includes both camels and cows because the root meaning (thickness) applies to both, and both share the legal rule of being shareable by seven.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a key lexical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: does the term 'badanah' in the context of hady refer only to camels, or does it include cows? Imam Muhammad presents the Hanafi view that badanah covers both, and then refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's objection. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to evaluate linguistic arguments in fiqh and appreciate how Hanafi usul handles conflicting hadith narrations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
Recognize that the dispute is over the definition of 'badanah' in Islamic law, which impacts which animals are valid for hady (sacrificial offering during Hajj).
Also examine why this definition matters for practical fiqh rulings.
2
State the Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that badanah is specific to camels, citing the hadith of Jumu'ah where the Prophet distinguished between 'badanah' and 'cow'.
Look at the exact wording quoted in the passage.
3
Analyse the Hanafi linguistic proof
The word 'badanah' derives from 'badanah' meaning thickness/plumpness, a quality found in both camels and cows. Therefore, the term linguistically covers both.
This is a Qiyas on the basis of shared meaning.
4
Analyse the Hanafi hadith critique
The Hanafis note that the correct narration of the Jumu'ah hadith uses 'jazur' (camel) instead of 'badanah', weakening the Shafi'i distinction.
This shows how variant readings impact proof strength.
5
Apply the practical consequence
Both camels and cows can be shared by up to seven persons in sacrifice, indicating they are treated similarly in law. This practical evidence supports inclusion.
This is a secondary Hanafi proof based on legal practice (urf shari'i).

Source Text

قَالَ وَالْبُدْنُ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ وَ الْبَقَرِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ مِنَ الْإِبِلِ خَاصَّةً لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ فِي حَدِيثِ الْجُمُعَةِ فَالْمُسْتَعْجِلُ مِنْهُمْ كَالْمُهْدِى بَدَنَهُ وَالَّذِى يَلِيْهِ كَالْمُهْدِى بَقَرَةً فَصَلَ بَيْنَهُما وَلَنَا الْبَدَنَهُ تُنْبِئُى عَنِ الْبَدَانَةِ وَهِيَ الصَّحَامَةُ وَقَدْ اِشْتَرَكَا فِي هَذَا الْمَعْنَى وَلِهَذَا يُجْزِى كُلَّ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهَا عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ وَالصَّحِيحُ مِنَ الرَّوَايَةِ فِي الْحَدِيثِ كَالْمُهْدِى جُزُورًا وَاللهُ تَعَالَى أَعْلَمُ بِالصَّوَاب ترجمہ امام محمد نے کہا اور بد نہ اونٹ و گائے سے ہیں اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ فقط اونٹ کے ساتھ مخصوص ہیں۔ کیونکہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے حدیث جمعہ میں فرمایا کہ لوگوں میں سے جلدی کر کے آنے والا اس کے مانند ہے جس نے بدنہ کو ہدی بھیجا اور جو اس سے متصل آنے والا ہے اس کے مانند ہے جس نے گائے ہدی بھیجی ۔ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے بدنہ اور گائے میں فصل کیا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بد نہ خبر دیتا ہے بدانت یعنی ضخامت کی اور اونٹ اور گائے اس معنی میں دونوں مشترک ہیں۔ اسی وجہ سے ان دونوں میں سے ہر ایک سات آدمیوں کی طرف سے جائز ہے۔ اور حدیث میں صحیح روایت كَالْمُهْدِی جُزُورا (اس کے مانند جس نے اونٹ ہدی بھیجا ) اور درست بات کو اللہ ہی زیادہ جانتا ہے۔ تشریح ماتن یعنی امام محمد نے فرمایا ہے کہ بدنہ کا اطلاق اونٹ اور گائے پر ہوتا ہے۔ امام شافعی نے فرمایا ہے ک فقط اونٹ پر ہوتا ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل حدیث جمعہ ہے جس میں فرمایا گیا جمعہ کے لئے جلدی جانے والا اجر و ثواب میں اس آدمی کی مانند ہے جس نے ہدی بنا کر مکہ کی طرف روانہ کیا ہو اور جو متصلاً اس کے بعد جانے والا ہے وہ اس کے مانند ہے جس نے گائے کو ہدی بنا کر بھیجا۔ اس حدیث میں جو بدنہ اور گائے کے درمیان فرق کیا گیا ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ گائے بد نہ کے علاوہ اور کوئی چیز ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ بد نہ کے لغوی معنی بدانت یعنی ضخامت کے ہیں۔ مطلب یہ ہے کہ جسم و جسامت والے جانور کو بد نہ کہتے ہیں۔ اور یہ معنی اونٹ اور گائے دونوں میں پائے جاتے ہیں۔ لہذا بد نہ کا اطلاق دونوں پر ہوگا۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ قربانی میں اونٹ اور گائے دونوں میں سے ہر ایک سات سات آدمیوں کی طرف سے کافی ہو جاتا ہے۔
He (Imam Muhammad) said: Al-budn includes camels and cows. Al-Shafi'i said: it is specific to camels only, because of the saying of the Prophet (peace be upon him) in the hadith of Jumu'ah: 'The one who hastens among them is like the one who offers a badanah, and the one who follows him is like the one who offers a cow.' He differentiated between them. Our proof: The word badanah indicates badanah (plumpness/thickness), and both (camels and cows) share this meaning, and for this reason each one of them suffices for seven persons. The correct narration in the hadith is 'like the one who offers a jazur (camel)'. And Allah knows best what is correct. Translation: Imam Muhammad said: Badanah applies to camels and cows. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is specific only to camels, because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said in the hadith of Jumu'ah: 'The one who hastens among them is like the one who offers a badanah, and the one who follows him is like the one who offers a cow.' He differentiated between them. Our proof: The word badanah indicates badanah (plumpness/thickness), and both (camels and cows) share this meaning. For this reason, each one of them suffices for seven persons. And the correct narration in the hadith is 'like the one who offers a camel (jazur)'. And Allah knows best what is correct. Explanation: The matn, i.e., Imam Muhammad, stated that the term badanah applies to camels and cows. Imam al-Shafi'i stated that it applies only to camels. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Jumu'ah in which it is said: 'The one who goes early to Jumu'ah is like one who has sent a badanah as hady to Makkah, and the one who goes after him is like one who has sent a cow as hady.' In this hadith, a distinction was made between badanah and cow, indicating that a cow is something other than badanah. Our proof is that the word badanah is derived from badanah which means thickness/plumpness, meaning a large-bodied animal, and this meaning is found in both camels and cows. Therefore, the term badanah applies to both. This is the reason why in sacrifice, each of them (camel and cow) suffices for seven persons.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school (represented by Imam Muhammad) and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the scope of the term 'badanah' in Islamic law. The term appears in texts about hady (sacrificial animals) and determines which animals are covered. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that badanah refers only to camels, citing a hadith about Jumu'ah where the Prophet distinguished between badanah and cows, implying cows are separate. The Hanafi school counters with two arguments: linguistic and practical. Linguistically, 'badanah' derives from 'badanah' meaning plumpness or thickness, a quality shared by both camels and cows. Practically, both camels and cows can be shared by up to seven persons in sacrifice (udhiyah/qurbani), indicating they are treated similarly. The Hanafis also note a variant reading of the hadith that uses 'jazur' (camel) instead of 'badanah', weakening the Shafi'i proof. The passage underscores how lexical analysis and legal practice ('urf shari'i) inform Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
بدنة (badanah): A sacrificial animal, specifically a camel or cow according to Hanafis; only a camel according to Shafi'is.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which animals are included in the term 'badanah'?
A) Only camels
B) Camels and cows
C) Camels, cows, and goats
D) Only cows

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school defines 'badanah' to include both camels and cows, based on linguistic derivation and legal practice, in contrast to the Shafi'i view that limits it to camels.

The Effect of Ish'ar and Taqlid on Entering Ihram: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Explains that ish'ar and taqlid do not constitute ihram, with intra-Hanafi reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the acts of ish'ar and taqlid do not make one a muhrim according to the Hanafi school and distinguish the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the matter.

Core Idea
Neither ish'ar nor taqlid automatically enters one into ihram; only acts exclusive to Hajj rites can.

This passage addresses a common point of confusion: if one marks or collars an animal for sacrifice, does one automatically become a muhrim? The Hanafi school clarifies that these acts, while associated with Hajj, do not constitute entering the state of ihram. The ruling hinges on whether the act is a specific rite (nusk) of Hajj and whether the intention is attached to that rite.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What exactly is disputed? The effect of ish'ar and taqlid on entering ihram.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position and dalil
Ish'ar is makruh, so it cannot be a valid nusk. Thus intention cannot attach.
Abu Hanifa's premise: makruh acts are invalid as rites.
3
State the Sahibayn's position and dalil
Ish'ar is not makruh but is not exclusive to Hajj (can be done for medical reasons), so still not a nusk.
Sahibayn's premise: acts not exclusive to Hajj cannot be rites.
4
Analyze the exception of taqlid
Taqlid is exclusive to hady, but only for badanah (camel/cow), not goats. Thus taqlid on goats does not cause ihram.
Distinguishes taqlid from ish'ar.
5
Synthesize the thamarah al-khilaf
Both positions agree on the outcome: no ihram. The ikhtilaf is in the reasoning, not the practical result.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الحج تشریح صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ اشعار کرنے سے محرم نہیں ہو گا کہ اشعار حضرت امام ابو حنیفہ کے نزدیک مکروہ ہے اور جو چیز مکروہ ہو وہ نسک حج کس طرح وہ سکتی ہے اور جب اشعار نسک حج نہیں ہے تو نیت احرام نسک حج کے ساتھ کہاں سے متصل ہوئی اور جب نسک حج کے ساتھ نیت متصل نہ ہوئی تو محرم نہیں ہوگا۔ اور صاحبین کے نزدیک اگر چہ اشعار اچھا ہے غیر مکروہ ہے۔ لیکن وہ حج کی خصوصیات میں سے نہیں ہے کیونکہ اشعار کبھی علاج کے واسطے کر دیتے ہیں پس جب صاحبین کے نزدیک بھی اشعار حج کا فعل مختص نہ ہوا تو ان کے نزدیک بھی محرم نہ ہو گا۔ برخلاف تقلید کے کہ وہ ہدی کے ساتھ مختص ہے کسی اور غرض میں نہیں ہوتا۔ سوال : اب رہا یہ سوال کہ جب تقلید فعل مختص ہے تو بکری کی گردن میں بھی قلادہ ڈالنے سے محرم ہونا چاہئے حالانکہ اس سے محرم نہیں ہوتا۔ جواب، بکری کا تقلید کرنا یعنی اس کو قلادہ پہنانا نہ معتاد ہے اور نہ سنت سے ثابت ہے بلکہ تقلید فقط بد نہ یعنی اونٹ گائے کے ساتھ خاص ہے۔ اس لئے بکری کو قلادہ پہنانے سے محرم نہ ہوگا۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya: Urdu commentary of Hidayah, vol. 3, book of Hajj. The commentator (Sahib al-Hidayah) says: One will not become a muhrim by performing ish'ar because ish'ar is makruh according to Imam Abu Hanifa. And a thing that is makruh cannot be a rite (nusk) of Hajj. When ish'ar is not a rite of Hajj, how can the intention of ihram be connected with the rite? And when the intention is not connected with the rite, one will not become a muhrim. According to the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), although ish'ar is good (not makruh), it is not specific to the rites of Hajj because ish'ar is sometimes done for medical treatment. So according to them too, ish'ar is not specific to the act of Hajj, so one will not become a muhrim. Contrary to taqlid, which is specific to the hady (sacrificial animal) and is not done for any other purpose. Question: If taqlid is a specific act, then placing a necklace around a goat's neck should also make one a muhrim, but it does not. Answer: Performing taqlid on a goat, i.e., putting a necklace on it, is not customary nor proven from the Sunnah. Rather, taqlid is specific only to badanah (camel or cow). Therefore, putting a necklace on a goat does not make one a muhrim.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author, commenting on the Hidayah, explains that neither ish'ar (marking the sacrificial animal) nor taqlid (putting a necklace on it) cause one to enter the state of ihram unless they are specific to the Hajj rites. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, ish'ar is makruh, so it cannot be a valid rite. According to the Sahibayn, ish'ar is not makruh but it is not exclusive to Hajj (it can be done for medical reasons). Therefore, in both views, ish'ar does not establish ihram. Taqlid, on the other hand, is exclusive to the hady, but only for camels and cows, not goats. Hence, taqlid on a goat does not make one a muhrim. The passage uses rational argument: if an act is not a specific rite (nusk) of Hajj, the intention of ihram cannot be attached to it.

Key Terms
اشعار (ish'ar): Marking a sacrificial animal (camel or cow) by cutting a hump or similar to indicate it is for sacrifice.
تقلید (taqlid): Putting a necklace or identifying mark on a sacrificial animal to indicate it is for Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, does putting a necklace on a goat make one a muhrim?
A) Yes, because taqlid is specific to the hady.
B) No, because taqlid for goats is not proven by Sunnah.
C) Yes, if the intention is for Hajj.
D) No, because goats are not used for sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, neither marking (ish'ar) nor collaring (taqlid) a sacrificial animal constitutes entering ihram unless the act is exclusive to Hajj rites and the intention is attached.

The Virtue of Qiran over Ifrad and Tamattu'
Establishes the Hanafi view that Qiran is the most virtuous form of Hajj

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the most virtuous form of Hajj and evaluate the proofs of the opposing schools.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school holds Qiran superior because combining two acts of worship is better, and the 'rukhsa' hadith does not diminish its virtue.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a classical inter-madhhab dispute: which form of Hajj is most virtuous? The Hanafi position is clear - Qiran is superior to both Ifrad and Tamattu'. The author presents the proofs of Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik, then systematically rebuts them. By the end of this lesson, you will not only know which form is preferred but understand the reasoning behind the Hanafi tarjih.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Position
Identify the core claim: Qiran is afdal (superior) to Tamattu' and Ifrad. This is the foundational point of the lesson.
2
Identify the Opposing Views
Note that Imam al-Shafi'i holds Ifrad as superior, and Imam Malik holds Tamattu' as superior. Understand their primary proofs.
3
Follow the Opponents' Proofs
For Shafi'i: the hadith that Qiran is a rukhsa (concession) and that Ifrad involves more talbiyah, travel, and shaving. For Maliki: that Tamattu' is mentioned in the Quran (2:196) while Qiran is not explicitly mentioned.
4
Analyse the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi rebuttal: the rukhsa hadith was to correct the Jahili belief that Umrah in Hajj months was evil, not to indicate inferiority. Talbiyah, travel, and shaving are not inherently meritorious. Tamattu' being mentioned in Quran does not imply superiority; Qiran is also implicitly mentioned in the verse 'Complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' interpreted as doing both together. Moreover, Qiran involves hastening and continuous ihram from miqat, which is more virtuous.
5
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafi recommend Qiran, Shafi'i recommend Ifrad, Maliki recommend Tamattu'. Additionally, according to Hanafi, the Qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'ys, while Shafi'i requires only one each. This affects the actual rites performed.

بَابُ الْقِرَان
تَرْجَمَۃ: یہ باب قرآن کے بیان میں ہے
تشریح: مصنف علیہ الرحمہ مفرد کے احکام سے فراغت پا کر اب مرکب یعنی قرآن اور تمتع کے احکام ذکر فرمائیں گے لیکن ہمارے نزدیک چونکہ قرآن افضل ہے اس لئے پہلے قران کے احکام ذکر کئے گئے اور اس کے بعد تمتع کے احکام ذکر کئے جائیں گے۔ یہ یادرکھئے کہ محرم کی چار قسمیں ہیں ۔
(1) مفرد بالمج جس کا بیان پہلے باب میں گذر چکا۔
(۲) مفرد بالعمر ہ جو دل سے عمرہ کی نیت کرے اور لبیک عمر کہے اور پھر عمرہ کے افعال ادا کرے۔ قرآن، قارن وہ شخص ہے جو حج اور عمرہ دونوں کر کے پھر بغیر احرام کھولے افعال حج ادا کرے۔
(۴) تمتع مستمع و مشخص ہے جو پہلے افعال عمرہ ادا کرے پھر احرام کھول دے پھر اسی سال حج کے زمانہ میں حج کا احرام باندھ کر حج کے افعال ادا کرے۔
قرآن کا حکم ، کون سا حج افضل ہے، اقوال فقہاء
الْقِرَانُ أَفْضَلَّ مِنَ التَّمَتُّع والافرادِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ الإِفْرَادُ أفْضَلُ وَقَالَ مَالِك التمتع أفضل من القران لأنَّ لَهُ ذِكرًا فِي الْقُرْآن وَلَا ذِكرَ لِلْقُرآن فِيهِ وَلِلشَّافِعِى قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْقِرَانُ رُحْصَةٌ وَلَانَّ فِي الْإِفْرَادِ زِيَادَةُ التَّلْبيَةِ وَالسَّفَرِ وَالْحَلَقِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلامُ يَا الَ مُحَمَّدِ أهلُوا بِحَيَّةٍ وَعُمْرَةِ مَعَاوَلانَّ فِيْهِ جَمْعًا بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَ تَيْن فَأَشْبَهَ الصَّوْمَ مَعَ الْاِعْتِكَافِ وَالْحَرَاسَةِ فِي سَبِيلِ اللهِ مَعَ صَلوةِ اللَّيْلِ والتلبيَّةُ غَيْرُ مَحْصُورَةٍ وَالسَّفَرُ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ وَالْحَلْقَ خُرُوجٌ عَن الْعِبَادَةِ فَلَا يُتَرَبَّحُ بِمَا ذُكرَ وَالْمَقْصُودُ بِمَا رُوى نَفَى قَول أهل الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ أَنَّ الْعُمْرَةَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجَ مِنْ أَفْجَرِ الْفُجُوْرِ وَلِلْقِرَانِ ذِكْرٌ فِي الْقُرْآنِ لأنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَاتِمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ أَنْ يُحْرِم بِهِمَا مِنْ دَوَيْرَةِ أهْلِه عَلى مَا رَوَيْنَا مِنْ قَبْل ثُمَّ فِيهِ تَعْجِيلُ الْإِحْرَامِ وَاسْتِدَامَةِ إِحْرَامِهِمَا مِنَ الْمِيْقَاتِ إلى أن يَفْرَغَ مِنْهُمَا وَلَا كَذلِكَ التَّمَتَّعِ فَكَانَ الْقِرَانُ أولَى مِنْهُ وَقِيلَ الْاخْتِلَافُ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَ الشَّافِعِيِّ بِنَاءً عَلى أنَّ الْقَارِنَ عِندَنَا يَطوف طَوَافَيْنَ وَيَسْعَى سَعْيَيْن وَعِنْدَهُ طَوَافًا وَاحِدَ أَوْسَعْيًا وَاحِدًا
ترجمہ قران تجمیع اور افراد سے افضل ہے اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ افراد افضل ہے اور امام مالک نے کہا کہ تمتع قران سے افضل ہے کیونکہ تمتع کا کتاب اللہ میں ذکر ہے اور کتاب اللہ میں قرآن کا ذکر نہیں ہے اور امام شافعی کی دلیل حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا قول الْقِرَانُ رُخصة ہے
Chapter of Qiran
Translation: This chapter is on the explanation of Qiran.
Commentary: After completing the rulings of Ifrad, the author (may Allah have mercy on him) will now mention the rulings of the combined types, i.e., Qiran and Tamattu'. According to us, since Qiran is superior, the rulings of Qiran are mentioned first, and then those of Tamattu' will follow. Know that there are four types of muhrim:
1. Mufrid bil-Hajj: one who intends Hajj only, already discussed.
2. Mufrid bil-‘Umrah: one who intends ‘Umrah only.
3. Qarin: one who intends both Hajj and ‘Umrah together and performs Hajj actions without opening ihram.
4. Mutamatti‘: one who first performs ‘Umrah, then opens ihram, then in the same year, at the time of Hajj, enters ihram for Hajj and performs its actions.
Ruling of Qiran: Which Hajj is superior? Statements of jurists:
Qiran is superior to Tamattu‘ and Ifrad. Al-Shafi‘i said: Ifrad is superior. Malik said: Tamattu‘ is superior to Qiran, because Tamattu‘ is mentioned in the Qur’an, while Qiran is not mentioned in it. Al-Shafi‘i has the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Qiran is a concession.' Also, in Ifrad there is an increase of talbiyah, travel, and shaving (halq). Our proof is his (peace be upon him) statement: 'O family of Muhammad, pronounce talbiyah for Hajj and ‘Umrah together.' Also, in it (Qiran) there is a combination of two acts of worship, so it resembles fasting with i‘tikaf, and guarding in the path of Allah with night prayer. Talbiyah is not limited, travel is not intended in itself, and shaving is exiting from worship, so no benefit is derived from what was mentioned. What was reported is intended to negate the saying of the people of Jahiliyyah that performing ‘Umrah during the months of Hajj is the most wicked of wicked deeds. Qiran is mentioned in the Qur’an because the meaning of His statement (Exalted) 'And complete the Hajj and the ‘Umrah for Allah' is that one enters ihram for both from one's dwelling as we narrated earlier. Moreover, in it there is hastening of ihram and continuity of ihram for both from the miqat until one finishes from them, and this is not so in Tamattu‘. So Qiran is more deserving than it. And it is said: The difference between us and al-Shafi‘i is based on the fact that the Qarin according to us performs two tawafs and two sa‘ys, while according to him, one tawaf and one sa‘y.
Translation: Qiran is superior to Tamattu‘ and Ifrad. Al-Shafi‘i said Ifrad is superior. Malik said Tamattu‘ is superior to Qiran because Tamattu‘ is mentioned in the Book of Allah, while Qiran is not mentioned in it. The proof of al-Shafi‘i is the statement of the Prophet (peace be upon him): 'Qiran is a concession.'
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage begins the chapter on Qiran (Hajj al-Qiran) from the Hidayah. The author first classifies the types of muhrim: Mufrid (Hajj only), Mufrid (Umrah only), Qarin (Hajj and Umrah combined in one ihram), and Mutamatti’ (Umrah first, then Hajj separately in the same year). Then the main ruling stated is that Qiran is superior to both Tamattu’ and Ifrad. This is the Hanafi position. The disputants are Al-Shafi’i (who favors Ifrad) and Malik (who favors Tamattu’). The text presents counter-reasons and rebuttals. For Shafi’i: the hadith that Qiran is a concession (rukhsa) implying it is less virtuous. Hanafi rebuttal: that hadith is to reject the Jahili belief that Umrah in Hajj months is evil, not to indicate inferiority. Hanafi proof: the Prophet commanded combining Hajj and Umrah; combining two worships is like combining fasting with i’tikaf or guarding in Allah’s path with night prayer. Also, Qiran is mentioned in the Qur’an (interpretation of 'complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' as doing both together from one’s home). Additionally, Qiran involves hastening ihram and maintaining ihram from miqat to completion, which is not in Tamattu’. The final point relates a difference with Shafi’i: according to Hanafi, a Qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa’ys, whereas Shafi’i requires only one each. The Urdu translation partially covers the beginning of the matn.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, performing both with a single set of actions (according to Hanafi, two tawafs and two sa'ys; according to Shafi'i, one each).
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first during Hajj months, opening ihram, then performing Hajj separately in the same year. Requires a sacrificial animal (dam).
افراد (ifrad): Performing only Hajj (or only Umrah) without combining. Mufrid bil-Hajj performs only Hajj rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which form of Hajj is considered the most virtuous?
A) Ifrad
B) Qiran
C) Tamattu'
D) All are equal

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the best form of Hajj, based on the Prophet's command to combine Hajj and Umrah and the principle that combining two acts of worship is superior.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
6 min
Which Hajj is Best: Qiran, Ifrad, or Tamattu'?
Dispute on virtue of Hajj types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the virtue of Qiran and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments.

Core Idea
Qiran is best because it combines two acts of worship and the Prophet commanded his family to do it.

When a person intends Hajj, they may choose among three forms: Qiran (Hajj and Umrah combined with one ihram), Ifrad (Hajj alone), and Tamattu' (Umrah then Hajj with separate ihrams). The Hanafi school holds that Qiran is the most excellent, but the Shafi'i and Maliki schools disagree. This lesson examines the proofs from each side and the Hanafi response, clarifying why the Prophet's directive for his family and the combination of worships make Qiran superior.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
State that the Hanafi school rules Qiran as the most excellent form of Hajj.
This is the mufta bihi in the Hanafi madhhab.
2
Examine the Hanafi dalil
Analyze the Prophet's command to his family to perform Hajj and Umrah together (Qiran), the analogy to combining fasting with i'tikaf, and the Quranic verse 'Complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' interpreted as performing both together.
The imperative form implies recommendation, not obligation.
3
State the opposing views
Present the Shafi'i position (Ifrad is best) and the Maliki position (Tamattu' is best), along with their proofs.
Shafi'i relies on the 'rukhsah' hadith; Maliki relies on explicit Quranic mention of Tamattu'.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafi school rebuts each opposing proof: the 'rukhsah' negates pre-Islamic custom, not superiority; extra talbiyah and travel are not inherently more virtuous; shaving is exiting worship; and Qiran also has Quranic basis.
The response shows a deeper understanding of the intention behind the proofs.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: Hanafis recommend Qiran, Shafi'is recommend Ifrad, Malikis recommend Tamattu'. A Muslim following a school should act accordingly.
The difference is in preference only; all forms are valid.

بَابُ الْقِرَانِ
الْقِرَانُ أَفْضَلَّ مِنَ التَّمَتُّعِ وَالْإِفْرَادِ وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ الْإِفْرَادُ أَفْضَلُ وَقَالَ مَالِكٌ التَّمَتُّعُ أَفْضَلُ مِنَ الْقِرَانِ لِأَنَّ لَهُ ذِكْرًا فِي الْقُرْآنِ وَلَا ذِكْرَ لِلْقُرْآنِ فِيهِ وَلِلشَّافِعِيِّ قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ الْقِرَانُ رُخْصَةٌ وَلِأَنَّ فِي الْإِفْرَادِ زِيَادَةَ التَّلْبِيَةِ وَالسَّفَرِ وَالْحَلَقِ وَلَنَا قَوْلُهُ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ يَا آلَ مُحَمَّدٍ أَهِلُّوا بِحَجَّةٍ وَعُمْرَةٍ مَعًا وَلِأَنَّ فِيهِ جَمْعًا بَيْنَ الْعِبَادَتَيْنِ فَأَشْبَهَ الصَّوْمَ مَعَ الِاعْتِكَافِ وَالْحِرَاسَةَ فِي سَبِيلِ اللَّهِ مَعَ صَلَاةِ اللَّيْلِ وَالتَّلْبِيَةُ غَيْرُ مَحْصُورَةٍ وَالسَّفَرُ غَيْرُ مَقْصُودٍ وَالْحَلْقُ خُرُوجٌ عَنِ الْعِبَادَةِ فَلَا يُتَرَجَّحُ بِمَا ذُكِرَ وَالْمَقْصُودُ بِمَا رُوِيَ نَفْيُ قَوْلِ أَهْلِ الْجَاهِلِيَّةِ أَنَّ الْعُمْرَةَ فِي أَشْهُرِ الْحَجِّ مِنْ أَفْجَرِ الْفُجُورِ وَلِلْقِرَانِ ذِكْرٌ فِي الْقُرْآنِ لِأَنَّ الْمُرَادَ مِنْ قَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى وَأَتِمُّوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلَّهِ أَنْ يُحْرِمَ بِهِمَا مِنْ دُوَيْرَةِ أَهْلِهِ عَلَى مَا رَوَيْنَا مِنْ قَبْلُ ثُمَّ فِيهِ تَعْجِيلُ الْإِحْرَامِ وَاسْتِدَامَةُ إِحْرَامِهِمَا مِنَ الْمِيقَاتِ إِلَى أَنْ يَفْرَغَ مِنْهُمَا وَلَا كَذَلِكَ التَّمَتُّعُ فَكَانَ الْقِرَانُ أَوْلَى مِنْهُ وَقِيلَ الِاخْتِلَافُ بَيْنَنَا وَبَيْنَ الشَّافِعِيِّ بِنَاءً عَلَى أَنَّ الْقَارِنَ عِنْدَنَا يَطُوفُ طَوَافَيْنِ وَيَسْعَى سَعْيَيْنِ وَعِنْدَهُ طَوَافًا وَاحِدًا وَسَعْيًا وَاحِدًا
Chapter of Qiran. Qiran is more excellent than Tamattu' and Ifrad. Al-Shafi'i said: Ifrad is more excellent. Malik said: Tamattu' is more excellent than Qiran, because it is mentioned in the Quran, while Qiran is not mentioned in it. Al-Shafi'i has the saying of him (peace be upon him): 'Qiran is a concession'; and because in Ifrad there is an increase of talbiyah, travel, and shaving (halq). Our proof is his saying (peace be upon him): 'O family of Muhammad, enter into ihram for Hajj and Umrah together'; and because in it there is a combination of two acts of worship, so it resembles combining fasting with i'tikaf, and guarding in the path of Allah with night prayer. Talbiyah is not limited, travel is not intended (as an aim), and shaving is exiting from worship, so preference is not established by what is mentioned. The purpose of what was narrated is to negate the saying of the people of ignorance that Umrah during the months of Hajj is the worst of sins. And Qiran has mention in the Quran, because the meaning of Allah's saying 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' is that one should enter ihram for both from his own dwelling, as we narrated before. Then in it there is early ihram and continuity of ihram of both from the miqat until he finishes them, and it is not so in Tamattu', so Qiran is more deserving than it. And it was said: The difference between us and al-Shafi'i is built on the fact that with us the qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'ys, while with him he performs one tawaf and one sa'y.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the virtue of the three types of Hajj: Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram), Ifrad (Hajj only), and Tamattu' (Umrah first, then Hajj with separate ihrams). The Hanafi position, as stated by the author, is that Qiran is the most excellent. Al-Shafi'i holds Ifrad to be best, while Malik holds Tamattu' to be best. The proof of al-Shafi'i is the hadith that Qiran is a concession (rukhsah), implying that Ifrad (the original requirement) is more virtuous. Additionally, in Ifrad there is more talbiyah, travel, and shaving (halq), each counted separately, so it involves more acts of worship. The Hanafi response is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) commanded his family to enter ihram for Hajj and Umrah together (Qiran), which indicates its superiority because the Prophet commands only the best for his family. Qiran combines two acts of worship, similar to combining fasting with i'tikaf or guarding the frontier with night prayer, which are deemed superior for combining. The additional elements in Ifrad are not inherently superior: talbiyah is not limited in quantity, travel is not an intended act of worship, and shaving is merely exiting worship. The hadith about concession is actually meant to refute the pre-Islamic belief that Umrah during Hajj months is sinful, not to show Qiran's inferiority. Furthermore, Qiran has Quranic basis in the verse 'Complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah', which is interpreted as performing both together from the beginning. It involves early and continuous ihram from the miqat, unlike Tamattu' where ihram is broken and then renewed. A key point: the difference also relates to rituals; according to the Hanafi school, the qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'ys (one for Umrah and one for Hajj), while al-Shafi'i holds that one tawaf and one sa'y suffice for both. This affects the practical virtue.

Key Terms
قِرَان (qiran): Performing Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram, without breaking ihram between them.
إِفْرَاد (ifrad): Performing Hajj alone without Umrah, dedicating the ihram solely for Hajj.
تَمَتُّع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then breaking ihram, and later entering ihram for Hajj in the same year.
رُخْصَة (rukhsah): A concession or dispensation allowing something that would otherwise be prohibited or less preferred.
أَفْضَل (afdal): More excellent or virtuous in terms of reward in the Sight of Allah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reason Qiran is considered the most excellent form of Hajj?
A) It is the only form explicitly mentioned in the Quran.
B) It was performed by the Prophet on his last Hajj.
C) It combines two acts of worship and was commanded by the Prophet for his family.
D) It requires fewer rituals than other forms.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the most excellent form of Hajj because it combines two acts of worship and was chosen by the Prophet for his family.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
The Most Virtuous Hajj: Hanafi Defense of Qiran
Inter-madhhab dispute on Hajj virtue with proofs and rebuttals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that Qiran is the most virtuous type of Hajj and evaluate the counter-arguments of the Shafi'i and Maliki schools.

Core Idea
Combining two acts of worship is more virtuous, so Qiran—combining Hajj and Umrah—is superior to Ifrad or Tamattu'.

Performing Hajj is a pillar of Islam, but scholars differ on which form—Ifrad, Qiran, or Tamattu'—is most virtuous. The Hanafi school, as presented in al-Hidayah, argues that Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram) is best, based on the Prophet's command and the principle of combining acts of worship. This lesson unpacks the proofs and responses to the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that Qiran is the most virtuous form of Hajj. Identify the key evidence: the Prophet's command to his family to combine Hajj and Umrah, and the analogy to combining fasting and i'tikaf.
This is the core claim being defended.
2
Identify the opposing schools and their proofs
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that Ifrad is superior based on a hadith that Qiran is a 'rukhsah' (concession) and that Ifrad has more talbiyah, travel, and halq. Imam Malik argues that Tamattu' is better because it is mentioned explicitly in the Quran (2:196).
Understand each proof before evaluating the Hanafi response.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to each opposing proof
For Shafi'i: the hadith about rukhsah actually refutes the Jahili belief that Umrah in Hajj months is sinful; concessions in this Shari'ah may be considered 'azimah. Talbiyah, travel, and halq are not sound measures of virtue. For Maliki: the verse 'Complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' is interpreted as commanding Qiran, so it is Quranically based.
Notice how the Hanafi response reinterprets the proofs rather than rejecting them outright.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
The difference affects the number of tawaf and sa'y performed by a Qarin. Hanafis require two tawaf and two sa'y (one each for Hajj and Umrah), while Shafi'is consider one tawaf and one sa'y sufficient. This practical difference underlies the disagreement in virtue.
This step connects the disputed ruling to actual practice.
5
Identify the underlying dispute
The schools differ on which type of Hajj the Prophet himself performed. Hanafis claim he performed Qiran, Malikis claim Tamattu', and Shafi'is claim Ifrad. Each school's position on virtue follows from their understanding of the Prophet's practice.
This deepens the understanding that ikhtilaf often traces back to different interpretations of the same sources.
