کو چاہئے کہ وہ مفرد کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ تلبیہ کہے اور رہا سفرتو وہ مقصود نہیں ہے۔ مقصود تو حج ہے اور سفر اس کو ادا کرنے کا وسیلہ ہے۔ اس لئے سفر وجہ ترجیح ثابت نہ ہوگا اور رہا حلق تو وہ بنفسہ عبادت نہیں بلکہ عبادت سے خروج ہے اس لئے حلق بھی وجہ ترجیح ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ روایت کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث القران رخصہ میں قرآن کی رخصت اور افراد کی عزیمت کو بیان کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ اہل جاہلیت کے ایک باطل عقیدہ کی تردید کرنا مقصود ہے ان کا عقیدہ یہ تھا کہ حج کے مہینوں میں عمرہ کرنا بد ترین گناہ ہے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ یہ عقید ہ غلط ہے بلکہ قران رخصت اسقاط ہے اور رخصت اسقاط اس شریعت میں عزیمت شمار ہوتا ہے پس جب قران کی اجازت ہے تو گویا اشہر حج میں عمرہ کی اجازت دی گئی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام مالک کی دلیل کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ قران کا قرآن پاک میں ذکر نہیں آیا غلط ہے کیونکہ باری تعالی کے قول واسمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلهِ سے ہی مراد ہے کہ حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام اپنے لوگوں کے جھونپڑوں سے باندھے اور حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھنا یہی قرآن ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے وجہ ترجیح بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ قران کی صورت میں حج کے احرام میں تجھیل ہے کیونکہ حج کا احرام ساتھ ہی باندھ لیا جاتا ہے اور تقبیل صفت محمود ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن کرنے میں حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احترام میقات سے لے کر دونوں کے افعال سے فراغت تک برابر باقی رہتا ہے۔ اس کے بر خلاف تمتع کہ تمتع کرنے میں افعال عمرہ ادا کرنے کے بعد احرام سے نکل جاتا ہے اور احرام کی استدامت بھی محمود ہے اس لئے قرآن تمتع سے اولیٰ ہوگا۔ بعض حضرات نے کہا ہے کہ یہ اختلاف کہ احناف کے نزدیک قرآن افضل ہے اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک افراد افضل ہے۔ اس پر مبنی ہے کہ قارن احناف کے نزدیک حج وعمرہ کے لئے دو طواف کرے گا اور دو ہی سعی کرے گا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک طواف وسعی میں تداخل ہو جائے گا۔ چنانچہ دونوں کے لئے ایک طواف اور ایک سعی کافی ہو جائے گی ۔ پس چونکہ دونوں کو جمع کرنے میں امام شافعی کے قول پر افعال ناقص ہوں گے یہ نسبت اس کے کہ ہر ایک کو الگ الگ کیا جائے۔ اس لئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک افراد افضل اور اولی ہے۔ فوائد بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کون سا حج کیا ہے چنانچہ احناف کا دعوی ہے کہ آپ نے حج قران کیا ہے اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ آپ نے حج تمتع کیا ہے اور امام شافعی کا دعوی ہے کہ آپ نے حج افراد گیا ہے۔ ہر ایک کے دلائل حدیث کی کتابوں میں مذکور ہیں۔
And because in Ifrad there is an increase of talbiyah, travel, and halq. And our proof is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O family of Muhammad, tie the ihram for Hajj and Umrah together.' And because in it two acts of worship are combined, so it resembles combining fasting and i'tikaf, and combining tahajjud prayer with guarding in the path of Allah. And talbiyah is countless, and travel is not the objective, and halq is exiting from worship. Therefore preference is not given by these things. And the purpose of the hadith narrated by Imam al-Shafi'i is to negate the statement of the people of Jahiliyyah (that performing Umrah during the months of Hajj is a grave sin). And Qiran is also mentioned in the Quran because the words of Allah 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' (al-Baqarah 2:196) mean to tie ihram for both from the dwellings of your people, according to what we have previously narrated. Then in Qiran there is quickness of ihram, and the sanctity of both remains equal from the miqat until completion, whereas Tamattu' is not like that, so Qiran is better than Tamattu'. And it was said that the difference between us and Imam al-Shafi'i is based on that in our view the Qarin performs two tawaf and two sa'y, while in Imam al-Shafi'i's view he performs one tawaf and one sa'y. Explanation: The Muhrim has three types: (1) Mufrid bil-Hajj, (2) Qarin, (3) Mutamatti'. There is a difference regarding their superiority. Thus he said: In our view Qiran is superior, in Imam al-Shafi'i's view Ifrad is superior, in Imam Malik's view Tamattu' is superior. Imam Malik's proof is that Tamattu' is mentioned in the Quran, as He said: 'Then whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj', and Qiran is not mentioned in the Quran, and it is well known that what is mentioned in the Quran is better than what is not. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof is the hadith of Aisha: 'Al-Qiranu rukhsatun', i.e., Qiran is a concession, Ifrad is an 'azimah, and it is clear that choosing the 'azimah is more virtuous than choosing the concession. So it is proven that Ifrad is superior. Second proof: In Hajj Ifrad there is an increase of talbiyah, travel, and halq, in that the Qarin will make one travel for both Hajj and Umrah, one talbiyah for both, and one halq for both, whereas the Mufrid will travel for Hajj alone, say talbiyah for Hajj alone, and do halq for Hajj alone. That is, in Qiran these three things are divided between Hajj and Umrah, whereas in Ifrad they are not divided. Our proof: The Prophet (peace be upon him) said: 'O family of Muhammad! Tie ihram for both Hajj and Umrah together.' Consider that the Messenger of Allah commanded his family to tie ihram for both together, and tying ihram for both together is called Qiran. So it is known that the Prophet commanded his family to do Qiran, and it is also clear that the Prophet only commands what is superior, not inferior. So it is proven that Qiran is superior. Second proof: In Qiran two acts of worship, Hajj and Umrah, are combined, so it resembles a person who combines fasting and i'tikaf, and in the battlefield prays tahajjud and also guards the Muslim army. As for Imam al-Shafi'i's rational argument, the answer is that talbiyah has no fixed quantity, so the Qarin should say more talbiyah than the Mufrid. As for travel, it is not the objective, the objective is Hajj, and travel is a means. So travel is not a basis for preference. As for halq, it is not in itself worship but exiting from worship, so halq is also not a basis for preference. The answer to the narration presented by Imam al-Shafi'i is that in the hadith 'Al-Qiranu rukhsah', the purpose is not to state that Qiran is a concession and Ifrad is an 'azimah, but rather to refute a false belief of the people of Jahiliyyah. Their belief was that performing Umrah during the months of Hajj is a grave sin. The Prophet said that this belief is false, rather Qiran is a concession, and a concession in this Shari'ah is considered an 'azimah. So when Qiran is permitted, it is as if permission for Umrah during the months of Hajj was given. The author of al-Hidayah, responding to Imam Malik's proof, said: 'Your statement that Qiran is not mentioned in the Quran is incorrect, because the words of Allah 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah' mean to tie ihram for both from the dwellings of your people, and tying ihram for both together is Qiran.' The author of al-Hidayah, stating the reason for preference, said: 'In Qiran there is quickness of ihram for Hajj because the ihram for Hajj is tied at the same time, and acceleration is a praiseworthy quality. Second reason: In Qiran the sanctity of both Hajj and Umrah remains equal from the miqat until completion of the actions of both, contrary to Tamattu' where after performing the actions of Umrah one exits from ihram, and the continuity of ihram is also praiseworthy, so Qiran is more virtuous than Tamattu'.' Some have said that this difference - that the Hanafis consider Qiran superior and Imam al-Shafi'i considers Ifrad superior - is based on that the Qarin, according to the Hanafis, performs two tawaf and two sa'y for Hajj and Umrah, while according to Imam al-Shafi'i, there is overlap (tadakhul) in tawaf and sa'y, so one tawaf and one sa'y suffice for both. Since in combining them according to Imam al-Shafi'i's view the actions would be deficient compared to doing each separately, therefore in his view Ifrad is superior and more virtuous. Benefit: The basis of the difference is what type of Hajj the Messenger of Allah performed. The Hanafis claim he performed Hajj Qiran, Imam Malik said he performed Hajj Tamattu', and Imam al-Shafi'i claims he performed Hajj Ifrad. The proofs of each are mentioned in the books of hadith.
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the most virtuous type of Hajj: Ifrad (Hajj only), Qiran (Hajj and Umrah combined with one ihram), and Tamattu' (Umrah first, then Hajj with separate ihrams). The Hanafi school (represented here by the author of al-Hidayah) holds Qiran as superior. Imam al-Shafi'i holds Ifrad as superior, and Imam Malik holds Tamattu' as superior. The passage presents each school's proofs and the Hanafi responses. Imam Malik's proof is that Tamattu' is explicitly mentioned in the Quran (2:196) while Qiran is not. The Hanafi response is that the same verse, 'And complete the Hajj and Umrah for Allah', is interpreted as commanding Qiran (combining both together), so Qiran is also Quranically based. Imam al-Shafi'i's proof includes a hadith that Qiran is a rukhsah (concession) and Ifrad is an 'azimah (determination), so the latter is better. The Hanafi response is that this hadith actually aims to refute the pre-Islamic belief that Umrah in Hajj months is sinful, not to rank concessions; moreover, in this Shari'ah, concessions are considered 'azimah. Shafi'i also argues that Ifrad involves more talbiyah, travel, and halq individually. The Hanafi response is that talbiyah is not quantifiable, travel is merely a means, and halq is not worship but exit from it. Additionally, the Hanafis argue that the Prophet commanded his family to do Qiran, indicating its superiority. The Hanafis also note that in Qiran, one combines two acts of worship, resembling combining fasting and i'tikaf or guarding the army while praying tahajjud. The passage concludes by noting that the underlying dispute stems from disagreement over which type of Hajj the Prophet himself performed. This is a classical ikhtilaf with practical implications: the Qarin performs two tawaf and two sa'y in the Hanafi school, whereas in the Shafi'i school one tawaf and one sa'y suffice; this difference influences the assessment of virtue.

Key Terms
افراد (ifrād): Performing only Hajj with one ihram, without combining Umrah.
قران (qirān): Combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram from the miqat.
تمتع (tamattu‘): Performing Umrah first during Hajj months, then Hajj with separate ihrams.
عزیمت (‘azīmah): A determined ruling (originally preferred), as opposed to rukhsah.
رخصت (rukhṣah): A concession or license, as opposed to 'azimah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Qiran considered more virtuous than Ifrad?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly said Qiran is superior in a hadith.
B) Because it combines two acts of worship, which is inherently more virtuous.
C) Because it requires more talbiyah, travel, and halq.
D) Because Imam al-Shafi'i held the opposite view.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that Qiran is the most virtuous form of Hajj because it combines two acts of worship, following the Prophet's command and the principle that combination enhances virtue.

Method of Performing Hajj Qiran - Description and Conditions
Describes the procedure for performing Qiran

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Hanafi method of performing Hajj Qiran and identify the condition that allows adding Hajj to an ongoing Umrah.

Core Idea
Qiran is combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram; the intention and talbiyah must mention both, starting with Umrah.

This lesson presents the standard Hanafi procedure for performing Hajj Qiran as described in al-Hidayah. You will learn the recommended wording of intention and talbiyah, the importance of mentioning Umrah first, and the key condition for adding Hajj to Umrah before completing four tawaf circuits. Understanding this method will help you correctly perform or guide others in the combined pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act
Recognize that Qiran means combining Hajj and Umrah in one state of ihram.
The term Qiran comes from the Arabic meaning 'to combine'.
2
Note the starting point
The pilgrim enters ihram for both from the miqat (the designated boundary).
Intention must be made for both together.
3
Memorize the intention wording
After the prayer, the pilgrim says: 'Allahumma inni uridu al-hajja wa al-‘umrata' and asks for ease and acceptance.
The wording is recommended but not obligatory for validity.
4
Understand the precedence of Umrah
In both intention and talbiyah, mention Umrah first because its actions (tawaf, sa'y) are performed first.
Talbiyah: 'Labbayk bi 'umratin wa hajjatin ma'an'.
5
Recognize the condition for changing intention
If a pilgrim started with Umrah alone, he can still make it Qiran by intending Hajj before completing four circuits of tawaf, as the majority of Umrah remains.
After four circuits, combination is no longer possible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَ صِفَةُ القِرَانِ أَنْ يُهِلَّ بِالْعُمْرَةِ وَالْحَج مَعًا مِنَ الْمِيقَاتِ وَيَقُولُ عَقِيبَ الصَّلوةِ اللَّهُمَّ إِنِّي أُرِيدُ الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ فَيَسِرُهُمَا لِىَ وَتَقَبَّلْهُمَا مِنِّي لأنَّ الْقِرَانَ هُوَ الْجَمْعُ بَيْنَ الْحَجِّ وَالْعُمْرَةِ مِنْ قَوْلِكَ قَرَنْتُ الشَّى بِالشَّيُّ إِذَا جَمَعْتُ بَيْنَهُمَا وَكَذَا إِذَا أَدْخَلَ حَجَّةً عَلَى عُمْرَةٍ قَبْلَ أَنْ يَطَّوفَ لَهَا أَرْبَعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ لِأَنَّ الْجَمْعَ قَدْ تَحَقَّقَ إِذِ الأَكْثَرَ مِنْهَا قَائِمُ وَمَتَى عَزَمَ عَلَى أَدَائِهِمَا يَسَّنَلَ التَيْسِيرَ فِيهِمَا وَقَدَّمَ الْعُمْرَةَ عَلَى الحَجّ فِيهِ وَ كَذلِک يَقُولُ لَبَيْكَ بِعُمَرَةٍ وَحَجَةٍ مَعَا لِأَنَّهُ يَبْدَأُ بِأَفَعَالِ الْعُمَرَةِ فَكَذَلِكَ يَبْدَأُ بِذِكْرِهَا وَإِنْ أَخَرَ ذَلِكَ فِي
He said: And the description of Qiran is that one enters ihram for Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat, and says after the prayer: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them from me,' because Qiran is the combination of Hajj and Umrah, from your saying 'qarantu al-shay'a bi al-shay'i' when you combine them. And likewise if he brings Hajj into Umrah before having performed four circuits of tawaf for it, because combination is achieved when the majority of it remains. And when he resolves to perform both, he asks for ease in them, and he gives precedence to Umrah over Hajj in his words. Likewise he says 'Labbayk bi 'umratin wa hajjatin ma'an' because he begins with the actions of Umrah, so he begins by mentioning it. And if he delays that in...
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement describing the method (sifah) of performing Hajj Qiran according to the Hanafi school. The pilgrim must enter ihram for both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously from the miqat. After a prayer (likely the two-rak'ah sunnah of ihram), he declares his intention: 'O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, make them easy and accept them from me.' The word 'Qiran' literally means combining, and this is achieved by making the intention for both together. If he intends Hajj after already having intended Umrah but before completing four circuits of tawaf, it is still considered Qiran because the majority of Umrah remains. Pilgrims are encouraged to ask for ease and to mention Umrah first in both intention and talbiyah, since the actions of Umrah come first. This ruling is straightforward and found in the matn of al-Hidayah, making it a memorization anchor.

Key Terms
تهليل (ihlāl): Entering the state of ihram and pronouncing talbiyah.
قَرَان (qirān): Combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram.
لَبَّيْكَ (labbayk): The talbiyah formula, here specified as 'Labbayk bi 'umratin wa hajjatin ma'an'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) 'Allahumma inni uridu al-hajja wa al-'umrata'

D) 'Nawaytu al-'umrata'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi method of Qiran requires intention for both Hajj and Umrah from the miqat, with Umrah mentioned first, and if starting with Umrah alone, Hajj must be added before completing four tawaf circuits.

Superiority of Hajj Qiran over Ifrad and Tamattu'
Hanafi argument for superiority of Qiran over Ifrad and Tamattu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that Qiran is superior to Ifrad and Tamattu', and evaluate the Shafi'i and Maliki counter-arguments.

Core Idea
Qiran is superior because it combines both Hajj and Umrah in a single continuous ihram, increasing devotion.

The types of Hajj—Ifrad, Tamattu', and Qiran—are all valid, but the schools differ on which is most virtuous. This passage presents the Hanafi case for Qiran, responding to the proofs of Imam Shafi'i (Ifrad) and Imam Malik (Tamattu'). Understanding this dispute reveals how each school interprets the same texts differently and how the ruling affects the number of rituals performed.

Guided Path
1
State the three types and the Hanafi position
Identify the three forms of Hajj: Ifrad (Hajj only), Tamattu' (Umrah then Hajj with break), and Qiran (Hajj and Umrah combined in one ihram). State that the Hanafi school holds Qiran as superior.
2
Identify the Hanafi proofs
List the evidence: talbiyah has no fixed quantity, so qarin says more; travel is a means, not an end; halq is not worship; Quran 2:196 implies Qiran; Qiran maintains continuous ihram reverence.
These proofs are both textual and rational.
3
Follow the opposing objections and Hanafi responses
Examine the Shafi'i claim that the Prophet performed Ifrad, and the Maliki claim that Qiran is not in the Quran. Understand how the Hanafi school refutes these: Shafi'i hadith refutes Jahili belief, not preference; Maliki claim is false because the verse commands both together.
4
Examine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: Hanafis require the qarin to perform two tawafs and two sa'ys (one for Umrah, one for Hajj), while Shafi'is allow one tawaf and one sa'y for both. This difference determines why Shafi'is prefer Ifrad (to avoid incomplete actions).
This is the key practical difference.
5
Recognize the root cause
The core of the dispute is which Hajj the Prophet ﷺ performed. Each school adduces its own hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جواب یہ ہے کہ تلبیہ کی کوئی مقدار مقرر نہیں ہے لہذا قارن کو چاہئے کہ وہ مفرد کے مقابلہ میں زیادہ تلبیہ کہے اور رہا سفرتو وہ مقصود نہیں ہے۔ مقصود تو حج ہے اور سفر اس کو ادا کرنے کا وسیلہ ہے۔ اس لئے سفر وجہ ترجیح ثابت نہ ہوگا اور رہا حلق تو وہ بنفسہ عبادت نہیں بلکہ عبادت سے خروج ہے اس لئے حلق بھی وجہ ترجیح ثابت نہ ہوگا۔ امام شافعی کی پیش کردہ روایت کا جواب یہ ہے کہ حدیث القران رخصہ میں قرآن کی رخصت اور افراد کی عزیمت کو بیان کرنا مقصود نہیں ہے بلکہ اہل جاہلیت کے ایک باطل عقیدہ کی تردید کرنا مقصود ہے ان کا عقیدہ یہ تھا کہ حج کے مہینوں میں عمرہ کرنا بد ترین گناہ ہے اللہ کے رسول صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا کہ یہ عقید ہ غلط ہے بلکہ قران رخصت اسقاط ہے اور رخصت اسقاط اس شریعت میں عزیمت شمار ہوتا ہے پس جب قران کی اجازت ہے تو گویا اشہر حج میں عمرہ کی اجازت دی گئی ۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے امام مالک کی دلیل کا جواب دیتے ہوئے فرمایا ہے کہ آپ کا یہ کہنا کہ قران کا قرآن پاک میں ذکر نہیں آیا غلط ہے کیونکہ باری تعالی کے قول واسمُوا الْحَجَّ وَالْعُمْرَةَ لِلهِ سے ہی مراد ہے کہ حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام اپنے لوگوں کے جھونپڑوں سے باندھے اور حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احرام ایک ساتھ باندھنا یہی قرآن ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے وجہ ترجیح بیان کرتے ہوئے فرمایا کہ قران کی صورت میں حج کے احرام میں تجھیل ہے کیونکہ حج کا احرام ساتھ ہی باندھ لیا جاتا ہے اور تقبیل صفت محمود ہے۔ دوسری وجہ یہ ہے کہ قرآن کرنے میں حج اور عمرہ دونوں کا احترام میقات سے لے کر دونوں کے افعال سے فراغت تک برابر باقی رہتا ہے۔ اس کے بر خلاف تمتع کہ تمتع شافعی کے نزدیک افراد افضل ہے۔ اس پر مبنی ہے کہ قارن احناف کے نزدیک حج وعمرہ کے لئے دو طواف کرے گا اور دو ہی سعی کرے گا۔ اور امام شافعی کے نزدیک طواف وسعی میں تداخل ہو جائے گا۔ چنانچہ دونوں کے لئے ایک طواف اور ایک سعی کافی ہو جائے گی ۔ پس چونکہ دونوں کو جمع کرنے میں امام شافعی کے قول پر افعال ناقص ہوں گے یہ نسبت اس کے کہ ہر ایک کو الگ الگ کیا جائے۔ اس لئے امام شافعی کے نزدیک افراد افضل اور اولی ہے۔ فوائد بنیاد اختلاف یہ ہے کہ رسول اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے کون سا حج کیا ہے چنانچہ احناف کا دعوی ہے کہ آپ نے حج قران کیا ہے اور امام مالک نے فرمایا کہ آپ نے حج تمتع کیا ہے اور امام شافعی کا دعوی ہے کہ آپ نے حج افراد گیا ہے۔ ہر ایک کے دلائل حدیث کی کتابوں میں مذکور ہیں۔
The answer is that talbiyah has no fixed quantity, so the qarin should say more talbiyah compared to the mufrid. As for travel, it is not the objective; the objective is Hajj, and travel is a means to perform it. Therefore, travel cannot be a basis for preference. As for halq (shaving), it is not worship in itself but an exit from worship, so halq also cannot be a basis for preference. The response to Imam Shafi'i's narration is that the hadith of qiran as a concession is not meant to state that qiran is a concession and ifrad is a resolve; rather, it aims to refute a false belief of the people of Jahiliyyah. Their belief was that performing Umrah during the months of Hajj is the worst sin. The Messenger of Allah ﷺ said that this belief is false. Rather, qiran is a concession and a lightening, and a concession that lightens is considered a resolve in this Sharia. So when qiran is permitted, it is as if Umrah is permitted during the months of Hajj. The author of Hidayah, responding to Imam Malik's proof, said that your claim that qiran is not mentioned in the Holy Quran is false, because the words of Allah 'wa asimū al-ḥajja wal-ʻumrata lillāh' mean that one should assume ihram for Hajj and Umrah from the huts of one's people, and assuming ihram for Hajj and Umrah together is exactly qiran. The author of Hidayah, stating the basis for preference, said that in the case of qiran, there is closeness in the ihram of Hajj because the ihram of Hajj is tied together with that of Umrah, and closeness is a praiseworthy quality. The second reason is that in qiran, the reverence of both Hajj and Umrah remains equal from the miqat until the completion of their actions. In contrast, in tamattu', after performing the actions of Umrah, one leaves ihram, and the continuity of ihram is also praiseworthy; therefore qiran is superior to tamattu'. Some people have said that this difference—that according to the Hanafis, qiran is superior, and according to Imam Shafi'i, ifrad is superior—is based on the fact that according to the Hanafis, the qarin will perform two tawafs for Hajj and Umrah and two sa'ys, whereas according to Imam Shafi'i, tawaf and sa'y interject, so one tawaf and one sa'y suffice for both. Since combining them according to Imam Shafi'i would result in incomplete actions compared to doing each separately, therefore according to Imam Shafi'i, ifrad is superior and preferable. The foundation of the difference is which Hajj the Messenger of Allah ﷺ performed: the Hanafis claim that he performed Hajj Qiran, Imam Malik said he performed Hajj Tamattu', and Imam Shafi'i claims he performed Hajj Ifrad. Each one's proofs are mentioned in books of hadith.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding the superiority of the different types of Hajj. The author presents the Hanafi position that Qiran is superior to both Ifrad (Shafi'i) and Tamattu' (Maliki). The Hanafi argument is based on rational and textual proofs. First, talbiyah has no fixed quantity, so the qarin can say more, indicating greater devotion. Second, travel is a means, not an end; the end is Hajj, so the length of travel does not make Ifrad superior. Third, shaving (halq) is not an act of worship but an exit from ihram, so it is not a basis for preference. Regarding the Shafi'i hadith that the Prophet ﷺ performed Ifrad, the Hanafi response is that this hadith was not meant to show Qiran as a concession and Ifrad as a resolve; rather, it refutes the pre-Islamic belief that Umrah during Hajj months is sinful. The Prophet ﷺ permitted Qiran, which effectively permitted Umrah at that time. In Hanafi law, a permissible concession is considered a resolve (azimah) in this Sharia. Against the Maliki claim that Qiran is not mentioned in the Quran, the author points to the verse 'wa atimmu al-hajja wal-ʻumrata lillah' (Quran 2:196), which they interpret as commanding both Hajj and Umrah together, i.e., Qiran. The Hanafis then give two reasons for Qiran's superiority: (1) it involves a single ihram for both acts, which is a praiseworthy closeness (tajhil), and (2) the reverence of ihram continues from the miqat until the completion of both, unlike Tamattu' where ihram is broken after Umrah. The practical consequence (thamar al-khilaf) is that in the Hanafi school, the qarin performs two separate tawafs and two sa'ys (one for Umrah, one for Hajj), while the Shafi'i school allows one tawaf and one sa'y to suffice for both. Because according to Shafi'is, combining results in incomplete actions compared to doing each separately, they prefer Ifrad. The root of the difference is which type of Hajj the Prophet ﷺ performed. Each school has its own hadith evidence.

Key Terms
قران (qiran): Combining Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram from the miqat.
افراد (ifrad): Performing only Hajj, without Umrah.
تمتع (tamattu'): Performing Umrah first, then Hajj separately in the same year, with a break of ihram between them.
تلبیہ (talbiyah): The formula recited upon entering ihram: 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...'

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is Qiran superior to Ifrad?
A) Because the Prophet ﷺ performed Ifrad
B) Because Qiran involves more talbiyah and preserves ihram continuity
C) Because Qiran is cheaper
D) Because the Quran explicitly commands Qiran

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds Qiran as the superior type of Hajj due to its combination of acts, continuous reverence, and interpretation of the Quranic command.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Method of Performing Hajj Qiran
Description of the method of performing Qiran from miqat to entering Makkah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the method of performing Hajj Qiran and apply the ruling that the pilgrim becomes a qarin when adding the intention for Hajj before completing four circuits of Umrah tawaf.

Core Idea
In Qiran, the pilgrim combines Hajj and Umrah from the miqat; adding Hajj before four tawaf circuits is valid because the majority of the Umrah remains.

The Hanafi school provides a detailed method for performing Hajj Qiran, where the pilgrim combines Umrah and Hajj in a single ihram. This lesson walks you through the key steps—from the initial talbiyah at the miqat to the sequence of tawaf and sa'y upon entering Makkah. You will also learn the critical condition under which a pilgrim who initially intended only Umrah can validly add the intention for Hajj, becoming a qarin.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Recognize that Qiran means combining Hajj and Umrah in one ihram, and it is a recommended (sunnah) type of Hajj.
Al-Quduri begins by describing the sifah (manner) of Qiran.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the Quranic verse 'fa man tamatta'a bi al-umrati ila al-hajj' (2:196) to give precedence to Umrah over Hajj.
The verse is used as a proof for performing Umrah actions first.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The phrasing of the verse presents Umrah before Hajj, indicating that the Umrah actions should be performed before the Hajj actions in a combined journey.
This is a linguistic (dalala) argument for the sequence.
4
Apply the conditional ruling
If a pilgrim adds Hajj after starting Umrah tawaf but before completing four circuits, he becomes a qarin because the majority of tawaf remains, treating the act as if no tawaf was performed.
This is based on the principle that the majority stands for the whole (al-akthar yaqumu maqam al-kull).
5
Understand the sufficiency of intention
Intention in the heart suffices; verbal talbiyah not required, by analogy with prayer.
This is a clarification to avoid the misconception that verbal pronouncement is obligatory.

[Al-Quduri] said: The description of Qiran is that one recites talbiyah for both Umrah and Hajj together from the miqat, and says after prayer: O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them from me. Because Qiran is the combination of Hajj and Umrah from your saying 'qarantu al-shay'a bi al-shay'i' when you combine them. Likewise, if one includes Hajj upon Umrah before completing four circuits of tawaf for it, because combination is achieved since the majority of it remains. When one resolves to perform both, he should ask for ease in them, and he gives precedence to Umrah over Hajj in that, and similarly he says 'Labbayk bi-umratin wa hajjatan ma'an' because he begins with the actions of Umrah, so he begins with its mention. If he delays that in the supplication and talbiyah, there is no harm because the waw indicates combination. If he intended in his heart and did not mention them in the talbiyah, it suffices by analogy with prayer. Commentary: Shaykh Abu al-Hasan says: The description of Qiran is that one assumes ihram for both Hajj and Umrah from the miqat and recites talbiyah for both, and after the prayer of reverence recites this supplication: O Allah, I intend Hajj and Umrah, so make them easy for me and accept them from me. The proof is that Qiran, meaning combining Hajj and Umrah, is derived from 'qarantu al-shay'a bi al-shay'i' which is used when you combine two things. Al-Quduri says: If someone assumed ihram for Umrah only and performed fewer than four circuits of tawaf—for example three—then intended Hajj, that person becomes a qarin, and his Hajj is Hajj Qiran because the majority of the tawaf remains. So the majority is treated as the whole, and it is said that he has not yet performed the tawaf of Umrah, and when he has not performed the tawaf of Umrah, combining Umrah and Hajj is actualized, and this is called Qiran. Therefore, in this case Qiran is actualized. When one resolves to perform both, he should pray for ease, and perform the actions of Umrah first and the actions of Hajj later, and in the talbiyah he says 'Labbayk bi-umratin wa hajjatan ma'an' because in the case of Qiran, since the beginning is with the actions of Umrah, he should mention it first. However, if he delays Umrah in the supplication and talbiyah, there is no harm because the waw indicates combination. But it is better to mention Umrah first because Allah Almighty gave precedence to Umrah in His saying 'fa man tamatta'a bi al-umrati ila al-hajj'. Al-Quduri says: If someone intended in his heart and did not mention Hajj and Umrah verbally in the talbiyah, it is allowed, just as in prayer verbal intention is not a condition; similarly here, verbal intention is not a condition. Then when he enters Makkah, he begins and performs tawaf around the House seven circuits, performing ramal in the first three of them, and after that he performs sa'y between Safa and Marwah. These are the actions of Umrah. Then he begins the actions of Hajj and performs tawaf al-qudum seven circuits and afterwards performs sa'y as we explained in the case of the mufrid. He gives precedence to the actions of Umrah due to the saying of Allah Most High: 'fa man tamatta'a bi al-umrati ila al-hajj', and Qiran is similar in meaning to Tamattu'. And he does not shave between...
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage gives the detailed method (sifah) of performing Hajj Qiran. It is a ruling with proof, based on linguistic derivation and analogy with prayer. The method begins at the miqat, where the pilgrim recites the talbiyah for both Hajj and Umrah together, and says a specific supplication after a prayer. The word 'qiran' itself comes from the Arabic meaning 'to join two things'. A key rule: if a person already in ihram for Umrah decides to add Hajj before completing four circuits of tawaf for Umrah, the combination is valid because the majority of tawaf remains; this is based on the principle that the majority stands for the whole. The qarin should ask for ease in performing both, and should perform the actions of Umrah first (tawaf and sa'y), then the actions of Hajj (tawaf al-qudum and sa'y). In the talbiyah, it is recommended to mention Umrah before Hajj because the actions of Umrah come first, but if one delays the mention, it is still valid because the conjunction 'wa' (and) indicates combination. The intention in the heart is sufficient; verbal pronouncement is not required, by analogy with prayer. Upon entering Makkah, the qarin immediately performs tawaf (with ramal in the first three circuits) and sa'y for Umrah. Then he performs tawaf al-qudum and sa'y for Hajj. The Hanafi school emphasizes that Qiran is similar to Tamattu' in the sense of combining, but with the difference that in Qiran, ihram is not broken between Umrah and Hajj. The passage also notes that the qarin does not shave (halq) between the two acts, meaning he remains in ihram until after Hajj actions are completed.

Key Terms
صفة القران (sifat al-qiran): The manner of performing Hajj Qiran, including the talbiyah, intention, and sequence of actions.
رمل (ramal): Walking briskly with short steps and shoulder movements during the first three circuits of tawaf.
طواف القدوم (tawaf al-qudum): The tawaf performed upon arrival in Makkah by a pilgrim who is not a resident; the qarin performs this after the Umrah tawaf.
تداخل (tadakhul): Interjection; the Shafi'i view that one tawaf and one sa'y suffice for both Hajj and Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person is performing Umrah and has completed three circuits of tawaf, then decides to add the intention for Hajj, what is the ruling?
A) He becomes a qarin and his Hajj is valid
B) He cannot add Hajj after starting Umrah
C) He must finish Umrah first and then start Hajj separately
D) His Umrah becomes invalid

Key Takeaway
In Qiran, the pilgrim combines Hajj and Umrah with a single ihram, performing two separate tawafs and sa'ys, and the intention in the heart suffices without verbal pronouncement.

Ruling on Du'a and Talbiyah in Qiran
Rules on du'a, talbiyah wording, and sufficiency of intention in heart for Qiran.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why intention (niyyah) in the heart suffices for Qiran and apply the analogy (qiyas) to salah to derive the ruling.

Core Idea
Intention in the heart suffices for Qiran; talbiyah is verbal confirmation, not a pillar.

This passage addresses a common question: must a Qarin utter the talbiyah precisely to make his ihram valid? The author clarifies that what matters is the internal intention, analogizing to salah. Understanding this principle resolves many practical doubts about the ihram formula.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is entering ihram for Qiran (Hajj and Umrah combined). The ruling is that it is valid (sahih) even if the talbiyah is not uttered, as long as intention is present.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to salah, where intention is in the heart. The text says 'إِعْتِبَارًا بِالصَّلوة' (by analogy to prayer).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In salah, niyyah is a condition fulfilled by the heart's intention, not by verbal utterance. Similarly, in ihram, the intention to enter the state of consecration is internal; the talbiyah is a recommended verbal confirmation but not essential for validity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools may require the verbal talbiyah for ihram, but the Hanafi school holds that intention in the heart suffices, based on the analogy to salah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الدَّعَاءِ وَالتَّليَّةِ لَا بَأسَ بِهِ لأَنَّ الْوَاوَ بِالْجَمْعِ وَلَوْنَوَى بِقَلْبِهِ وَلَمْ يَذْكُرُهُمَا فِي التَلْبَيَةِ أَجْزَاهُ إِعْتِبَارًا بِالصَّلوة.
Regarding the supplication and the talbiyah: there is no harm in it, because the waw is for conjunction. And if he intends in his heart and does not mention them in the talbiyah, it suffices him, by analogy to prayer.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This concise matn ruling addresses two aspects of the Qiran form of Hajj. First, the du'a and talbiyah: the Qarin may recite a specific du'a after the prayer asking Allah to make Hajj and Umrah easy and accept them. In the talbiyah, he says 'Labbayk bi 'Umratin wa Hajjah', mentioning Umrah first because its actions precede Hajj. However, if he reverses the order or omits one, it is still valid because the waw (wa) indicates conjunction, not sequence. Second, if he intends both worships in his heart without uttering them in the talbiyah, it suffices. This is by qiyas (analogy) to salah, where intention (niyyah) is in the heart and verbal utterance is not required. Thus, the validity of ihram for Qiran depends on the internal intention, not on the specific wording of the talbiyah.

Key Terms
تَلْبِيَة (talbiyah): The specific phrase 'Labbayk Allahumma labbayk...' recited upon entering ihram, here mentioning both Hajj and Umrah.
قِرَان (qiran): The type of Hajj where one enters ihram for both Umrah and Hajj simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The ihram is invalid.
B) The ihram is valid and sufficient.
C) He must repeat the intention verbally.
D) He must sacrifice an animal.

Key Takeaway
Intention in the heart makes Qiran valid; the talbiyah is a recommended verbalization, not a requirement.

Actions of the Qarin Upon Entering Makkah
Describes the sequence of tawaf and sa'i for the Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the sequence of tawaf and sa'i for a Qarin upon entering Makkah and explain why he does not shave between Umrah and Hajj.

Core Idea
A Qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'is upon entering Makkah—first for Umrah, then for Hajj.

This lesson details the specific sequence of rituals for a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) upon entering Makkah. Unlike the Mufrid (Hajj-only pilgrim), the Qarin begins with Umrah actions, then proceeds to Hajj actions, all while remaining in ihram. Understanding this order is essential to correctly performing Qiran.

Guided Path
1
Identify the pilgrim type
Note that the subject is the Qarin, who intends both Umrah and Hajj with a single ihram. This affects the sequence of actions.
The Mufrid only has Hajj actions; the Mutamatti' performs Umrah first then Hajj with separate ihrams.
2
State the Umrah sequence
Upon entering Makkah, the Qarin first performs the Umrah tawaf (7 circuits) with raml in the first three, followed by sa'i between Safa and Marwah.
Raml is brisk walking with shoulders bared, sunnah for men in any tawaf followed by sa'i.
3
State the Hajj sequence
After completing Umrah actions, the Qarin performs the Hajj tawaf (tawaf al-qudum, 7 circuits) with raml in the first three, followed by another sa'i.
The text says 'seven circuits' but the OCR note corrects an error: it should be seven, not nine.
4
Explain the rationale for the order
The order (Umrah before Hajj) is derived from the Quranic verse on Tamattu' (2:196), and Qiran is considered similar in meaning (fee ma'na al-mut'ah).
Abu Hanifa and his students consider Qiran a type of Tamattu', hence the same order.
5
Explain the shaving prohibition
The Qarin does not shave after Umrah because it would violate the ihram of Hajj. He only shaves on the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr), like the Mufrid.
Shaving breaks ihram; the Qarin remains in Hajj ihram until the Day of Sacrifice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِذَا دَخَلَ مَكَةَ ابْتَدَأَوَطَافَ بِالْبَيْتِ سَبْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ يُرَمَلُ فِى الثَّلَتِ الأَوَّلِ مِنْهَا وَيَسْعَى بَعَدَهَا بَينَ الصَّفَا وَالْمَرْوَةِ وهذا أَفَعَالُ الْعُمْرَةِ ثُمَّ يَبْدَأُ بأفعال الحَج فَيَطُوفُ طَوَافَ القُدُوْمِ تَسْعَةَ أَشْوَاطٍ وَيَسْعَى بَعْدَهُ كَمَا بَيْنَا فِي الْمُفْرِدِ وَيُقَدِّمُ أَفْعَالَ الْعُمْرَةِ لِقُولِ تَعَالَى فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَقِّ وَالْقِرَانُ فِي مَعْنَى الْمُتَعَةِ وَلَا يَحِلقٌ بَيْنَ الْعُمْرَةِ وَ الْحَجّ لِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ جِنايَةُ على إِحْرَامِ الْحَج وَإِنَّمَا يَحْلِقُ فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ كَمَا يَحْلِقُ الْمُفْرِدُ
So when he enters Makkah, he begins and circumambulates the House seven circuits, performing raml in the first three of them, and performs sa'i after that between Safa and Marwah. This is the actions of Umrah. Then he begins the actions of Hajj: he circumambulates the tawaf of arrival seven circuits and performs sa'i after it, as we explained in al-Mufrid. He gives precedence to the actions of Umrah due to the saying of the Exalted: 'So whoever performs Tamattu' with Umrah to Hajj...' and Qiran is in the meaning of Tamattu'. He does not shave between Umrah and Hajj, because that would be an offense against the ihram of Hajj. He only shaves on the Day of Sacrifice, as the Mufrid shaves.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage provides the detailed sequence of rituals for a Qarin upon entering Makkah. Unlike the Mufrid (who performs tawaf al-qudum first), the Qarin begins with the Umrah tawaf, performing raml (brisk walking with shoulders bared) in the first three circuits. After tawaf, he performs sa'i between Safa and Marwah. This completes the Umrah portion. Then he performs the Hajj portion: he performs tawaf al-qudum (also with raml in the first three) and then another sa'i. This sequence is based on the Quranic verse (2:196) which mentions Umrah before Hajj in Tamattu', and since Qiran is similar in meaning, the same order applies. The Qarin does not shave or cut his hair after Umrah because he remains in ihram for Hajj; shaving would be a violation (jinayah) of the Hajj ihram. He only shaves on the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr) after completing all Hajj rites, just as the Mufrid does.

Key Terms
رَمَل (ramal): Brisk walking with shoulders bared during tawaf, performed in the first three circuits.
طَوَاف الْقُدُوم (tawaf al-qudum): The arrival tawaf performed by a person entering Makkah from outside.
قِرَان (qiran): Performing Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram.
مُفْرِد (mufrid): One who performs Hajj alone without Umrah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Two tawafs, two sa'is.
C) Two tawafs, one sa'i.
D) One tawaf, two sa'is.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin must perform two separate tawafs and sa'is upon entering Makkah—first for Umrah, then for Hajj—and must not shave until the Day of Sacrifice.

Hanafi vs Shafi'i on Number of Tawafs for Qarin
Dispute on number of tawafs for Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of tawafs and sa'is for a Qarin and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the concepts of tadakhul and maqasid.

Core Idea
In Qiran, the arkan of each worship must be performed completely; means can overlap, but ends cannot.

This passage presents a classic inter-madhhab dispute: does the Qarin perform one or two tawafs and sa'is? The Hanafi school insists on two of each, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that one suffices due to the principle of tadakhul. The Hanafi response relies on Companion practice and a logical distinction between means (wasa'il) and ends (maqasid). Let's unpack the arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed ruling
Determine the exact issue: the number of tawafs and sa'is for the Qarin. The Hanafi school says two of each; Imam al-Shafi'i says one of each.
Both agree the Qarin combines Umrah and Hajj with one ihram.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
The Shafi'i argument is based on the hadith 'Umrah entered into Hajj' and the principle of tadakhul (overlap), citing that the Qarin uses one talbiyah, one journey, and one shaving, so similarly the arkan should overlap.
This hadith is also used to justify the permissibility of Qiran itself.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from practice
The Hanafis cite the report of Subay' ibn Ma'bad, who performed two tawafs and two sa'is as a Qarin, and 'Umar's approval: 'You have been guided to the Sunnah of your Prophet.' This gives direct Companion endorsement.
This is a dalil naqli (narrative proof) with zanni thubut and dalala.
4
Understand the logical argument
Hanafis distinguish between wasa'il (means) and maqasid (ends). The journey, talbiyah, and shaving are means to enter and exit ihram; they can overlap. But tawaf and sa'i are the objectives of the worshps, and each worship must be performed completely without overlap.
This is a rational argument based on the nature of worship.
5
Apply the analogy of voluntary prayer
Just as two rak'ahs of nafl are performed with one takbir but do not overlap (they remain separate units), similarly the arkan of Umrah and Hajj remain separate even if combined in one journey.
The analogy shows that overlapping means does not imply overlapping ends.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ يَتَحَلَّلُ بِالْحَلْقِ عِنْدَنَا لَا بِالذَّبْحِ كَمَا يَتَحَلَّلُ الْمُفْرِد ثُمَّ هَذَا مِنْ مَذْهَبِنَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي يَطُوفُ طَوَافًا وَاحِدَاوَ يَسْعَى سَعيًا وَاحِدًا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دَخَلَتِ الْعُمَرَةُ فِى الْحَجّ إِلى يَوْمِ الْقِيمَةِ وَلِأَنَّ مَبْنَى الْقِرَانِ عَلَى التَّدَا خُلِ حَتَّى اكْتُقِيَ فِيهِ بِتَلِيَّةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَسَفَرٍ وَاحِدٍ وَحَلْقِ وَاحِدٍ فَكَذَلِكَ فِي الْأَرْكَانِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ لَمَّا طَافَ صُبى بْنُ مَعْبَدٍ طَوَافَيْنِ وَ سَعَى سَعَينِ قَالَ لَهُ عُمَرُ هُدِيتَ لِسُنَّةِ نَبِيِّكَ وَلِأَنَّ الْقِرَانَ ضَمُّ عِبَادَةِ إِلى عِبَادَةٍ وَذُلِكَ إِنَّمَا يَتَحَقَّقُ بِادَاءِ عَمَلِ كُلَّ وَاحِدَ عَلَى الْكَمَالِ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا تَدَاخُلَ فِى الْعِبَادَاتِ الْمُقْصُودَةِ وَالسَّفَر للتوسل والتلبية للتحريم وَالْحَلَقَ لِلتَّحَلُّلِ فَلَيْسَتْ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاء بِمَقَاصِدَ بِخِلَافِ الْأَرْكَانِ الْاتَرَى أَنَّ شَفَتَى التَّطَوع لَا يَتَدَا خَلَانِ وَ بِتَحْرِيمَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ يُودْيَانِ وَمَعْنَى مَارَوَاهُ دَخَلَ وَقْتُ الْعُمْرَةِ فِي وَقْتِ الْحَج
And he becomes permitted (halal) by shaving according to us, not by sacrificing, as the Mufrid becomes halal. Then this is from our madhhab. Al-Shafi'i said: He performs one tawaf and one sa'i, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Umrah has entered into Hajj until the Day of Resurrection,' and because the basis of Qiran is on tadakhul (overlap), so that one talbiyah, one journey, and one shaving suffice for it; thus likewise in the pillars. And our proof: that when Subay' ibn Ma'bad performed two tawafs and two sa'is, 'Umar said to him: 'You have been guided to the Sunnah of your Prophet.' And because Qiran is the combining of one worship to another worship, and that is only realized by performing the actions of each completely. And because there is no tadakhul in the primary acts of worship (maqsudah), while the journey is a means (tawassul), the talbiyah is for making ihram, and the shaving is for becoming halal; these things are not aims (maqasid), unlike the pillars (arkan). Do you not see that the two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer do not overlap (tadakhalan) and are performed with a single tahrimah? And the meaning of what he narrated ('Umrah entered into the time of Hajj' is that the time of Umrah entered into the time of Hajj.
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage presents a full inter-madhhab dispute. The Hanafi position (stated first) is that the Qarin becomes halal by shaving, not by sacrificing, like the Mufrid. Then it contrasts the Shafi'i position: Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the Qarin performs only one tawaf and one sa'i, because the Prophet said, 'Umrah has entered into Hajj until the Day of Resurrection,' implying tadakhul (overlap). Also, since the Qarin suffices with one talbiyah, one journey, and one shaving, similarly the arkan should be combined. The Hanafi response provides two proofs. First, the reported practice of Subay' ibn Ma'bad, who performed two tawafs and two sa'is as a Qarin, and 'Umar (radiAllahu anhu) approved him, saying 'You have been guided to the Sunnah of your Prophet.' This indicates that the correct practice is two of each. Second, a logical argument: Qiran means combining two worships, which requires performing the actions of each completely without overlap. The journey, talbiyah, and shaving are mere means (tawassul) and not the objectives (maqasid), so they can be combined, but the arkan (tawaf, sa'i) are the objectives themselves and cannot be merged. An analogy is two rak'ahs of nafl prayer: they are performed with a single takbirat al-ihram, yet they remain separate units without overlapping. Finally, the Hanafis interpret the hadith 'Umrah entered into Hajj' as referring to the time (waqt), i.e., the time for Umrah is within the time for Hajj, not that the acts themselves merge.

Key Terms
تَدَاخُل (tadakhul): The concept that acts of worship overlap or are subsumed into one another, reducing the total number of actions.
مَقَاصِد (maqasid): The intrinsic aims or objectives of an act of worship (e.g., tawaf, sa'i).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the Hanafi position on the number of tawafs and sa'is for a Qarin?
A) One tawaf and one sa'i.
B) Two tawafs and one sa'i.
C) Two tawafs and two sa'is.
D) One tawaf and two sa'is.

Key Takeaway
For the Qarin, the Hanafi school requires two separate tawafs and two sa'is because the arkan of Umrah and Hajj are independent objectives that cannot overlap.

Qarin's Tawaf and Sa'y: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i Dispute
Dispute on number of tawaf and sa'y for Qarin, and method of tahlul

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the number of tawafs and sa'y for the Qarin, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument using the principle of tadakhul.

Core Idea
Tadakhul applies to means, not ends: a Qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'ys because each worship is distinct.

This lesson examines a key inter-madhhab dispute regarding the rituals of the Qarin—one who performs Hajj and Umrah in a single ihram. The Hanafi school requires separate tawaf and sa'y for each, while the Shafi'i school allows a single set. We will analyze the evidence and the principle of tadakhul (interpenetration) that underlies the disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school requires: two tawafs and two sa'y s, and tahlul by shaving not sacrifice.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its dalil
State that Shafi'i allows one tawaf and one sa'y, based on the hadith 'Dakhalat al-umrah fi al-hajj' and analogy with tadakhul in travel and talbiyah.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Explain how the Hanafis interpret the hadith as referring to time, and why tadakhul in means does not extend to ends.
4
Understand the Hanafi supporting evidence
Examine the hadith of Subay' ibn Ma'bad and the analogy with voluntary prayers.
5
Determine the practical consequence
Note that the Hanafi Qarin performs more actions, while the Shafi'i Qarin does fewer; tahlul method also differs.

الْعُمْرَةِ وَ الْحَجّ لِأَنَّ ذَلِكَ جِنايَةُ على إِحْرَامِ الْحَج وَإِنَّمَا يَحْلِقُ فِي يَوْمِ النَّحْرِ كَمَا يَحْلِقُ الْمُفْرِدُ وَيَتَحَلَّلُ بِالْحَلْقِ عِنْدَنَا لَا بِالذَّبْحِ كَمَا يَتَحَلَّلُ الْمُفْرِد ثُمَّ هَذَا مِنْ مَذْهَبِنَا وَقَالَ الشَّافِعِي يَطُوفُ طَوَافًا وَاحِدَاوَ يَسْعَى سَعيًا وَاحِدًا لِقَوْلِهِ عَلَيْهِ السَّلَامُ دَخَلَتِ الْعُمَرَةُ فِى الْحَجّ إِلى يَوْمِ الْقِيمَةِ وَلِأَنَّ مَبْنَى الْقِرَانِ عَلَى التَّدَا خُلِ حَتَّى اكْتُفِيَ فِيهِ بِتَلِيَّةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ وَسَفَرٍ وَاحِدٍ وَحَلْقِ وَاحِدٍ فَكَذَلِكَ فِي الْأَرْكَانِ وَلَنَا أَنَّهُ لَمَّا طَافَ صُبَي بْنُ مَعْبَدٍ طَوَافَيْنِ وَ سَعَى سَعَينِ قَالَ لَهُ عُمَرُ هُدِيتَ لِسُنَّةِ نَبِيِّكَ وَلِأَنَّ الْقِرَانَ ضَمُّ عِبَادَةِ إِلى عِبَادَةٍ وَذُلِكَ إِنَّمَا يَتَحَقَّقُ بِادَاءِ عَمَلِ كُلَّ وَاحِدَ عَلَى الْكَمَالِ وَلِأَنَّهُ لَا تَدَاخُلَ فِى الْعِبَادَاتِ الْمُقْصُودَةِ وَالسَّفَر للتوسل والتلبية للتحريم وَالْحَلَقَ لِلتَّحَلُّلِ فَلَيْسَتْ هَذِهِ الْأَشْيَاء بِمَقَاصِدَ بِخِلَافِ الْأَرْكَانِ الْاتَرَى أَنَّ شَفْعَى التَّطَوُّع لَا يَتَدَا خَلَانِ وَ بِتَحْرِيمَةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ يُؤَدِّيَانِ وَمَعْنَى مَارَوَاهُ دَخَلَ وَقْتُ الْعُمْرَةِ فِي وَقْتِ الْحَج
[The Umrah] and Hajj because that is an offense against the ihram of Hajj, and he only shaves on the Day of Sacrifice just as the individual performer (mufrid) shaves. And he becomes halal by shaving according to us, not by slaughter, just as the individual performer becomes halal. Then this is our madhhab. Al-Shafi'i said: He performs one tawaf and one sa'y, due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'Umrah has entered into Hajj until the Day of Resurrection,' and because the basis of Qiran is on interpenetration (tadakhul) such that one talbiyah, one travel, and one shaving suffice for it, so likewise in the pillars (arkan). And our evidence is that when Subay' ibn Ma'bad performed two tawafs and two sa'y s, Umar said to him: 'You have been guided to the sunnah of your Prophet.' And because Qiran is the joining of one worship to another, and that is only realized by performing the actions of each completely. And because there is no interpenetration in intended acts of worship. Travel is a means, talbiyah is for making ihram sacred, and shaving is for tahlul. These things are not ends in themselves, unlike the pillars. Do you not see that the two rak'ahs of voluntary prayer do not interpenetrate, yet they are performed with a single opening takbir? And the meaning of what he narrated is: 'The time of Umrah has entered into the time of Hajj.'
Source pages p. 383

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the rituals of the Qarin (one who performs Hajj and Umrah together). The text first states the Hanafi position: the Qarin, upon entering Makkah, should perform the acts of Umrah first (tawaf with raml and sa'y), then the acts of Hajj (tawaf al-qudum and another sa'y). He should not shave between them; shaving is only on Yawm al-Nahr. Then the dispute is introduced: According to the Hanafis, the Qarin becomes halal by shaving, not by sacrifice, similar to the Mufrid. Then the Shafi'i view is presented: a single tawaf and a single sa'y suffice for both Hajj and Umrah, because the Prophet said 'Umrah has entered into Hajj until the Day of Resurrection,' and because Qiran implies interpenetration (tadakhul) – one talbiyah, one journey, and one shaving suffice, so the same should apply to the pillars. The Hanafis respond with several proofs: First, the hadith that Subay' ibn Ma'bad performed two tawafs and two sa'y s, and Umar (radiAllahu anhu) praised him, indicating the sunnah is to perform two. Second, Qiran means combining two distinct acts of worship, so each must be performed fully. Third, there is no tadakhul in acts that are ends in themselves (maqasid); travel, talbiyah, and shaving are means (wasail), not ends, so they can be shared, but the pillars (tawaf and sa'y) are ends and cannot be merged. The author analogizes to voluntary prayers: two separate rak'ahs do not interpenetrate even if performed with a single takbir. Finally, the Shafi'i hadith is interpreted as meaning the time of Umrah enters the time of Hajj, not that the acts themselves merge. The relied-upon Hanafi position is that the Qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'y s, and tahlul is by shaving.

Key Terms
قرآن (Qiran): A type of Hajj where one enters ihram with the intention of both Hajj and Umrah simultaneously.
تداخل (tadakhul): Interpenetration or merging of acts so that one performance fulfills two obligations.
تحلل (tahlul): The act of leaving the state of ihram, normally by shaving or cutting hair.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, how many tawafs must a Qarin perform?
A) One tawaf
B) Two tawafs
C) Three tawafs
D) None, only sa'y is required

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school requires a Qarin to perform two tawafs and two sa'ys because intended acts of worship do not interpenetrate; the Shafi'i view that acts merge is based on a different interpretation of the same hadith.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
10 min
Separate Tawaf and Sa'i Required for the Qiran (Hanafi vs. Shafi'i)
Inter-madhhab dispute on number of tawaf/sa'i for Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on the required number of tawaf and sa'i for a Qarin, support it with the hadith of Subay' ibn Ma'bad, and evaluate the Shafi'i argument based on the hadith 'dakhilat al-'umrah fi al-hajj'.

Core Idea
A Qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'is because acts of worship do not interpenetrate.

This lesson tackles a key difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools regarding the rituals of Hajj al-Qiran. The Hanafi school requires the Qarin to perform separate tawaf and sa'i for his 'umrah and hajj, while the Shafi'i school holds that one set suffices. The dispute rests on the interpretation of prophetic hadith and the principle of whether acts of worship can overlap. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between means and ends in ritual law.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafi school holds that a Qarin must perform two separate tawafs and two separate sa'is—one for 'umrah and one for hajj. The main proof is the hadith of Subay' ibn Ma'bad, who performed two tawafs and two sa'is, and 'Umar (RA) confirmed he had followed the Sunnah.
This is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opposing Shafi'i position and its proof
Imam al-Shafi'i (and Imam Malik, and one narration of Ahmad) holds that one tawaf and one sa'i suffice. Their proof is the hadith 'dakhilat al-'umrah fi al-hajj ila yawm al-qiyamah' (Umrah is included in Hajj until the Day of Resurrection), and the analogy that since means (travel, talbiyah, halq) are combined, the pillars (tawaf and sa'i) should also be combined.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i proof
The Hanafis respond that the hadith refers to the permissibility of performing 'umrah during the months of hajj, not to the merging of rituals. Moreover, there is a fundamental distinction between means (wasail) and ends (maqasid). Means can be shared, but ends—the actual acts of worship—cannot interpenetrate. This is illustrated by the example of nafl prayers: two separate units cannot be combined into one, even though one intention (tahrimah) suffices for multiple.
The key principle: 'La tadakhul fi al-ibadat al-maqsudah' (no interpenetration in intended acts of worship).
4
Examine the ruling on incorrect order (dam not due)
The text also discusses a scenario where the Qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'is but delays the sa'i of 'umrah and advances the tawaf al-qadum (arrival tawaf). Despite this improper order, no penalty (dam) is due. According to Abu Hanifa, this is because tawaf al-qadum is a sunna, and omitting a sunna does not require blood, so advancing it also does not. According to the Sahibayn, any precedence or delay in rituals does not incur blood.
This shows the flexibility within the Hanafi school regarding order, as long as the essential acts are performed.
5
Conclude with the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical consequence is that a Hanafi Qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'is, whereas a Shafi'i Qarin performs one each. If a Hanafi mistakenly does only one tawaf, his hajj may still be valid but he must make a dam? The text does not specify; the ruling is that the required acts are separate. For the improper order, no compensation is due.

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم کتاب الحج یہ ہے کہ جب میی بن معبد نے دو طواف اور دوستی کیں تو اس سے حضرت عمر نے کہا تو نے اپنے نبی صلى الله عليه وسلم کی سنت کی راہ پائی اور اس لئے کہ قران ایک عبادت کو دوسری عبادت میں ملانے کا نام ہے اور یہ ہر ایک کے افعال پورے پورے ادا کرنے سے متحقق ہوگا۔ اور اس لئے کہ عبادات مقصورہ میں تداخل نہیں ہے۔ اور سفر وسیلہ ہے اور تلبیہ تحریم کے لئے ہے اور حلق حلال ہونے کے لئے ہے۔ پس یہ چیزیں مقصود بالذات نہیں ہیں۔ برخلاف ارکان کے ، کیا نہیں دیکھتے ہو کہ نفل کے دو شفع متداخل نہیں ہوتے حالانکہ دونوں ایک تحریمہ سے ادا ہو جاتے ہیں اور اس کے معنی جس کو امام شافعی نے روایت کیا یہ ہے کہ عمرہ کا وقت حج کے وقت میں داخل ہو گیا۔ تشریح شیخ ابوالحسن قدوری فرماتے ہیں کہ قارن ہمارے نزدیک حلق کے ذریعہ ہی احترام سے نکلے گا ذبح کے ذریعہ احترام سے نہیں نکلے گا۔ جس طرح مفرد بالمج حلق کے ساتھ احترام سے نکلتا ہے۔ حلال ہونے میں ذبح کو کوئی دخل نہیں ہے۔ چنانچہ قارن اگر یوم نحر میں قربانی کر کے خوشبو وغیرہ استعمال کرے گا تو اس پر جرمانہ لازم ہو گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ قارن کا افعال حج اور افعال عمرہ دونوں کو الگ الگ ادا کرنا ہمارا مذ ہب ہے ورنہ تو امام شافعی کے نزدیک قارن حج اور عمرہ دونوں کے لئے ایک ہی طواف کرے گا اور ایک ہی سعی کرے گا یہی امام مالک کا مذہب ہے اور امام احمد کی ایک روایت بھی یہی ہے۔ امام شافعی کی دلیل قول نبی کریم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم دَخَلَتِ الْعُمْرَةُ فِي الْحَجَ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَةِ ہے یعنی عمر و قیامت تک حج میں داخل ہو گیا پس اس حدیث کی روشنی میں افعال حج، افعال عمرہ کے لئے بھی کافی ہو جائیں گے۔ یعنی حج کا طواف اور سعی عمرہ کے طواف اور سعی کے لئے کفایت کریں گے عمرہ کے لئے علیحدہ طواف اور سعی کرنے کی چنداں ضرورت نہیں ہے ورنہ وہ عمرہ حج میں داخل نہ ہوگا۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قران کی بنیاد تداخل پر ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ قرآن میں حج اور عمرہ دونوں کے لئے ایک ہی تلبیہ ہوتا ہے ایک ہی سفر ہوتا ہے اور حلال ہونے کے لئے ایک ہی حلق ہوتا ہے۔ پس اسی طرح ارکان یعنی طواف اور سعی میں بھی تداخل ہوگا چنانچہ دونوں کے لئے ایک طواف اور ایک سعی کافی ہے۔
ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ صبی بن معبد جو حج قرآن ادا کر رہے تھے انہوں نے دو طواف کئے اور دوسھی کیں تو فاروق اعظم نے فرمایا کہ تو نے اپنے نبی کی سنت کی راہ پائی۔ اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ رسول اللہ صلى الله عليه وسلم کی سنت یہ ہے کہ قارن دو طواف کرے اور دو سعی کرے، دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ قران ایک عبادت کو دوسری عبادت کے ساتھ ملانے کا نام ہے اور یہ اسی صورت میں متحقق ہوگا جبکہ دونوں میں سے ہر عبادت کے افعال کو پورا پورا ادا کرے۔ ہماری طرف سے تیسری دلیل اور امام شافعی کی عقلی دلیل کا جواب یہ ہے کہ عبادات مقصودہ میں تداخل نہیں ہوتا مثلا دو نمازوں میں تداخل نہیں ہوگا کہ ایک نماز دوسری نماز کے قائم مقام ہو جائے اور رہا سفر تو وہ مکہ تک پہنچ کر افعال ادا کرنے کا وسیلہ اور ذریعہ ہے اور تلبیہ کہنا ما سوائے احرام کو حرام کرنے کا ذریعہ ہے اور حلق کرنا احرام سے نکلنے کا ذریعہ ہے یہ تینوں چیزیں وسائل کا درجہ رکھتی ہیں ان کے برخلاف ارکان کہ وہ مقاصد کا درجہ رکھتے ہیں اس لئے ان مسائل پر ارا کان کو قیاس کرنا درست نہ ہوگا ملاحظہ فرمائیے کہ نفل کے بعد دو، دوگانہ یعنی دو دورکعت متداخل نہیں ہو سکتیں یعنی ایسا نہیں ہو سکتا کہ فل کا ایک دوگانہ ادا کرنے سے دو، دوگانہ یعنی چار رکعت ادا ہو جائیں ۔ حالانکہ اگر دو، دوگانہ یعنی نفل کی چار رکعت ایک تحریمہ سے ادا کرنا چاہے تو ادا کر سکتا ہے۔ پس تحریمہ جو حصول نماز کا وسیلہ ہے وہ دو، دوگانہ یعنی چار رکعت کے لئے ایک کافی ہے لیکن ارکان عبادت متداخل نہ ہوں گے ورنہ دونوں دوگانہ متداخل ہو کر فقط ایک دوگانہ سے ادا ہو جاتے بلکہ ہزاروں دوگانہ نہ صرف دو رکعت یعنی ایک دوگانہ سے ادا ہو جایا کرتے۔ رہی امام شافعی کی وہ حدیث کہ قیامت تک عمرہ حج میں افضل ہو گیا اس کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ عمرہ کا وقت جن کے وقت میں داخل ہو گیا اور اس سے مقصود اہل جاہلیت کے قول ( کہ اشہر حج میں عمرہ کرنا بد ترین گناہ ہے) کی تردید اور ابطال کرنا ہے۔
دو طواف اور دوستی کا حکم
قَالَ وَ إِنْ طَافَ طَوَافَيْنِ لِعُمْرَتِهِ وَحَجَّتِهِ وَسَعَى سَعْيَيْنِ يُجْزِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ أَتَى بِمَا هُوَ الْمُسْتَحَقُّ عَلَيْهِ وَقَدْ أَسَاءَ بِتَأْخِير سَعيِ العُمَرَةِ وَتَقْدِيمِ طَوافِ التَّحِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِ وَ لَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَيْءٍ أَمَّا عِندَهُمَا فَظَاهِرُ لِأَنَّ التَّقْدِيمَ وَالتَّاخِيرَ فِى الْمَتَاسِك لَا يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ عِنْدَهُمَا وَعِندَة طَوَافُ التَّحِيَّةِ سُنّة وَتَرَكة لا يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ فَتَقْدِيمُهُ أَولَى وَالسَّعَى بِتَأخِيرِم بِالاشْتِغَالِ بِعَمَلِ آخَرَ لَا يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ فَكَذَا بِالاشْتِغَالِ بِالطَّوَافِ ترجمہ کہا اور اگر اپنے عمرہ اور حج کے لئے دوطواف کئے ۔ اور دو سعی کیں تو یہ اس کو کفایت کرے گا۔ کیونکہ وہ اس چیز کو لایا جو اس پر واجب تھی البتہ اس نے عمرہ کی سعی کو مؤخر کر کے اور طواف قدوم کو سعی پر مقدم کر کے برا کیا اور اس پر کچھ لازم نہ ہو گا چنانچہ صاحبین کے نزدیک تو ظاہر ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک مناسک میں تقدیم و تاخیر موجب دم نہیں ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک طواف قدوم سنت ہے اور اس کا ترک موجب دم نہیں ہے لہذا اس کی تقدیم تو بدرجہ اولی موجب دم نہ ہوگی۔ اور سعی اپنی تاخیر کی وجہ سے دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہو کر دم واجب نہیں کرتی پس اس طرح طواف کے ساتھ مشغول ہونا بھی موجب دم نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قارن نے دو طواف کئے یعنی ایک طواف سات شوط کا عمرہ کے لئے پھر دوسرا طواف یعنی حج کا طواف قدوم کیا پھر دو سعی کہیں ایک عمرہ کے لئے دوسری حج کے لئے تو یہ جائز ہے۔ کیونکہ جس بات کا اس پر استحقاق ہے اس کو بجا لایا لیکن اس نے برا کیا کیونکہ عمرہ کی سعی حج کے طواف قدوم سے مؤخر ہو گئی ہے حالانکہ عمرہ کی سعی طواف قدوم سے مقدم ہونی چاہئے تھی اور طواف قدوم عمرہ کی سعی سے متقدم ہو گیا حالانکہ طواف قدوم عمرہ کی سعی سے مؤخر ہونا چاہئے تھا لیکن اس تقدیم اور تاخیر کی وجہ سے اس پر جرمانہ ( دم ) واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک مناسک حج اور عمرہ کی تقدیم اور تاخیر سے دم وغیرہ کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک تاوان اس لئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے اور اسکا بالکل ترک کرنا دم واجب نہیں کرتا تو اس کو مقدم کر دینا بدرجہ اولی دم وغیرہ جرمانہ واجب نہ کرے گا۔ اور رہا عمرہ کی سعی کا طواف قدوم سے مؤخر ہونا تو اس سے بھی دم واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ سعی کا طواف کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے مؤخر ہونا موجب دم نہیں ہے۔ مثلاً عمرہ کے طواف کے بعد کھانے پینے اور سونے میں مشغول ہو گیا پھر عمرہ کی سعی کی تو کچھ واجب نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اسی طرح حج کے طواف قدوم کے ساتھ مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے اگر عمرہ کی سعی مؤخر ہو گئی تو اس سے بھی دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔
Commentary on Al-Hidayah: The explanation of the ruling that a Qarin must perform two tawafs and two sa'is. It mentions the hadith of Subay' ibn Ma'bad and the dispute with Imam Shafi'i. Then the matn from Al-Hidayah: 'And if he performs two tawafs for his 'umrah and hajj and two sa'is, it suffices him because he has done what was required of him, and he has done wrong by delaying the sa'i of 'umrah and advancing the tawaf of arrival (tahiyyah) over it, and nothing is incumbent upon him. As for according to the two (Sahibayn), it is apparent because precedence and delay in the rituals do not necessitate blood (dam) according to them. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), the tawaf of arrival is a sunna, and its complete omission does not necessitate blood, so its precedence is even less likely. And the sa'i, by delaying it through engagement in another act, does not necessitate blood, so similarly does engagement in tawaf.' Followed by Urdu translation and explanation.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the number of tawaf and sa'i a Qarin must perform. The Hanafi position, supported by the hadith of Subay' ibn Ma'bad, requires two separate tawafs and two sa'is—one for 'umrah and one for hajj. Imam al-Shafi'i, citing the hadith 'dakhilat al-'umrah fi al-hajj,' holds that one tawaf and one sa'i suffice. The Hanafi response distinguishes between means (travel, talbiyah, halq) which can be combined, and ends (the actual acts of worship) which cannot interpenetrate. It also addresses the ruling on incorrect order: if one performs the tawafs and sa'is but delays the 'umrah sa'i or advances the tawaf al-qadum, the act remains valid with no penalty (dam) due, based on either the Sahibayn's general rule or Abu Hanifa's reasoning that the omitted sunna does not incur blood.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): A person performing Hajj al-Qiran, combining 'umrah and hajj with one ihram.
طواف (ṭawāf): Circumambulation of the Ka'bah; a pillar of hajj and 'umrah.
سعی (saʿy): Walking between Safa and Marwah; a wajib act of hajj and 'umrah.
دم (dam): Blood; a sacrificial penalty required for certain violations in hajj.
تداخل (tadākhul): Interpenetration or overlapping of acts; Hanafis hold it does not occur in acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on a Qarin who performs two tawaf and two sa'is but delays the sa'i of 'umrah after the tawaf of arrival?
A) His hajj is invalid and he must repeat it.
B) He has fulfilled his obligation but has done wrong, and no penalty is due.
C) He must offer a dam for the incorrect order.
D) He must repeat the sa'i in the correct order.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin must perform two separate tawafs and two sa'is for his 'umrah and hajj; if he does so but in the wrong order, no penalty is due.

Sacrificial Animal (Dam) Required for the Qarin
Ruling on the type of sacrifice for the Qarin and timing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the types of animals permissible for dam al-qiran and the timing of slaughter according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The Qarin must slaughter a goat, cow, camel, or a share in one after stoning on the Day of Nahr.

In Hajj al-Qiran, the pilgrim combines 'umrah and hajj and is required to offer a sacrificial animal (dam al-qiran). This lesson explains which animals are acceptable, the permissibility of sharing, and when the slaughter must take place. The ruling is analogous to tamattu'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Timing
The slaughter must occur after stoning the Jamrat al-'Aqabah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah).
This timing is specific to the Qarin.
2
List Permissible Animals
The text lists a goat, a cow, a camel (budnah), or one-seventh of a camel or cow.
One-seventh indicates sharing is allowed.
3
Understand 'Budnah'
Here budnah means specifically a camel, though the term can apply to a cow in other contexts.
This clarification avoids confusion.
4
Note the Basis
The ruling is because Qiran is similar to Tamattu', which has a prescribed hadi.
The hadi is from camels, cows, and goats.
5
Apply the Ruling
The Qarin must fulfill this wajib act; failure requires compensation.
Compensation details are beyond this passage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قارن کے لئے ذبح کا حکم
قَالَ وَإِذَا رَمَى الْجَمْرَةَ يَوْمَ النَّحْرِ ذَبَحَ شَاةَ أوْ بَقَرَةً أو بُدَنَةً أَوْ سَبْعَ بُدَنَةٍ فَهَذَا دَمُ الْقِرَانِ لِأَنَّهُ فِي مَعْنَى الْمُتَعَةِ وَالْهَدَى مَنصُوصُ عَلَيْهِ فِيْهَا وَالْهَدَى مِنَ الْإِبِلِ وَالْبَقَرَ وَالْغَنَمِ عَلَى مَانَذَكُرُهُ فِى بَابِهِ إِنْشَاءَ اللهُ وَأَرَادَ بِالْبَدِّنَةِ هُنَا الْبَعِيرُ وَإِنْ كَانَ إِسْمُ الْبُدْنَةِ يَقَعُ عَلَيْهِ وَعَلَى الْبَقَرِ عَلى ما ذَكَرْنَا وَكَمَا يَجُوزُ سَبْعُ الْبعير يَجُوزُ سَبْعُ الْبَقَرَة ترجمه قدوری نے کہا اور جب یوم نحر کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کر چکا تو ذبیح کرے ایک بکرٹی یا گائے یاد نہ یا بد نہ کا ساتواں حصہ۔ یہ دم قران
The ruling on slaughtering for the Qarin: He (Al-Quduri) said: And when he has stoned the Jamrat al-'Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a goat, or a cow, or a camel, or one-seventh of a camel. This is the blood (dam) of Qiran, because it is similar to Tamattu', and the hadi (sacrificial animal) is prescribed therein. The hadi is from camels, cows, and goats, as we will mention in its chapter, God willing. Here budnah means camel, although the name budnah applies to both camel and cow as we mentioned. And just as one-seventh of a camel is permissible, so is one-seventh of a cow. Urdu translation: Al-Quduri said: When he has stoned Jamrat al-'Aqabah on the Day of Nahr, he slaughters a goat, cow, or camel, or one-seventh of a budnah. This is the dam of Qiran.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage states the ruling regarding the sacrificial animal required for the Qarin. After stoning the Jamrat al-'Aqabah on the Day of Nahr (10th Dhul Hijjah), the Qarin must slaughter an animal as dam al-qiran. The permissible animals are: a goat, a cow, a camel, or one-seventh of a camel or cow. This ruling is because the Qiran is similar to Tamattu', for which the hadi (sacrificial animal) is prescribed in the Qur'an. The text clarifies that 'budnah' here specifically refers to a camel, although the term can also apply to a cow. The author also notes that sharing in a camel or cow (one-seventh each) is permissible.

Key Terms
دم القران (dam al-qirān): The sacrificial animal required from a person performing Hajj al-Qiran as a penalty for combining 'umrah and hajj.
بدنة (budnah): In this context, specifically a camel, though the term can also apply to a cow.
یوم النحر (yawm al-nahr): The Day of Slaughtering, i.e., the 10th of Dhul Hijjah.
جمرة عقبة (jamrat al-ʿaqabah): The large pillar (jamrah) closest to Mina, used in stoning ritual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) A whole camel
B) A whole cow
C) A goat
D) One cow for seven Qarins

Key Takeaway
The Qarin must slaughter a goat, cow, camel, or a share of one, after stoning on the Day of Nahr.

Ruling on Two Tawafs and Two Sa'is for Qiran: No Penalty for Improper Order
Intra-Hanafi dispute on penalty for improper order of tawaf and sa'i for a qarin.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'is in improper order, and explain why no dam is required according to both Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
A qarin's two tawafs and two sa'is are valid; improper order between them does not require dam.

This passage from Al-Quduri's matn, as expanded in Al-Hidayah, addresses a practical scenario for a qarin (one performing Hajj and 'Umrah together). The key question is whether violating the preferred order between tawaf and sa'i incurs a penalty. The Hanafi school unanimously says no, but their justifications differ. This lesson unpacks the two lines of reasoning and clarifies the underlying principles.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and ruling
Identify the act: a qarin performs two tawafs and two sa'is but reverses the order of sa'i of 'Umrah and tawaf al-tahiyyah. The ruling: it suffices, and no dam is required.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement
Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) agree on the ruling but differ in reasoning. Note the two arguments.
3
Trace Imam Abu Hanifa's argument
He argues that tawaf al-tahiyyah is a sunnah; omission of a sunnah does not require dam, so advancement is even less significant. Also, delaying sa'i due to another act (like tawaf) does not require dam.
This is a talil (causality) based on the nature of the act.
4
Trace the Sahibayn's argument
They hold a general principle: advancement or delay in any ritual (manasik) never necessitates dam.
This is a broader usul-based argument.
5
Derive the practical implication
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) is that only the reasoning differs, but the outcome is the same. This illustrates that the Hanafi school prioritizes the validity of the act over strict order.
Use this to reinforce the concept of ikhtilaf within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قَالَ وَإِنْ طَافَ طَوَافَيْنِ لِعُمْرَتِهِ وَحَجَّتِهِ وَسَعَى سَعْيَيْنِ يُجْزِيهِ لِأَنَّهُ أَتَى بِمَا هُوَ الْمُسْتَحَقُّ عَلَيْهِ وَقَدْ أَسَاءَ بِتَأْخِيرِ سَعْيِ الْعُمْرَةِ وَتَقْدِيمِ طَوَافِ التَّحِيَّةِ عَلَيْهِ وَلَا يَلْزَمُهُ شَيْءٌ أَمَّا عِنْدَهُمَا فَظَاهِرٌ لِأَنَّ التَّقْدِيمَ وَالتَّأْخِيرَ فِي الْمَنَاسِكِ لَا يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ عِنْدَهُمَا وَعِنْدَهُ طَوَافُ التَّحِيَّةِ سُنَّةٌ وَتَرْكُهُ لَا يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ فَتَقْدِيمُهُ أَوْلَى وَالسَّعْيُ بِتَأْخِيرِهِ بِالاشْتِغَالِ بِعَمَلٍ آخَرَ لَا يُوجِبُ الدَّمَ فَكَذَا بِالاشْتِغَالِ بِالطَّوَافِ. ترجمہ: کہا اور اگر اپنے عمرہ اور حج کے لئے دو طواف کئے اور دو سعی کیں تو یہ اس کو کفایت کرے گا کیونکہ وہ اس چیز کو لایا جو اس پر واجب تھی البتہ اس نے عمرہ کی سعی کو مؤخر کر کے اور طواف قدوم کو سعی پر مقدم کر کے برا کیا اور اس پر کچھ لازم نہ ہو گا چنانچہ صاحبین کے نزدیک تو ظاہر ہے کیونکہ ان کے نزدیک مناسک میں تقدیم و تاخیر موجب دم نہیں ہے اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک طواف قدوم سنت ہے اور اس کا ترک موجب دم نہیں ہے لہذا اس کی تقدیم تو بدرجہ اولیٰ موجب دم نہ ہوگی اور سعی اپنی تاخیر کی وجہ سے دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہو کر دم واجب نہیں کرتی پس اس طرح طواف کے ساتھ مشغول ہونا بھی موجب دم نہ ہوگا۔ تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر قارن نے دو طواف کئے یعنی ایک طواف سات شوط کا عمرہ کے لئے پھر دوسرا طواف یعنی حج کا طواف قدوم کیا پھر دو سعی کیں ایک عمرہ کے لئے دوسری حج کے لئے تو یہ جائز ہے کیونکہ جس بات کا اس پر استحقاق ہے اس کو بجا لایا لیکن اس نے برا کیا کیونکہ عمرہ کی سعی حج کے طواف قدوم سے مؤخر ہو گئی ہے حالانکہ عمرہ کی سعی طواف قدوم سے مقدم ہونی چاہئے تھی اور طواف قدوم عمرہ کی سعی سے متقدم ہو گیا حالانکہ طواف قدوم عمرہ کی سعی سے مؤخر ہونا چاہئے تھا لیکن اس تقدیم اور تاخیر کی وجہ سے اس پر جرمانہ (دم) واجب نہ ہوگا۔ صاحبین کے نزدیک تو اس لئے کہ ان کے نزدیک مناسک حج اور عمرہ کی تقدیم اور تاخیر سے دم وغیرہ کوئی تاوان واجب نہیں ہوتا اور امام صاحب کے نزدیک تاوان اس لئے واجب نہ ہوگا کہ طواف قدوم سنت ہے اور اس کا بالکل ترک کرنا دم واجب نہیں کرتا تو اس کو مقدم کر دینا بدرجہ اولیٰ دم وغیرہ جرمانہ واجب نہ کرے گا۔ اور رہا عمرہ کی سعی کا طواف قدوم سے مؤخر ہونا تو اس سے بھی دم واجب نہ ہوگا کیونکہ سعی کا طواف کے علاوہ کسی دوسرے کام میں مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے مؤخر ہونا موجب دم نہیں ہے مثلاً عمرہ کے طواف کے بعد کھانے پینے اور سونے میں مشغول ہو گیا پھر عمرہ کی سعی کی تو کچھ واجب نہیں ہوتا پس اسی طرح حج کے طواف قدوم کے ساتھ مشغول ہونے کی وجہ سے اگر عمرہ کی سعی مؤخر ہو گئی تو اس سے بھی دم واجب نہ ہوگا۔
He said: And if he performs two tawafs for his 'Umrah and Hajj, and performs two sa'is, it suffices him, because he has brought what is due upon him. However, he has done wrong by delaying the sa'i of 'Umrah and advancing tawaf al-tahiyyah over it, and nothing is incumbent upon him. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), it is apparent because advancement and delay in the rituals do not necessitate blood (dam) according to them. And according to him (Abu Hanifa), tawaf al-tahiyyah is a sunnah, and its abandonment does not necessitate blood, so its advancement is even more (permissible). And delaying the sa'i by engaging in another act does not necessitate blood, so likewise by engaging in tawaf.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof and an intra-Hanafi dispute. The author (Al-Quduri) states that if a qarin (one performing Hajj and 'Umrah together) performs two tawafs (one for each) and two sa'is, it is valid. Although he acted improperly by delaying the sa'i of 'Umrah and performing tawaf al-tahiyyah (the arrival tawaf for Hajj) before it, no penalty (dam) is required. The reason differs between the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) and Imam Abu Hanifa. The Sahibayn hold that any advancement or delay in the rituals never requires dam. Imam Abu Hanifa argues that tawaf al-tahiyyah is a sunnah, and its complete omission does not require dam, so its advancement is even less problematic. Additionally, delaying sa'i due to another act (like eating or sleeping) does not require dam, so delaying it due to performing tawaf also does not. This illustrates the Hanafi principle that order between rituals is not obligatory for validity, though it is recommended.

Key Terms
طواف التحيَّة (tawaf al-tahiyyah): The arrival tawaf performed upon entering Makkah for Hajj, also called tawaf al-qudum.
سعي (sa'y): The ritual walking between Safa and Marwah, wajib in Hajj and 'Umrah.
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice (of a sheep, goat, or share of a larger animal) required as penalty for certain violations or as thanks.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, why does Imam Abu Hanifa hold that no dam is required for advancing tawaf al-tahiyyah over the sa'i of 'Umrah?
A) Because tawaf al-tahiyyah is a fard and its advancement is obligatory.
B) Because tawaf al-tahiyyah is a sunnah and its omission does not require dam, so its advancement is even less significant.
C) Because the Sahibayn said so.
D) Because the Quran explicitly permits it.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the order between tawaf and sa'i is not a condition of validity; a qarin who performs two tawafs and two sa'is in improper order does not incur any penalty.
