Dam al-Qiran and Its Substitute of Fasting
Establishes the obligation of sacrifice (dam al-qiran) and its alternative of fasting ten days

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the obligation of dam al-qiran on the qarin, explain the qiyas linking qiran to tamattu', and apply the alternative ruling of fasting ten days.

Core Idea
The qarin must sacrifice or fast ten days, just like the mutamatti', due to qiyas on irtifaq bi-nusukayn.

This passage from Al-Hidayah clarifies the ruling for a qarin (one performing Hajj and 'Umrah together). After stoning the Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, the qarin must offer a sacrifice (dam al-qiran) from sheep, cow, or camel. If he cannot afford an animal, he must fast ten days: three during Hajj (the last being the Day of 'Arafah) and seven after returning home. The proof is qiyas on tamattu', based on Quran 2:196.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What must the qarin do after stoning the Jamrat al-Aqabah? He must slaughter a sacrificial animal (dam al-qiran). Identify the hukm level: wajib.
2
Specify the conditions of the sacrifice
The sacrifice can be a sheep, cow, camel, or a seventh share of a camel or cow. The animal must meet the conditions of hady (e.g., healthy, minimum age). The time is after stoning on the Day of Sacrifice.
Sharing in a large animal (up to seven people) is allowed.
3
Recognize the proof: qiyas on tamattu'
The obligation of sacrifice for the qarin is not directly in the Quran; it is derived by qiyas (analogy) on tamattu'. The asl is tamattu' (hady wajib by Quran 2:196). The illah is benefiting from performing two rituals (irtifaq bi-nusukayn). The far is qiran. Hence the same ruling applies.
The Quranic text is qat'i al-thubut but zanni al-dalala.
4
Identify the alternative: fasting
If the qarin cannot find or afford an animal, he must fast ten days: three days during Hajj (preferably the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, Yawm al-Tarwiyah, and Yawm 'Arafah) and seven days after returning home.
The fasting is a substitute (badal) for the sacrifice.
5
Apply the preference: delay fasting
It is recommended to delay the three days of fasting as late as possible (to just before Yawm al-Nahr) in the hope that one may later afford the animal.
The intent is to give priority to the original obligation (sacrifice).

أَنْ يَقْدِرَ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ. ترجمہ: قدوری نے کہا اور جب یوم نحر کو جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کر چکا تو ذبح کرے ایک بکری یا گائے یا اونٹ یا بد نہ کا ساتواں حصہ۔ یہ دم قران ہے کیونکہ قرآن تمتع کے معنی میں ہے اور ہدی کی قربانی تمتع میں منصوص علیہ ہے۔ اور ہدی اونٹ، گائے اور بکری سے ہوتی ہے چنانچہ ہم اس کو انشاء اللہ اس کے باب میں ذکر کریں گے۔ اور یہاں بدنہ سے مراد اونٹ ہے اگر چہ بدنہ کا لفظ اونٹ، گائے دونوں پر بولا جاتا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے ذکر کیا اور جس طرح اونٹ کا ساتواں حصہ جائز ہے اسی طرح گائے کا ساتواں حصہ بھی جائز ہے۔ تشریح: فرماتے ہیں کہ قارن جب یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کر چکا تو وہ ایک بکری یا گائے یا اونٹ یا بد نہ کا ساتواں حصہ قربانی کرے اور اس کا نام دم قرآن ہے۔ اس قربانی کے واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن، حج اور عمرہ کو جمع کرنے میں تمتع کے معنی میں ہے اور تمتع کے اندر ہدی کی قربانی منصوص ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَجِّ فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدْی (البقرة 196) پس جب حج تمتع میں قربانی واجب ہے تو قرآن میں بھی واجب ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہدی، اونٹ، گائے، بکری سب کی ہوتی ہے۔ تفصیل باب الہدی میں ذکر کی جائے گی۔ اور یہاں بدنہ سے اونٹ مراد ہے اگر چہ بدنہ کا لفظ اونٹ اور گائے دونوں پر بولا جاتا ہے پس جس طرح اونٹ کے ساتویں حصہ کی قربانی جائز ہے اسی طرح گائے کے ساتویں حصہ کی قربانی بھی جائز ہے۔ اور جب قارن کے پاس ذبح کے لئے کوئی چیز نہ ہو تو تین دن کے حج میں روزے رکھے کہ آخری دن عرفہ کا دن ہو۔ اور سات روزے جب اپنے اہل میں واپس آئے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ جو کوئی ہدی نہ پائے تو اس پر واجب ہے تین دن کے روزے حج میں اور سات جب تم لوٹو۔ یہ دس پورے ہوئے۔ پس نص اگر چہ تمتع کے حق میں وارد ہوئی ہے لیکن قرآن بھی اسی کے مثل ہے کیونکہ قارن بھی حج وعمرہ دونوں نسک سے مستفید ہے۔ اور حج سے مراد واللہ اعلم اس کا وقت ہے اس لئے کہ نفس حج ظرف بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ مگر افضل یہ ہے کہ یوم ترویہ سے ایک دن پہلے کا اور یوم ترویہ اور یوم عرفہ کا روزہ رکھے۔ کیونکہ روزہ رکھنا تو ہدی کا بدل ہے پس اصل یعنی ہدی پر قدرت کی امید کے پیش نظر اس کے آخری وقت تک روزہ کو مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے۔ تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قارن اگر قربانی کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو بایں طور کہ گنجائش نہ ہو یا گنجائش تو ہو مگر جانور دستیاب نہ ہو تو اس پر دس روزے واجب ہوں گے اس طور پر کہ تین روزے یوم نحر سے پہلے حج کے زمانہ میں رکھے اور سات روزے جب اپنے گھر واپس آئے۔ دلیل باری تعالى كا قول فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَاثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَسَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمْ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةٌ (البقرة 196) ہے۔ یہ آیت اگر چہ حج تمتع کے حق میں وارد ہوئی ہے مگر چونکہ قرآن بھی اسی کے مثل ہے بایں طور کہ قارن اور متمتع دونوں حج اور عمرہ کی دو دو عبادتیں کرتے ہیں۔ پس اس مشارکت اور مماثلت کی وجہ سے جو حکم تمتع ہے وہی قرآن کا ہو گا۔
He said: And when he has stoned the Jamrah on the Day of Sacrifice, he slaughters a sheep, or a cow, or a camel, or a seventh of a camel. This is the dam of qiran because it is in the meaning of tamattu', and the hady (sacrificial animal) is explicitly mentioned in it. And the hady is from camels, cows, and sheep as we will mention in its chapter, if Allah wills. And by 'badanah' here he means a camel, although the term 'badanah' applies to both camel and cow as we mentioned. And just as a seventh of a camel is permissible, so too is a seventh of a cow permissible. Then if he does not have what to slaughter, he fasts three days during Hajj, the last of which is the Day of 'Arafah, and seven days when he returns to his family, due to the saying of Allah the Exalted: 'And whoever cannot find [a sacrificial animal] – then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you have returned; that is ten complete [days].' So the text, although it came regarding tamattu', the qiran is similar to it, because he benefits from performing two rituals. And what is meant by 'Hajj' – and Allah knows best – is its time, because the [act of] Hajj itself is not suitable as a time. However, the best is that he fasts the day before Yawm al-Tarwiyah, Yawm al-Tarwiyah, and Yawm 'Arafah, because fasting is a substitute for the hady, so it is recommended to delay it to its last time in the hope that he may be able to perform the original [sacrifice].
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof establishing the sacrifice (dam al-qiran) required of a qarin. After stoning Jamrat al-Aqabah on the 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the qarin must slaughter a sheep, cow, or camel (or a seventh share of a larger animal). This is called dam al-qiran. The reason: qiran is analogous to tamattu' (where hady is explicitly required by Quran 2:196). The term 'badanah' here specifically means a camel, though it can also apply to a cow. Sharing in a camel or cow (up to seven people) is allowed. If the qarin cannot afford an animal, he must fast three days during Hajj (preferably on the day before Tarwiyah, Tarwiyah, and 'Arafah) and seven days after returning home, completing ten days. Although the Quranic verse (2:196) mentions tamattu', qiran is similar because both involve combining two rituals (Hajj and 'Umrah). Thus the ruling applies by qiyas. The preferred time for fasting is delayed to the last possible moments (before Nahr) in hopes of affording the original sacrifice.

Key Terms
دم القران (dam al-qiran): The obligatory sacrifice required of a qarin (one performing Hajj and 'Umrah together) as thanks for combining the two rituals.
هَدْي (hady): Sacrificial animal (camel, cow, or sheep) offered in the Haram as part of Hajj.
بدنہ (badanah): A large sacrificial animal; in this context, specifically a camel, though the term can apply to a cow as well.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the basis for equating qiran with tamattu' regarding the obligation of sacrifice?
A) A specific hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
B) Ijma' of all scholars.
C) Qiyas: both involve benefiting from performing two rituals (Hajj and 'Umrah).
D) The verse specifically mentions qiran.

Key Takeaway
Dam al-qiran is wajib on the qarin by qiyas on tamattu', with an alternative of fasting ten days if unable to sacrifice.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate

Qiran Sacrifice and Substitute Fasting
Ruling on sacrifice for Qiran and substitute fasting

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the sacrifice (Dam al-Qiran) for the Qarin and explain the substitute fasting when unable to sacrifice.

Core Idea
The Qarin must sacrifice an animal; if unable, he must fast ten days – three during Hajj and seven after returning.

This lesson explains the obligation of sacrifice (Hadi) for a pilgrim performing Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah). The passage from Al-Hidayah establishes the ruling by analogy to Tamattu’, and details the alternative of fasting when sacrifice is not possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The act is the sacrifice (Dam al-Qiran) required from the Qarin pilgrim. The ruling is wajib (obligatory) based on the Hanafi school. If unable, fasting becomes wajib.
The sacrifice is not a rukn but a wajib; omission requires compensation.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is Quran 2:196, which commands sacrifice for Tamattu’. The Hanafi school applies this to Qiran by analogy (qiyas).
The verse's imperative 'fama istaysara min al-hady' indicates obligation according to Hanafi usul.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Qiran and Tamattu’ share the effective cause (illa): both combine Hajj and Umrah in a single journey. Thus, the ruling of sacrifice is transferred from Tamattu’ to Qiran.
This is a clear qiyas jali (evident analogy).
4
Identify the substitute ruling
If the Qarin cannot find or afford a sacrificial animal, he must fast ten days: three days during Hajj (before the Day of Sacrifice) and seven days after returning home.
The three days must be completed by the Day of Arafah.
5
Note the preferred timing
The author recommends fasting on the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah (the day before Tarwiyah, Tarwiyah, and Arafah) to delay the substitute as much as possible, hoping to be able to perform the original sacrifice.
This mirrors the recommendation for tayammum.

کتاب الحج ہے کیونکہ قرآن تمتع کے معنی میں ہے اور ہدی کی قربانی تمتع میں منصوص علیہ ہے۔ اور ہدی اونٹ، گائے اور بکری سے ہوتی ہے چنانچہ ہم اس کو انشاء اللہ اس کے باب میں ذکر کریں گے۔ اور یہاں بدنہ سے مراد اونٹ ہے۔ اگر چہ بدنہ کا لفظ اونٹ ،گائے دونوں پر بولا جاتا ہے جیسا کہ ہم نے ذکر کیا اور جس طرح اونٹ کا ساتواں حصہ جائز ہے اسی طرح گائے کا ساتواں حصہ بھی جائز ہے۔ تشریح فرماتے ہیں کہ قارن جب یوم نحر میں جمرہ عقبہ کی رمی کر چکا تو وہ ایک بکری یا گائے یا اونٹ یا بد نہ کا ساتواں حصہ قربانی کرے اور اس کا نام دم قرآن ہے۔ اس قربانی کے واجب ہونے کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ قرآن، حج اور عمرہ کو جمع کرنے میں تمتع کے معنی میں ہے اور تمتع کے اندر ہدی کی قربانی منصوص ہے چنانچہ ارشاد ہے فَمَنْ تَمَتَّعَ بِالْعُمْرَةِ إِلَى الْحَج فَمَا اسْتَيْسَرَ مِنَ الْهَدَى البَقَرَة: ١٩٢) پس جب حج تمتع میں قربانی واجب ہے تو قرآن میں بھی واجب ہوگی۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ ہدی ، اونٹ ، گائے ، بکری سب کی ہوتی ہے۔ تفصیل باب الہدی میں ذکر کی جائے گی۔ اور یہاں بدنہ سے اونٹ مراد ہے اگر چہ بد نہ کا لفظ اونٹ اور گائے دونوں پر بولا جاتا ہے پس جس طرح اونٹ کے ساتویں حصہ کی قربانی جائز ہے اسی طرح گائے کے ساتویں حصہ کی قربانی بھی جائز ہے۔ ذبح کرنے کے لئے جانور نہ پائے تو دس روزے رکھے اور کس طریقہ پر روزے رکھے جائیں گے فَإِذَا لَمْ يَكُنُ لَهُ مَا يَذْبَحُ صَامَ ثَلقَةٌ أَيَّامٍ فِى الْحَجَ اخِرُهَا يَوْمَ عَرَفَةَ وَسَبْعَةَ أَيَّامٍ إِذَا رَجَعَ إِلَى أَهْلِهِ لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَجِّ وَ سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمُ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةً فَالنَّصُّ وَإِنْ وَرَدَ فِي التَّمَتَّعِ فَالْقِرَانُ مِثْلُهُ لاَنَّهُ مُرْتَفِقَ بِأدَاءِ المُسْكَيْنِ وَالْمُرَادُ بِالْحَج وَاللهُ أَعْلَمُ وَقْته لأنَّ نَفْسَهُ لَا يُصْلِحُ ظَرْفًا إِلَّا أَنَّ الْأَفْضَلَّ أنْ يَصُومَ قَبْلَ يَوْمِ التَّرْوِيَهِ بِيَوْمٍ وَيَوْمِ التَّرُوِيَّةِ وَيَوْمٍ عَرَفَةَ لأنَّ الصَّوْمَ بَدَل عَنِ الْهَدَي فَيَسْتَحِبُّ تَأْخِيرُهُ إِلَى آخِرِ وَقْتِهِ رِجَاء أَنْ يَقْدِرَ عَلَى الْأَصْلِ
ترجمہ پس اگر قارن کے پاس ذبح کے لئے کوئی چیز نہ ہو تو تین دن کے حج میں روزے رکھے کہ آخری دن عرفہ کا دن ہو۔ اور سات روزے جب اپنے اہل میں واپس آئے کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ہے کہ جو کوئی ہدی نہ پائے تو اس پر واجب ہے تین دن کے روزے حج میں اور سات جب تم لوٹو ۔ یہ دس پورے ہوئے پس نص اگر چہ تمتع کے حق میں وارد ہوئی ہے لیکن قرآن بھی اسی کے مثل ہے کیونکہ قارن بھی حج وعمرہ دونوں نسک سے مشفع ہے۔ اور حج سے مراد واللہ اعلم اس کا وقت ہے اس لئے کہ نفس حج ظرف بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا۔ مگر افضل یہ ہے کہ یوم ترویہ سے ایک دن پہلے کا اور یوم ترویہ اور یوم عرفہ کا روزہ رکھے ۔ کیونکہ روزہ رکھنا تو ہدی کا بدل ہے پس اصل یعنی ہدی پر قدرت کی امید کے پیش نظر اس کے آخری وقت تک روزہ کو مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قارن اگر قربانی کرنے پر قادر نہ ہو بایں طور کہ گنجائش نہ ہو یا گنجائش تو ہومگر جانور دستیاب نہ ہو تو اس پر دس روزے واجب ہوں گے اس طور پر کہ تین روزے یوم نحر سے پہلے حج کے زمانہ میں رکھے اور سات روزے جب اپنے گھر واپس آئے۔ دلیل باری تعالى كا قول فمَن لَّمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلثَةِ أَيَّام فى الحجّ وَ سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُمُ تِلْكَ عَشَرَةٌ كَامِلَةً ہے۔ (البقرۃ (۱۹۹) یہ آیت اگر چہ حج تمتع کے حق میں وارد ہوئی ہے مگر چونکہ قرآن بھی اسی کے مثل ہے بایں طور کہ قارن اور متمتع دونوں حج اور عمرہ کی دو دو عبادتیں کرتے ہیں۔ پس اس مشارکت اور مماثلت کی وجہ سے جو حکم تمتع ہے وہی قرآن کا ہو گا۔ صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ آیت فصيام ثلثة اَيَّامٍ فِي الْحَج میں حج سے مراد حج کا وقت ہے۔ کیونکہ نفس حج ظرف بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتا ہے۔ حج کا وقت چونکہ شوال سے شروع ہو جاتا ہے اس لئے احرام باندھنے کے بعد جب چاہے تین روزے رکھے۔ لیکن افضل یہ ہے کہ ۷۔۸۔۹ ذی الحجہ کور کھے ۔ کیونکہ روزہ ہدی کے بدلے میں واجب ہوا ہے اس لئے روزہ کو آخر وقت تک مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے اس امید پر کہ ممکن ہے اصل یعنی ہدی پر قدرت ہو جائے جیسے فاقد الماء کے ٹیم کے ساتھ نماز کو آخر وقت تک مؤخر کرنا مستحب ہے۔
The Book of Hajj: Because Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah) has the meaning of Tamattu', and the sacrifice of Hadi is textually required for Tamattu'. And Hadi is from camel, cow, and goat. We will mention this in its chapter, Allah willing. Here 'badanah' means camel, although the word is used for both camel and cow. Just as a seventh share of a camel is permissible, so is a seventh share of a cow. Explanation: When the Qarin has thrown the pebbles at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, he should sacrifice a goat, cow, camel, or a seventh share of a badanah, and this is called 'Dam al-Qiran'. The proof for the obligation of this sacrifice is that Qiran, in combining Hajj and Umrah, has the meaning of Tamattu', and the sacrifice of Hadi is textually required for Tamattu'. Allah says: 'Whoever performs Tamattu' of Umrah to Hajj, then whatever is easy of the Hadi' (al-Baqarah 2:196). So when sacrifice is obligatory in Tamattu', it is also obligatory in Qiran. The author of Hidayah says: Hadi is from camel, cow, and goat. Details will be mentioned in the chapter on Hadi. Here 'badanah' means camel, although the word is used for both camel and cow. So just as sacrificing a seventh share of a camel is permissible, so is a seventh share of a cow. If he does not find an animal to slaughter, he should fast: three days during Hajj, the last of which is the Day of Arafah, and seven days when he returns to his family, because Allah says: 'And whoever does not find [an animal], then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete' (al-Baqarah 2:196). So the text, although revealed for Tamattu', applies similarly to Qiran because the Qarin also performs both rituals. And 'during Hajj' means, Allah knows best, its time, because the essence of Hajj cannot be a container. But the best is to fast the day before the Day of Tarwiyah, the Day of Tarwiyah, and the Day of Arafah, because fasting is a substitute for Hadi, so it is recommended to delay it to its last time hoping to be able to perform the original. Translation: So if the Qarin has nothing to slaughter, he should fast three days during Hajj, the last being the Day of Arafah, and seven days when he returns to his family, because Allah says: Whoever does not find Hadi, upon him is a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete. So the text, although revealed for Tamattu', Qiran is similar because the Qarin benefits from performing both rites. And 'during Hajj' means, Allah knows best, its time, because the essence of Hajj cannot be a container. But the best is to fast the day before the Day of Tarwiyah, the Day of Tarwiyah, and the Day of Arafah, because fasting is a substitute for Hadi, so it is recommended to delay it to its last time hoping to be able to perform the original. Explanation: The matter is that if the Qarin is not able to sacrifice, either because of lack of means or because the animal is not available, then ten fasts are obligatory upon him: three fasts before the Day of Sacrifice during the time of Hajj, and seven fasts when he returns to his home. The proof is the command of Allah: '…then a fast of three days during Hajj and seven when you return; that is ten complete' (al-Baqarah 2:196). This verse, although revealed for Tamattu', is similar for Qiran because both the Qarin and the Mutamatti' perform two acts of worship, Hajj and Umrah. So due to this participation and similarity, the same ruling applies to Qiran. The author of Hidayah says: In the verse 'fast of three days during Hajj', 'Hajj' means the time of Hajj, because the essence of Hajj cannot be a container. The time of Hajj begins from Shawwal, so after assuming ihram, he may fast whenever he wishes. But the best is to fast on the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah. Because fasting is substituted for Hadi, it is recommended to delay it to the last time hoping that the original, i.e., Hadi, may become possible, just as it is recommended for the one without water to delay prayer to the end of its time with tayammum.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran. It explains the obligation of sacrifice for the Qarin (one who performs Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram) and the alternative of fasting if one cannot afford the sacrifice. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah, commenting on the Arabic text, first clarifies the types of animals valid for Hadi: camel, cow, goat. A seventh share of a camel or cow is permissible. Then the ruling: after the Qarin throws pebbles at Jamrat al-Aqabah on the Day of Sacrifice, he must slaughter a sheep, cow, camel, or a seventh share of a badanah (camel). This sacrifice is called 'Dam al-Qiran'. The proof is that Qiran is legally analogous to Tamattu', where the Quran explicitly requires Hadi. The verse from al-Baqarah (2:196) is cited. Since the Qarin also combines Hajj and Umrah, the same obligation applies. If the Qarin cannot obtain an animal, he must fast ten days: three during the Hajj period (by the Day of Arafah) and seven after returning home. The text specifies that the three fasts must be completed before the Day of Sacrifice, with the preferred days being the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah. Delaying the fast to the last moment is recommended, hoping to be able to perform the original sacrifice. This is analogous to the one performing tayammum who delays prayer to the end of its time.

Key Terms
قارن (Qārin): A pilgrim who performs Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram, intending both at once.
هدي (Hady): The sacrificial animal offered during Hajj, especially in Tamattu' or Qiran, as a thank offering.
بدنہ (Badanah): A sacrificial camel, though the term is also used for a cow. In this passage, it specifically means camel.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must the Qarin (person performing Qiran) do if he cannot find an animal for sacrifice?
A) Perform Qada of the sacrifice later
B) Fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning home
C) Give charity equivalent to the value of the animal
D) Nothing, because sacrifice is not obligatory for Qiran

Key Takeaway
The Qarin must either sacrifice an animal or fast ten days (three during Hajj, seven after), with the preferred timing for the three fasts being the 7th, 8th, and 9th of Dhul Hijjah.

Hajj — Pilgrimage
intermediate
8 min
Fasting the Seven Days in Makkah After Hajj: Hanafi vs Shafi'i
Dispute about location of substitute fasts for Qarin

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school permits fasting the seven days in Makkah after Hajj and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on Quranic interpretation.

Core Idea
The Hanafi interpretation of 'idha raja'tum' as 'completion' permits fasting the seven days anywhere, not just at home.

After completing Tamattu' or Qiran Hajj, pilgrims must fast seven days as a substitute for the sacrificial animal. A key question is where these fasts can be performed. This lesson examines the dispute between Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding fasting in Makkah, focusing on the interpretation of the Quranic phrase 'idha raja'tum.'

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and opposing view
State the Hanafi position that fasting in Makkah after Hajj is permissible, and note that Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees.
2
Examine the Shafi'i proof
Understand the Shafi'i argument that the verse conditions the fasts upon physical return home (ruju'), and the exception for intending permanent stay.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Learn the Hanafi linguistic interpretation that 'raja'tum' means 'faraghtum' (completion of Hajj), making completion the cause for the fasts.
The cause (sabab) suffices for performance anywhere.
4
Determine the practical difference
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis allow flexibility; Shafi'is require return home unless intending permanent stay.

Source Text

وَاِنْ صَامَهَا بِمَكَّةَ بَعْدَ فَرَاغِهِ مِنَ الْحَجِّ جَازَ وَ مَعْنَاهُ بَعْدَ مَضى أَيَّامِ التَّشْرِيْقِ لأنَّ الصَّوْمَ فِيهَا مَنْهِيٌّ عَنْهُ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ لا يَجُوزُ لِأَنَّهُ مُعَلَّقَ بِالرُّجُوعِ إِلَّا أَنْ يَنوِي الْمُقَامَ فَحِينَئِذٍ يَجْزِيهِ لَتَعَدُّرِ الرُجُوعِ وَلَنَا أن مَعْنَاهُ رَجَعْتُم عَنِ الْحَجَ أَى فَرَغْتُمُ إِذَا الْفَرَاعُ سَبَبُ الرُجُوعِ إِلَى أهْلِهِ فَكَانَ الْأَدَاءُ بَعْدَ السَّبَبِ فَيَجُوزُ
ترجمہ اور اگر سات روزے حج سے فراغت کے بعد مکہ میں رکھے تو جائز ہے اور اس کے معنی یہ ہیں کہ ایام تشریق گذر جانے کے بعد ر کھے۔ کیونکہ ایام تشریق میں روزہ ممنوع ہے اور امام شافعی نے کہا کہ جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ ساتوں روزے رجوع پر معلق ہیں مگر یہ کہ وہ شخص مکہ میں ٹھہرنے کی نیت کرے تو اس وقت رجوع کے معذ ر ہونے کی وجہ سے جائز ہوگا۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ رجعتم کے معنی رَجَعْتُمْ عَنِ الْحَجَّ یعنی فَرَغْتُم کے ہیں ۔ اس لئے کہ فراغ اپنے اہل کی طرف لوٹنے کا سبب ہے۔ تو چونکہ ادا سبب کے بعد ہوئی اس لئے جائز ہے۔ تشریح پہلے مسئلہ میں کہا گیا ہے کہ سات روزے اپنے وطن لوٹنے پر رکھے گا لیکن اگر قارن نے حج سے فراغت کے بعد مکہ ہی میں سات روزے رکھ لیے تو جائز ہے مگر یہ شرط ہے کہ ایام تشریق گذر جانے کے بعد رکھے کیونکہ ایام تشریق میں روزہ رکھنا ممنوع ہے۔ حضرت امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ قارن کے لئے ان سات روز دے کا مکتہ المکرمہ میں رکھنا جائز نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول و سَبْعَةٍ إِذَا رَجَعْتُم (البقرة: ۱۹۶) میں ان سات روزوں کو رجوع پر معلق کیا گیا ہے اور رجوع اسی وقت متحقق ہوگا جبکہ یہ شخص اپنے وطن پہنچ جائے اس لئے مکہ میں ان روزوں کا رکھنا جائز نہیں ہے ہاں اگر اس نے مکہ میں قیام کی نیت کر لی تو اب مکہ میں رکھنا بھی جائز ہے کیونکہ اس صورت میں رجوع متعد رہو گیا ہے۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ باری تعالیٰ کے قول رَجَعْتُم کے معنی فرم کے ہیں یعنی جب تم حج سے فارغ ہو گئے تو سات روزے رکھ لو ۔ خواہ مکہ میں خواہ راستہ میں خواہ وطن میں پہنچ کر ۔ صاحب ہدایہ کہتے ہیں کہ حج سے فارغ ہونا اپنے اہل میں واپس آنے کا سبب ہوتا ہے پس در حقیقت یہ حج سے فراغت ہے۔ پس حج سے فراغت کے بعد جب سات روزے رکھے تو سبب کے بعد روزے پائے گئے اور سبب کے بعد جو چیز بھی پائی جاتی ہے وہ ادا ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے حج سے فراغت کے بعد یہ سات روزے بھی ادا ہو جائیں گے ۔ اگر چہ مکہ ہی میں ادا کئے ہوں۔
And if he fasts them (the seven days) in Makkah after finishing Hajj, it is permissible. Its meaning is after the days of Tashreeq have passed, because fasting during those days is prohibited. Al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible because it is tied to returning (ruju'), unless he intends to stay (in Makkah), then it would suffice due to the impossibility of returning. Our proof is that 'raja'tum' (when you return) means 'rajatum 'an al-Hajj' i.e., 'faraghtum' (you have completed), because completion is the cause of returning to one's family. So the performance (of the fast) occurred after the cause, thus it is permissible. Translation: And if he fasts the seven days in Makkah after finishing Hajj, it is permissible. Its meaning is after the days of Tashreeq have passed, because fasting during those days is prohibited. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible because the seven days are conditioned upon returning (to one's home), except if he intends to stay in Makkah, then at that time it will be permissible due to the impossibility of returning. Our proof is that the meaning of 'raja'tum' is 'you have completed Hajj', i.e., 'faraghtum'. Because completing is the cause of returning to one's family. So when the fast was performed after the cause, it is permissible. Explanation: In the previous matter, it was said that the seven fasts should be observed upon returning to one's homeland. But if the Qarin, after finishing Hajj, fasts the seven days in Makkah itself, it is permissible, but with the condition that the days of Tashreeq have passed because fasting during them is prohibited. Imam al-Shafi'i said: It is not permissible for the Qarin to fast these seven days in Makkah al-Mukarramah, because Allah's statement 'when you return' (al-Baqarah 2:196) conditions these fasts upon returning, and returning is only realized when he reaches his homeland. So fasting in Makkah is not permissible. However, if he intends to stay in Makkah, then fasting there is permissible because then returning becomes impossible. Our proof is that Allah's word 'raja'tum' means 'faraghtum', i.e., when you have completed Hajj, then fast seven days, whether in Makkah, on the way, or after reaching home. The author of Hidayah says: Completing Hajj is the cause of returning to one's family, so in reality it is completion of Hajj. So when he fasts after completing Hajj, the fast is performed after the cause, and whatever is performed after its cause is valid. Therefore, these seven fasts performed after finishing Hajj are valid, even if done in Makkah.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the location of the seven fasts for the Qarin. The Hanafi position, as explained by the author, is that it is permissible to fast the seven days in Makkah after finishing Hajj, provided the days of Tashreeq (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) have passed because fasting during those days is prohibited. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that the Quranic verse 'seven when you return' ('wa sab'atin idha raja'tum') requires the fasts to be performed after returning home. However, if one intends to stay in Makkah permanently, then fasting there becomes permissible due to the impossibility of returning. The Hanafi response is that 'raja'tum' in the verse actually means 'faraghtum', i.e., 'you have completed Hajj', not 'you have returned home'. The completion of Hajj is the cause for returning to one's family, and the obligation of fasting is tied to this completion, not to the physical act of returning. Therefore, fasting after completion of Hajj is valid anywhere, including Makkah. The author adds that this is a matter of linguistic interpretation: 'raja'tum' in Quranic usage can mean 'return from a task' i.e., completion.

Key Terms
ایام تشریق (Ayyām al-Tashrīq): The three days following the Day of Sacrifice (11th, 12th, 13th of Dhul Hijjah) during which fasting is prohibited.
رجوع (Rujū‘): Literally 'returning'. In this context, it is interpreted by Hanafis as 'completion of Hajj' (faragh), not necessarily physical return home.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when can the Qarin fast the seven days of substitute?
A) Anytime during Hajj
B) Only after returning home
C) After completing Hajj in Makkah, after the days of Tashreeq
D) Anytime in the year

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi interpretation of 'idha raja'tum' as 'when you have completed Hajj' permits the substitute fasts to be performed anywhere after Hajj, offering flexibility to pilgrims.

Missing the Three Fasts Before Yawm al-Nahr: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Ruling on missing the three fasts before Yawm al-Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a Qarin who misses the three fasts before Yawm al-Nahr and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
Missing the deadline for substitute fasts in Qiran forfeits the option to fast; only sacrifice remains.

In the Hajj of Qiran, a Qarin who cannot afford a sacrifice must fast three days during Hajj and seven after returning. But what if the three days are missed before the Day of Sacrifice? The Hanafi school holds that the time is fixed, so only the sacrifice (dam) remains. Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Malik differ. Let's examine the reasoning behind each position and the practical consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
What is the scenario? A Qarin is required to fast three days during Hajj if he cannot sacrifice. He misses these days before the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr).
The Qarin combines Hajj and Umrah.
2
State the Hanafi position and its basis
According to Hanafis, once the Day of Sacrifice arrives, only a blood sacrifice (dam) suffices. The fast cannot be made up later.
The timing of the fasts is a condition for their validity as a substitute.
3
Contrast with the Shafi'i position
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that these are timed fasts, like Ramadan, and can be made up (qada) after the specified days.
Shafi'is draw an analogy to missed Ramadan fasts.
4
Note the Maliki position
Malik holds that the fast can still be performed during the days of Tashreeq (the 11th, 12th, and 13th of Dhul-Hijjah) based on the general Quranic command.
The verse says 'three days during Hajj' which may include these days.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: Hanafis require sacrifice; Shafi'is allow fasting after Eid; Malikis allow fasting during Tashreeq.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is the sacrifice.

Source Text

وَإِنْ فَاتَهُ الصَّوْمُ حَتَّى أتى يَومُ النَّحْرِ لَم يجزهُ إِلَّا الدَّمَ وَ قَالَ الشَّافِعِيُّ يَصُومُ بَعْدَ هَذِهِ الْأَيَّامِ لِأَنَّهُ صَوْمٌ مُوقَت فَيُقْضَى كَصَوْمِ رَمَسَانَ وَقَالَ سَالِكَ يَصُوْمٌ فِيهَا لِقَوْلِهِ تَعَالَى فَمَنْ لَمْ يَجِدْ فَصِيَامُ ثَلَثَةِ أَيَّامٍ فِي
And if the fast is missed (by him) until the Day of Sacrifice comes, nothing suffices him except the blood (i.e., sacrifice). Al-Shafi'i said: He fasts after these days because it is a timed fast, so it is made up like the fast of Ramadan. And Malik said: He fasts during them (i.e., the days) because of Allah's statement: 'Whoever does not find, then a fast of three days during Hajj' (al-Baqarah 2:196).
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a dispute regarding the Qarin who fails to complete the three fasts before the Day of Sacrifice (Yawm al-Nahr). According to the Hanafi school, if the three days of fasting are missed until the Day of Sacrifice arrives, the fast is no longer valid as a substitute, and the blood sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory. It cannot be replaced by fasting after the Day of Sacrifice. Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, holding that since these are timed fasts, they can be made up (qada) later, similar to the missed fasts of Ramadan. Imam Malik holds a third view: one should still fast during the days of Tashreeq if possible, citing the general Quranic command. The Hanafi position here is that the fasts have a specific time window (before the Day of Sacrifice), and once that window closes, the obligation shifts permanently to the sacrifice. The text is cut off, but the disagreement is clear.

Key Terms
دم (Dam): A blood sacrifice (animal) required as a penalty or substitute for a missed obligation in Hajj.
قضاء (Qaḍā’): Making up a missed religious obligation after its specified time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the three fasts of Qiran are a strictly timed substitute; once the time expires, only the sacrifice remains.

Ruling on Missing Three Fast Days Before Yawm al-Nahr for Qiran
Hanafi ruling that only a dam suffices if three fasts are missed before Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the three fasts of qiran are missed before Yawm al-Nahr and explain why qada is not permitted, distinguishing the Shafi'i and Maliki positions.

Core Idea
The three fasts are a substitute for the dam; once Hajj time expires, only a dam suffices.

In Hajj rituals, a qarin who cannot offer a dam must fast three days before Yawm al-Nahr. What if he misses that deadline? The Hanafi school gives a definitive answer, but other madhhabs differ. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind the Hanafi ruling and its practical implications.

1
Identify the core issue
The issue is the fate of the three fasts if missed before Yawm al-Nahr.

Shafi'i allows qada after Tashriq; Malik allows fasting during Tashriq.

The mashhur hadith prohibiting fasting on Tashriq restricts the Quranic text; additionally, the substitute (badal) is confined to its time.
5

This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

And if the fast is missed until the day of Nahr comes, nothing suffices him except a dam. Al-Shafi'i said: He should fast after these days because it is a time-bound fast, so it may be made up like Ramadan fasts. Malik said: He should fast during them (the days of Tashriq) because Allah says 'fast three days during Hajj' and this (Tashriq) is its time. Our proof is the well-known prohibition of fasting during these days, so the text is restricted by it, or deficiency enters the fast, so what was obligatory completely cannot be performed with deficiency.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage addresses the situation where a pilgrim performing qiran (or tamattu) fails to observe the three days of fasting before Yawm al-Nahr (the day of sacrifice). According to the Hanafi school, once Yawm al-Nahr arrives, the only valid option is to offer a dam (sacrificial animal); fasting at any later time is not acceptable. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that these fasts are time-bound and should be made up after the days of Tashriq, analogizing to Ramadan qada. Imam Malik considers the days of Tashriq themselves as part of the Hajj period, thus allowing fasting then. The Hanafi response rests on two points: First, the well-known (mashhur) hadith prohibiting fasting on the days of Tashriq restricts the general Quranic permission. Second, the fasts are a substitute (badal) for the dam, and substitutes established contrary to qiyas are confined to their specific context (the time of Hajj); once that time passes, the original obligation (dam) returns. The commentary further explains that performing a deficient fast cannot fulfill a complete obligation, and that leaving the fasts results in reversion to the original requirement of a dam.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): Substitute: the three fasts serve as a substitute for the dam. Substitutes are confined to their specific time and cannot be performed outside it.
وقت الحج (waqt al-ḥajj): The time of Hajj, which for Hanafi excludes the days of Tashriq for fasting but includes them for Malik.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
If the three fasts of qiran are missed until Yawm al-Nahr, the Hanafi school requires a dam; no subsequent fasting is accepted.

Qarin's Missed Fasts: Dam vs. Qada
Hanafi position on three fasts for Qarin when missed before Nahr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on a Qarin who misses the three fasts before Yaum al-Nahr and distinguish it from the Shafi'i and Maliki positions by citing the hadith prohibition and the principle of badal.

Core Idea
A substitute (badal) cannot extend beyond its textual limit; after Hajj time, the original sacrifice revives.

This lesson examines a critical dispute about the Qarin pilgrim who misses the three fasts that serve as a substitute for the sacrificial animal (hadi). The Hanafi school insists that once Yaum al-Nahr arrives, fasting is no longer an option and a blood sacrifice (dam) becomes obligatory. We will explore the proofs from hadith, the concept of badal, and the practical consequences across madhahib.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: the Qarin must offer a dam; the three fasts cannot be made up after Yaum al-Nahr.
The ruling is based on the hadith prohibiting fasting on the Days of Tashriq.
2
Identify the opponent's view and proof
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i permits qada after Tashriq (based on qiyas with Ramadan) and Imam Malik permits fasting during Tashriq (based on the general Quranic command).
Shafi'i: qiyas; Maliki: literal reading of 'three days during Hajj'.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand that the well-known hadith of prohibition restricts the Quranic text. Also, the fasts are a badal that must stay within its specified time (time of Hajj).
Badal principle: substitutes are only valid when the Lawgiver specifies them; they don't carry over.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: Hanafi says dam is wajib; Shafi'i says qada fasts; Maliki says fast during Tashriq.
This affects a pilgrim's obligations after missing the initial fasts.

And for us is the well-known prohibition of fasting in these days, so the text is restricted by it, or deficiency enters it, so what is obligatory completely is not performed by it. And it is not performed after them because fasting is a substitute, and substitutes are not established except by a text that has specified it with the time of Hajj, and the permissibility of blood is on the original. Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute regarding a Qarin who misses the three fasts before Yaum al-Nahr. The Hanafi school holds that once Yaum al-Nahr arrives, the only option is to offer a dam (blood sacrifice); fasting is no longer sufficient. Imam Shafi'i argues that these fasts can be made up after the Days of Tashriq, similar to making up missed Ramadan fasts. Imam Malik argues that these fasts should be observed during the Days of Tashriq themselves, as those days are part of the Hajj period. The Hanafi response relies on a well-known hadith prohibiting fasting on the Days of Tashriq. This hadith restricts the general Quranic command to fast 'three days during Hajj' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:196) to days other than Tashriq. Furthermore, the Hanafi argument states that the fasts are a substitute (badal) for the Hadi, and substitutes are only valid when specifically designated by the Lawgiver; the text limits this substitute to the time of Hajj. If the fasts are not performed within the Hajj period, the ruling reverts to the original obligation of offering a sacrifice. This is supported by a narration from Umar (ra) who, in a similar case, commanded a sheep to be slaughtered.

Key Terms
بادل (badal): A substitute; here, the fasts are a substitute for the sacrificial animal (hadi).
قارن (qarin): A pilgrim performing Hajj al-Qiran (combining Hajj and Umrah with one ihram).
یوم نحر (yawm al-nahr): The 10th of Dhul-Hijjah, the day of sacrificing animals.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what must a Qarin do if he misses the three fasts before Yaum al-Nahr?
A) Fast during the Days of Tashriq
B) Fast after the Days of Tashriq
C) Offer a dam (blood sacrifice)
D) Nothing

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a Qarin who misses the three substitute fasts before Yaum al-Nahr must offer a dam; the fasts cannot be made up later because a substitute is confined to its specified time.

Qarin Unable to Afford Hadi Must Offer Two Dam
Ruling for Qarin who cannot afford Hadi and the obligation of two dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Qarin who cannot afford the hadi and identify the two obligatory dam.

Core Idea
A Qarin unable to afford hadi owes two wajib dam: one for qiran and one for premature tahallul.

This lesson presents a concise ruling from the Hanafi tradition: when a Qarin (one performing Hajj al-Qiran) cannot afford the sacrificial animal (hadi) after missing the alternative fasts, he may exit ihram but incurs two blood sacrifices (dam). Understanding this penalty is essential for fulfilling Hajj obligations correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person and scenario
Recognize that the subject is a Qarin (performing Hajj al-Qiran) who is unable to afford the hadi (sacrificial animal).
The Qarin combines Hajj and Umrah in one ihram and is originally required to sacrifice a hadi.
2
State the permission granted
The text says he becomes halal (exits ihram) even without the hadi. This is a concession (rukhsah) for hardship.
3
State the penalty incurred
Upon exiting, he owes two dam (blood sacrifices).
Dam is a sheep or goat wajib as compensation.
4
Name the two dam
The first dam is for qiran (substitute for the hadi or fasting), and the second dam is for premature tahallul (exiting ihram before sacrifice).
The text calls the first 'dam al-tamattu' but in context it is for qiran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَلَوْ لَمْ يَقْدِرْ عَلَى الْهَدْيِ تَحَلَّلَ وَ عَلَيْهِ دَمَانِ : دَمُ التَّمَتُّعِ وَ دَمُ التَّحَلُّلِ قَبْلَ الْهَدْيِ
So if he is not able to afford the hadi, he becomes halal (releases ihram) and upon him are two dam: the dam of tamattu' and the dam of becoming halal before the hadi.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This is a ruling statement for a Qarin who cannot afford the sacrificial animal (hadi) after missing the three fasts. The Qarin is allowed to exit ihram (tahallul) without having offered the hadi, but he incurs two dam: one for qiran (here mistakenly called dam al-tamattu' in the text, but in context it is for qiran) and one for exiting ihram before offering the hadi. The first dam is in place of the three fasts, and the second is a penalty for shaving or cutting nails before sacrifice.

Key Terms
حلال (halal): State of being out of ihram; permitted to do things forbidden during ihram.
دم (dam): Blood sacrifice; specifically a sheep or goat required as compensation in Hajj.
هدی (hadi): Sacrificial animal brought to the Haram during Hajj.

Ruling on the Qarin Who Goes to Arafat Without Performing Umrah
Ruling on Qarin who goes to Arafat without entering Makkah for Umrah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) who fails to enter Makkah for Umrah and goes directly to Arafat, and explain the rationale for his becoming a rejecter (rafid) of Umrah and the need for a compensatory sacrifice (dam).

Core Idea
A Qarin becomes a rejecter of his Umrah only by actually standing at Arafat, not by mere intention or turning.

This passage addresses a specific situation in the combined pilgrimage (Qiran): the Qarin must perform Umrah before Hajj. If he skips entering Makkah and proceeds to Arafat, he abandons his Umrah. The text clarifies that the rejection occurs at the moment of standing at Arafat, not by mere turning, and draws a helpful distinction from the case of Friday prayer to illustrate the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor and the situation
The ruling concerns a Qarin—someone who has entered ihram for both Hajj and Umrah together. He does not enter Makkah to perform Umrah first but instead proceeds directly to Arafat.
2
Recognize the ruling and its condition
The text states that such a Qarin becomes a rejecter (rafid) of his Umrah 'by the standing' (bi al-wuquf) at Arafat. Note: the ruling is conditional upon actual standing, not merely turning towards Arafat.
3
Understand the reasoning (ta'lil)
The reason is that by standing at Arafat, he makes it impossible to perform Umrah afterwards, because the acts of Umrah would then be built upon the acts of Hajj, which is contrary to the prescribed order (first Umrah, then Hajj).
4
Note the refinement: mere turning vs actual standing
The text explicitly adds that 'he does not become a rejecter by mere turning' and that this is the correct view from Abu Hanifa. Only the actual standing at Arafat triggers the ruling.
5
Examine the distinction from the Friday prayer case
The author draws a comparison: a person who prays Zuhr at home and then proceeds to the Friday prayer is commanded to proceed, so he is not a rejecter. In contrast, proceeding in Qiran (and Tamattu') is prohibited. This farq justifies why the Qarin becomes a rejecter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْخُلِ الْقَارِنُ مَكَّةَ وَ تَوَجَّهَ إِلَى عَرَفَاتٍ فَقَدْ صَارَ رَافِضًا لِعُمْرَتِهِ بِالْوُقُوفِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ عَلَيْهِ أَدَاؤُهَا لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ بَانِيًا أَفْعَالَ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَجِّ وَ ذَلِكَ خِلَافُ الْمَشْرُوعِ وَلَا يَصِيرُ رَافِضًا بِمُجَرَّدِ التَّوَجُّهِ هُوَ الصَّحِيحُ مِنْ مَذْهَبِ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ أَيْضًا وَالْفَرْقُ لَهُ بَيْنَهُ وَبَيْنَ مُصَلِّي الظُّهْرِ يَوْمَ الْجُمُعَةِ إِذَا تَوَجَّهَ إِلَيْهَا أَنَّ الْأَمْرَ هُنَالِكَ بِالتَّوَجُّهِ مَأْمُورٌ بِهِ بَعْدَ أَدَاءِ الظُّهْرِ وَ التَّوَجُّهُ فِي الْقِرَانِ وَ التَّمَتُّعِ مَنْهِيٌّ
For if the Qarin does not enter Makkah and proceeds to Arafat, then he has become a rejecter of his Umrah by the standing (at Arafat), because its performance has become impossible for him, since he becomes a builder of the acts of Umrah upon the acts of Hajj, and that is contrary to what is prescribed. And he does not become a rejecter by mere turning, and that is the correct view from the school of Abu Hanifa as well. And the distinction for him between this and the one praying Zuhr on Friday when he proceeds to it is that the command there is to proceed, commanded after performing Zuhr, while proceeding in Qiran and Tamattu' is prohibited.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage clarifies the ruling for a Qarin who, intending to perform both Umrah and Hajj with one ihram, fails to enter Makkah first and instead goes directly to Arafat. By standing at Arafat (the main ritual of Hajj), he effectively abandons his Umrah because performing Umrah after Hajj would be invalid—the acts of Umrah cannot be built upon the acts of Hajj, as the prescribed order is Umrah first, then Hajj. Thus he becomes a rejecter of his Umrah. However, the correct view from Abu Hanifa is that merely turning his direction towards Arafat does not make him a rejecter; the rejection only occurs by actually performing the standing at Arafat. The distinction is drawn from the case of the Friday prayer: a person who proceeds to the Friday prayer after having already prayed Zuhr at home is commanded to proceed, but in Qiran and Tamattu', proceeding to Arafat without first performing Umrah is prohibited.

Key Terms
رافض (rafid): One who abandons or rejects an act of worship; here, the Qarin rejects his Umrah by failing to perform it before Hajj.
وقف (wuquf): Standing at Arafat; a fundamental pillar of Hajj.
بان (bani): One who builds or superimposes; here, the Qarin would be building acts of Umrah upon acts of Hajj, which is invalid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When does a Qarin become a rejecter of his Umrah according to the text?
A) When he merely intends to go to Arafat
B) When he turns towards Arafat
C) When he actually stands at Arafat
D) When he returns from Arafat

Key Takeaway
A Qarin becomes a rejecter of his Umrah only by actually standing at Arafat, not by mere intention or turning, and must offer a dam as compensation.

Refutation of Shafi'i on Qada of Tamattu Fasts After Tashreeq
Rebuttal of Imam Shafi'i's view on late qada of Tamattu fasts

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that the three fasts of Tamattu cannot be made up after the days of Tashreeq and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A badal (substitute) cannot be performed outside its specified time; the sacrifice, being original, is not bound.

In this passage, the Hanafi school refutes Imam al-Shafi'i's position that the three fasts of Tamattu can be performed after the days of Tashreeq. The key is understanding the distinction between a substitute (badal) and the original act. The Shariah has tied this substitute specifically to the time of Hajj, and thus it cannot be delayed. The practice of Umar (RA) supports this view.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
The Hanafi school holds that the three fasts of Tamattu must be performed within the days of Hajj and cannot be made up after the days of Tashreeq.
This is based on the nature of the fast as a badal (substitute) for the sacrifice.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that the fasts can be made up after the days of Tashreeq.
The text does not provide his exact proof, but the Hanafi response addresses the reasoning.
3
Follow the Hanafi response
The Hanafi response argues that the fast is a badal established by nass and tied to the time of Hajj. The sacrifice, by contrast, is an original act and not a substitute.
The narration from Umar (RA) where he commands a similar situation to sacrifice a goat supports the Hanafi view.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, a Qarin who misses the three fasts during Hajj cannot make them up later; he must sacrifice an animal instead.
This shows the consequence of the legal difference.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الْأَصْلِ وَعَنْ عُمَرَانَةَ أَمَرَ فِى مِثْلِهِ بِذَبْحِ الشَّاةِ ترجمہ اور ایام تشریق کے بعد بھی ادا نہیں کئے جائیں گے کیونکہ روزہ بدل ہے اور بدلے قائم نہیں کئے جاتے مگر شریعت کی طرف سے اور نص نے اس بدل کو وقت حج کے ساتھ مخصوص کر دیا ہے اور قربانی کا جائز ہونا اپنی اصل پر ہے اور حضرت عمر سے روایت ہے کہ آپ نے ایسے واقعہ میں بکری ذبح کرنے کا حکم دیا ہے۔ تشریح اس عبات میں امام شافعی کا رد ہے بایں طور کہ مذکورہ تین روزوں کی قضا ایام تشریق کے بعد بھی درست نہیں ہے۔ کیونکہ را دم قرآن کا بدل ہے اور بدل منجانب شارع ثابت ہوتا ہے اور شرع یعنی نص نے اس کو وقت حج کے ساتھ مخصوص کر دیا ہے پس جب وقت حج کے ساتھ مخصوص ہے تو وقت حج کے بعد یعنی ایام تشریق کے بعد ان کے ادا کرنے کی اجازت نہ ہوگی۔ اور قربانی کا جائز ہونا روزہ کا بدل نہیں ہے بلکہ وہ اپنی اصل پر ہے۔ ہماری تائید اس سے بھی ہوتی ہے کہ ایک قارن بدی کا جانور قربانی نہ کر سکا اور ایام حج کے تین روزے بھی فوت ہو گئے تھے کہ یوم نحر آ گیا تو اس کو حضرت عمر نے فتویٰ دیا کہ بکری قربانی کرے یعنی بدی کا جانور دے جو اصل ہے۔
The original: And from Umar that he commanded in a similar situation to slaughter a sheep. Translation: And they will not be performed even after the days of Tashreeq because the fast is a substitute and substitutes are not established except by the Shariah, and the text (nass) has specified this substitute with the time of Hajj, and the permissibility of sacrifice is based on its original ruling. And it is narrated from Umar that he commanded in such an incident to slaughter a goat. Explanation: In this passage, there is a refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i that the qada of the three fasts is not valid after the days of Tashreeq because the dam for Qiran is a substitute, and a substitute is established by the Lawgiver, and the Shariah (i.e., the text) has specified it with the time of Hajj. When it is specified with the time of Hajj, then after that time, i.e., after the days of Tashreeq, there is no permission to perform them. And the permissibility of sacrifice is not a substitute for the fast; rather, it is based on its own original ruling. Our view is supported by the fact that a Qarin could not sacrifice his animal and the three days of fasting were missed, and when the Day of Nahr came, Umar gave a fatwa that he should sacrifice a goat, i.e., give the sacrificial animal which is the original.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of Imam al-Shafi'i's position. The issue is whether the three fasts of Tamattu' can be performed after the days of Tashreeq. The Hanafi view, supported by the practice of Umar, holds that these fasts are a specific substitute (badal) for the sacrifice, and the Shariah has tied them to the time of Hajj. Therefore, once the days of Tashreeq have passed, it is not valid to perform them. The sacrifice, on the other hand, is not a substitute but an original act of worship. The narration from Umar strengthens the Hanafi position: a Qarin who missed both sacrifice and fasts was told by Umar to sacrifice a goat (the original act), not to make up the fasts.

Key Terms
بدل (badal): A substitute act of worship, here the three fasts standing in for the sacrifice in Tamattu.
دم قرآن (dam al-qiran): The blood penalty (sacrifice) required of a Qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) They are valid, but a dam is required.
D) They are forgiven and no qada is needed.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the three fasts of Tamattu are a badal tied to the Hajj time and cannot be performed after the days of Tashreeq; instead, a sacrifice must be offered.

Qarin Unable to Afford Hadi: Exiting Ihram and Two Dams
Ruling on a Qarin's inability to sacrifice

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling for a Qarin who cannot afford the Hadi and identify the two wajib dams required.

Core Idea
A Qarin unable to sacrifice may exit ihram but must offer two dams: one for Tamattu and one for premature halal.

This lesson focuses on a specific scenario in Hajj Qiran: when a Qarin cannot afford the sacrificial animal (Hadi) after missing the compensating fasts. The Hanafi school provides clear guidance that the pilgrim may exit ihram but incurs two wajib compensations (dam). Understanding this ruling clarifies how the school balances hardship with the obligation to fulfill the ritual.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Recognize that this ruling applies to a Qarin (one combining Hajj and Umrah) who is unable to find or afford the Hadi after having missed three fasts that were a substitute for the sacrifice.
The context implies the Qarin had already missed the three fasts of Hajj.
2
Determine the ruling on exiting ihram
The text states that if he cannot afford the Hadi, he becomes halal (permitted to exit ihram). This is a concession (rukhsah) due to inability.
Exiting ihram is permissible (mubah), not obligatory.
3
Identify the two wajib dams
Upon exiting, he owes two dams: one for Tamattu (ダ้ม التمتع) because the fasts were a substitute for the Tamattu sacrifice, and one for becoming halal before the Hadi (ダ้ม التحلل قبل الهدي).
The second dam compensates for prematurely ending ihram without sacrificing.
4
Understand the wisdom (hikmah)
The two dams preserve the integrity of the Hajj: one replaces the missed sacrifice of Tamattu, the other addresses the premature termination of ihram, ensuring that all wajib acts are compensated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If he is not able to find the Hadi, he becomes halal and owes two dams. So if he does not have the power over the Hadi, he becomes halal, and upon him are two dams: the dam of Tamattu and the dam of becoming halal before the Hadi. And if the Qarin does not enter Mecca and heads towards Arafat, then he becomes a rejecter of his Umrah by standing (at Arafat), because performing it becomes impossible for him, since he becomes one who bases the actions of Umrah on the actions of Hajj, and that is contrary to the prescribed way. Explanation: The scenario is that a Qarin who missed the three fasts of Hajj, if he does not have the ability to sacrifice, then he becomes halal, i.e., he removes his ihram. Now upon him are two dams: one dam for Qiran and the other dam because he became halal before slaughtering the Hadi. The second issue is that if the Qarin, instead of performing the pillars of Umrah, goes straight to Arafat, then at the moment of standing at Arafat he becomes an abandoner of Umrah, because now for this Qarin performing Umrah has become impossible. It became impossible because if he performs Umrah after Hajj, the actions of Umrah will be based upon the actions of Hajj, while this is against the prescribed way, and the prescribed way is that the Qarin first performs Umrah and then performs Hajj.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings for a Qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah). First: if a Qarin cannot afford the sacrificial animal (Hadi) after missing three fasts, he may exit ihram (become halal) but owes two dams: one for Tamattu (because the fasts were a substitute for the sacrifice) and one for becoming halal before sacrificing. Second: if a Qarin proceeds directly to Arafat without performing Umrah, he is considered to have abandoned Umrah by standing at Arafat. This is because it would require performing Umrah after Hajj, which is not the prescribed order. The prescribed order is Umrah first, then Hajj.

Key Terms
ھدی (hady): The sacrificial animal offered during Hajj, especially for Tamattu and Qiran.
دم (dam): A blood penalty, i.e., a sacrificial animal required as compensation for missing or altering a wajib act in Hajj.
قرآن (qiran): The type of Hajj where one combines Hajj and Umrah with one ihram.
تحلل (tahallul): The act of exiting ihram, becoming halal (permitted to do previously prohibited acts).

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Two dams: one for Tamattu and one for premature halal.
C) Three dams: one for each missed fast.
D) No dam is required because he was unable to sacrifice.

Key Takeaway
A Qarin who cannot afford the Hadi may exit ihram but must offer two wajib dams: one for Tamattu and one for premature halal.

Qarin Going to Arafat Without Umrah: Abandoning Umrah
Ruling on a Qarin who skips Umrah and goes to Arafat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a Qarin who proceeds directly to Arafat without performing Umrah becomes a rejecter of his Umrah and state the Hanafi position on this action.

Core Idea
A Qarin who goes to Arafat without Umrah abandons it because performing Umrah after Hajj is invalid.

This lesson addresses a procedural error in Hajj Qiran: when a pilgrim proceeds to Arafat before performing the Umrah actions. The Hanafi ruling is that such a Qarin becomes a rejecter (rafid) of his Umrah, as it becomes impossible to perform Umrah in the correct order. Understanding this highlights the importance of sequence in the combined pilgrimage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
The Qarin does not enter Mecca to perform Umrah but heads directly to Arafat for the Hajj standing.
The Qarin has not yet performed the Umrah actions (tawaf, sa'i).
2
Determine the ruling upon standing at Arafat
By standing at Arafat, the Qarin becomes 'rafid' (rejecter) of his Umrah. The Umrah is considered abandoned.
The act of wuquf at Arafat is pivotal.
3
Understand why Umrah becomes impossible
If he were to perform Umrah after Hajj, the actions of Umrah would be based on (buniya 'ala) the actions of Hajj, which is contrary to the prescribed order (mashru'). The prescribed order is Umrah first, then Hajj.
The principle: 'buniya 'ala' means the later actions would depend on the earlier, which is invalid for two separate rituals.
4
Know the consequence
The Qarin's Qiran is effectively void; he becomes a Mufrid (performing Hajj only) and must offer a dam for the discarded Umrah (according to Hanafi fiqh, though not explicit in this passage).
The text itself only states he becomes a rejecter; additional rulings are from standard Hanafi sources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ھدی پر قادر نہ ہو تو حلال ہو جائے اور اس پر دودم لازم ہیں فَلَوْ لَمْ يَقْدِرْ عَلَى الْهَدْيِ تَحَلَّلَ وَ عَلَيْهِ دَمَانِ دَهُ التَمَتَّعُ وَ دَمُ التَحَكُل قَبْلَ الْهَدَى فَإِنْ لَمْ يَدْخُلِ الْقَارِنُ مَكَّةَ وَ توجه إلى عرفات فَقَدْ صَارَ رَافِضًا لِعُمْرَتِهِ بِالْوُقُوفِ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَدَّرَ عَلَيْهِ أدَاؤُهَا لِأَنَّهُ يَصِيرُ بَانِيَا أَفْعَالَ الْعُمْرَةِ عَلَى أَفْعَالِ الْحَج وَ ذَلِكَ خِلَافَ الْمَشْروع ترجمہ پھر اگر قارن نے ہدی پر قدرت نہ پائی تو حلال ہو جائے اور اس پر دو قربانی واجب ہیں ایک قربانی تمتع کی اور ایک بدی سے پہلے حلال ہونے کی۔ اور اگر قارن مکہ میں داخل نہ ہوا بلکہ عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہوا تو وہ اپنے عمرہ کو وقوف عرفہ کے ساتھ ترک کرنے والا ہو گیا کیونکہ اس پر عمرہ کا ادا کر نا مععد رہو گیا اس لئے کہ افعال عمرہ کو حج پر بنا کرنے والا ہو جائے گا اور یہ خلاف مشروع ہے۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قارن جس کے تین روزے حج کے فوت ہو گئے تھے اگر اس کو ہدی پر قدرت حاصل نہ ہو تو وہ حلال ہو جائے یعنی احرام کھول دے اب اس پر دو دم واجب ہوں گے ایک دم قرآن اور دوسرا دم اس لئے واجب ہوگا کہ ہدی کا جانور ذبح کرنے سے پہلے حلال ہو گیا۔ دوسرا مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قارن بجائے ارکان عمرہ ادا کئے اگر سید ھا عرفات چلا گیا تو وہ وقوف عرفہ کرتے ہی تارک عمرہ ہو گیا کیونکہ اب اس قارن کے لئے عمرہ ادا کرنا متعذر ہو گیا ہے۔ عمرہ کرنا اس لئے حعذر ہو گیا کہ اگر اس نے حج کے بعد عمرہ کیا تو افعال عمرہ کا ترتب افعال حج پر ہو گا۔ حالانکہ یہ خلاف مشروع ہے اور مشروع یہ ہے کہ قارن پہلے عمرہ ادا کرے اور پھر حج کرے۔
If he is not able to find the Hadi, he becomes halal and owes two dams. So if he does not have the power over the Hadi, he becomes halal, and upon him are two dams: the dam of Tamattu and the dam of becoming halal before the Hadi. Commentary
This passage presents two rulings for a Qarin (one who combines Hajj and Umrah). First: if a Qarin cannot afford the sacrificial animal (Hadi) after missing three fasts, he may exit ihram (become halal) but owes two dams: one for Tamattu (because the fasts were a substitute for the sacrifice) and one for becoming halal before sacrificing. This is because it would require performing Umrah after Hajj, which is not the prescribed order. The prescribed order is Umrah first, then Hajj.

Key Terms
رافض (rafid): One who rejects or abandons something; here, the Qarin who abandons his Umrah.
بنی علی (buniya 'ala): Basing one action upon another; here, performing Umrah actions based on Hajj actions.
مشروع (mashru'): Legislated, prescribed; refers to the correct order of rituals.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Abandonment of Umrah by Mere Intention and Ruling on Qiran Dam
Intra-Hanafi dispute on abandonment of Umrah by mere intention and ruling on Qiran dam

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on whether mere intention abandons Umrah for a Qarin, and state the resulting rulings on Qiran dam, dam for abandonment, and qada.

Core Idea
Mere intention does not abandon Umrah; only actual wuquf does, and then the Qiran dam drops but a dam and qada become wajib.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute: does a Qarin who heads to Arafat without performing Umrah become an abandoner? The correct view of Abu Hanifa is that only actual standing at Arafat constitutes abandonment. We also see the consequences for the Qiran dam and the obligations of dam and qada.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the correct view of Abu Hanifa regarding when a Qarin becomes an abandoner of Umrah. Note that mere intention does not suffice; only actual wuquf at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah makes him a tarik.
2
Identify the opponent's analogy
Recognize the opposing narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad, which uses qiyas with Friday prayer: just as heading to Friday prayer after Zuhr abandons Zuhr, heading to Arafat abandons Umrah.
The illa is the act of heading to a later obligation.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the distinction: in Friday prayer, heading is commanded after Zuhr; in Qiran/Tamattu, heading to Arafat before Umrah is prohibited. This difference breaks the analogy.
Hence the qiyas is invalid because the illa is not identical.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Contrast the practical outcomes: if mere intention abandons, he is tarik from the moment he heads out; if only wuquf, he is tarik only after standing at Arafat.
The mufta bihi is that only wuquf abandons.
5
Apply the ruling on dam and qada
Once Umrah is actually abandoned (by wuquf), the Qiran dam drops because he did not combine both rites. Instead, he owes a dam for abandoning the Umrah after starting it and must perform qada of Umrah.
This resembles the muhsar who also owes dam and qada.

Will one be considered an abandoner of Umrah by merely heading towards Arafat or not? And he does not become a rejecter by mere intention; that is the correct view of Abu Hanifa as well. And the distinction for him between this and the one who prays Zuhr on Friday and then heads to the Friday prayer is that the command there is to head after performing Zuhr, whereas heading towards Arafat in Qiran and Tamattu is prohibited before performing Umrah, so they differ. Translation: And by heading towards Arafat, he will not become an abandoner of Umrah; this is the correct madhhab of Abu Hanifa. And according to Imam Abu Hanifa's madhhab, the difference between this and the one who prays Zuhr on Friday and then heads to the Friday prayer is that in the Friday case, heading after performing Zuhr is commanded, whereas in Qiran and Tamattu, heading towards Arafat before performing Umrah is prohibited, so the two cases differ. Explanation: The Qarin will not be considered an abandoner of Umrah by merely heading towards Arafat; rather, he will be considered an abandoner only when he reaches Arafat after the 9th of Dhul Hijjah and stands there. The correct madhhab of Abu Hanifa is this. However, from Abu Hanifa, there is a narration of Hasan that heading towards Arafat makes Umrah abandoned. Analogy would be that just as on Friday, one who prays Zuhr at home and then merely heads to the Friday prayer, his Zuhr prayer is considered abandoned, similarly, by merely heading towards Arafat, the Qarin's Umrah would be abandoned. But according to Imam Abu Hanifa's madhhab, the reason for the distinction is that in the Friday case, when he prays Zuhr and then heads to the Friday prayer, the command to go to the Friday prayer (fas'aw ila dhikrillah) is still present, whereas in Qiran and Tamattu, heading towards Arafat before performing Umrah is prohibited. Given this difference, how can heading to Arafat be analogized to heading to Friday prayer? If he abandons Umrah, the Qiran dam drops. He said: And the Qiran dam drops from him because when his Umrah becomes invalid, he was not able to perform both rites. Upon him is a dam for abandoning his Umrah after starting it, and upon him is its qada because the start was valid, so he resembles the muhsar. Translation: Quduri said: And the Qiran sacrifice falls from his liability because when Umrah was abandoned, he was not given the ability to perform both rites. However, upon him is a sacrifice for abandoning his Umrah after starting it, and upon him is the qada of Umrah because starting it was valid. So he resembles the muhsar. Explanation: When the Qarin goes straight to Arafat without performing the pillars of Umrah, the Qiran dam drops from his liability because by abandoning Umrah, he no longer combined both acts of worship. Therefore, the dam of thanks (Qiran) is no longer wajib. However, he must make up the Umrah (qada) and owes one dam for abandoning it after starting. The dam is wajib because he abandoned it after starting, and qada is wajib because starting it was valid, just as in the case of a nafl act if abandoned, qada becomes wajib. This person resembles the muhsar (one prevented from completing Hajj/Umrah). The muhsar is one who tied ihram but was prevented due to an enemy etc., so he removes ihram, but upon him is a sacrifice and qada. Similarly, the one who abandons Umrah owes a sacrifice and qada. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage addresses two issues: first, whether a Qarin who merely intends to go to Arafat without performing Umrah is considered to have abandoned Umrah. The correct Hanafi view (from Abu Hanifa) is that mere intention does not constitute abandonment; actual wuquf at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah does. A narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that even intention abandons Umrah, but Abu Hanifa distinguishes this from the Friday prayer case where heading after Zuhr is commanded. In Qiran/Tamattu, heading to Arafat before Umrah is prohibited, so analogy fails. Second, if Umrah is actually abandoned (by wuquf), the Qiran dam drops because he no longer combined both rites. However, he owes a dam for abandoning the Umrah after starting it and must make up the Umrah (qada). This resembles the muhsar (one prevented) who also owes a sacrifice and qada.

Key Terms
تارک عمرہ (tarik al-umrah): One who abandons Umrah after having started it, here by going to Arafat without performing it.
محصر (muhsar): One who is prevented from completing Hajj or Umrah due to external factors like an enemy.
قیاس (qiyas): Analogical reasoning applied here to compare heading to Arafat with heading to Friday prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the correct view of Abu Hanifa, when does a Qarin become an abandoner of Umrah?
A) As soon as he intends to go to Arafat.
B) When he actually stands at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah.
C) When he leaves Mecca without performing Umrah.
D) When he performs any part of Hajj.

Key Takeaway
Mere intention does not abandon Umrah; only actual wuquf does, and then the Qiran dam drops but a dam for abandonment and qada become wajib.

Does a Qarin Abandon Umrah by Going to Arafat?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on qarin and Umrah abandonment

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi position on whether a qarin's turn towards Arafat abandons Umrah by distinguishing between the Friday prayer analogy and the actual rule.

Core Idea
A qarin's Umrah is not abandoned by merely heading to Arafat; only actual wuquf after zawal on the 9th abandons it.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidayah addresses a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute: when a qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) proceeds to Arafat without first performing the rites of Umrah, does his Umrah become legally abandoned? Imam Abu Hanifa's correct madhhab states that it does not—only actual wuquf after zawal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah causes abandonment. However, a narration from Hasan ibn Ziyad claims otherwise, using an analogy (qiyas) to the Friday prayer case. The passage then deconstructs this analogy by highlighting a critical difference between the two scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core legal question
What exactly is being disputed? The question is: does a qarin who sets out towards Arafat without performing the rites of Umrah become a deserter (tarik) of Umrah?
The hijjah is not that he abandons Hajj—he is proceeding to Arafat for Hajj—but that he may have abandoned the Umrah portion.
2
State the correct Hanafi position and the intra-madhhab variant
Imam Abu Hanifa's correct (sahih) madhhab: merely turning towards Arafat does not abandon Umrah. Only reaching Arafat after zawal on the 9th and performing wuquf does. The variant from Hasan ibn Ziyad (a narration from Abu Hanifa) holds that merely turning towards Arafat abandons Umrah.
The variant is from the Nawadir, not the Zahir al-Riwayah.
3
Understand the proposed analogy (qiyas)
The variant supports its view by qiyas to the Friday prayer case: just as praying Zuhr at home and then setting out for Friday prayer abandons the Zuhr, similarly setting out for Arafat after starting Umrah should abandon the Umrah.
In the Friday case, the command to go to Friday (fas'aw ila dhikrillah) overrides the previous obligation.
4
Analyze the distinction (farq) that invalidates the analogy
The correct madhhab distinguishes: in the Friday case, after Zuhr the command to go to Friday (amr) remains operative. In the Umrah case, before completing Umrah there is a prohibition (nahy) against going to Arafat. The presence of a command vs. a prohibition changes the ruling.
Illa of the Friday case is that the act of turning is done under a command; the Umrah case lacks that command.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the first view (correct) is adopted, the qarin's Umrah remains valid and he must perform it after Hajj. If the second view (narration) is adopted, the Umrah is abandoned, requiring a dam (sacrifice) and qada.
The mufta bihi is the first view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف الهدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد سوم عَنْهُ قَبْلَ أَدَاءِ الْعُمْرَةِ فَافْتَرَقَا کتاب الحج ترجمہ اور حض عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہونے سے عمرہ ترک کرنے والا نہ ہوگا یہی امام ابوحنیفہ کا صیح مذہب ہے۔ اور امام صاحب کے مذہب پر اس کے درمیان اور جمعہ کے دن ظہر پڑھ کر جمعہ کی طرف متوجہ ہونے والے کے درمیان فرق یہ ہے کہ جمعہ کے مسئلہ میں ادائے ظہر کے بعد متوجہ ہونے پر حکم متوجہ ہے اور قرآن اور تمتع کے مسئلہ میں ادائے عمرہ سے پہلے عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہونے سے اس کو منع کیا گیا ہے تو دونوں مسئلوں میں فرق ہو گیا۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ قارن عرفات کی طرف محض متوجہ ہونے سے عمرہ کا تارک شمار نہ ہوگا بلکہ تارک عمرہ اس وقت شمار ہوگا جبکہ وہ نویں ذی الحجہ کوز وال کے بعد عرفات میں پہنچا اور وقوف کیا۔ امام ابوحنیفہ کا صحیح مذہب بھی یہی ہے لیکن امام ابوحنیفہ سے حسن کی روایت یہ ہے کہ عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہونے سے عمرہ متروک ہو جائے گا۔ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ جس طرح جمعہ کے روز گھر میں ظہر کی نماز پڑھ کر جمعہ کی طرف محض متوجہ ہونے سے ظہر کی نماز ترک ہو جاتی ہے اسی طرح قارن کے عرفات کی طرف محض متوجہ ہونے سے عمرہ ترک ہو جائے گا۔ مگر امام صاحب کے مذہب پر وجہ فرق یہ ہے کہ مسئلہ جمعہ میں جب ظہر پڑھ کر جمعہ کی طرف متوجہ ہوا تو اس کو جمعہ کے لئے جانے کا خطاب فَاسْعَوْا إِلَى ذِكْرِ اللهِ (الجمعة: 9) ابھی موجود ہے اور قرآن اور تمتع کے مسئلہ میں ادائے عمرہ سے پہلے عرفات کی طرف متوجہ ہونے سے اس کو منع کیا گیا ہے پس ان دونوں مسئلوں میں اس قدر فرق کے ہوتے ہوئے توجہ عرفات کو توجہ جمعہ پر قیاس کرنا کس طرح درست ہو گا۔
Ashraf al-Hidayah, Urdu commentary of Hidayah, volume three: 'from him before performing Umrah, so they separated'. Book of Hajj. Translation: He will not be considered a deserter of Umrah merely by turning towards Arafat. This is the correct madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. And in the madhhab of Imam Sahib, the difference between him and the one who prays Zuhr on Friday and then goes to Friday prayer is that in the Friday issue, after performing Zuhr, turning towards Friday is commanded, whereas in the issue of Qiran and Tamattu', turning towards Arafat before performing Umrah is prohibited. So the two issues differ. Explanation: The issue is that a qarin is not considered a deserter of Umrah merely by turning towards Arafat; rather, he will be considered a deserter of Umrah only when he reaches Arafat after zawal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah and performs wuquf. This is also the correct madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa. However, from Imam Abu Hanifa, the narration of Hasan is that turning towards Arafat will cause Umrah to be abandoned. And analogy (qiyas) is that just as on the day of Friday, by praying Zuhr at home and merely turning towards Friday, the Zuhr prayer becomes abandoned, similarly by the qarin merely turning towards Arafat, Umrah will be abandoned. But according to the madhhab of Imam Sahib, the reason for the distinction is that in the Friday issue, when he turns towards Friday after praying Zuhr, the address to go to Friday (Surah al-Jumu'ah, verse 9) is still present, whereas in the issue of Qiran and Tamattu', turning towards Arafat before performing Umrah is prohibited. So when there is this much difference between the two issues, how can turning towards Arafat be analogized to turning towards Friday?
Source pages p. 390

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning the qarin (one performing Hajj and Umrah together) who proceeds to Arafat without first performing the rites of Umrah. The issue is whether merely heading to Arafat constitutes abandonment of Umrah. Imam Abu Hanifa's correct madhhab is that it does not; only by actually reaching Arafat after zawal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah and performing wuquf does the Umrah become abandoned. However, there is a narration from Imam Abu Hanifa via Hasan ibn Ziyad that the mere intention to go to Arafat abandons the Umrah. The passage then discusses a potential analogy (qiyas) to the case of Friday prayer: if one prays Zuhr at home and then proceeds to Friday, the Zuhr is abandoned. By similar reasoning, proceeding to Arafat might be considered abandonment of Umrah. But the distinction is made: in the Friday case, the command to go to Friday (fas'aw ila dhikrillah) remains operative; in the Hajj case, the command is actually to perform Umrah first, so going to Arafat before Umrah is a violation, not compliance. Hence the qiyas fails. The teacher should highlight that this is an example of how the Hanafi madhhab uses careful analysis of the operative cause (illa) to distinguish between seemingly similar cases.

Key Terms
قارن (qārin): One who performs Hajj and Umrah together with a single ihram.
متروک (matrūk): Abandoned; in this context, the Umrah becomes legally abandoned if the person proceeds to Arafat without performing its rites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) As soon as he leaves his residence towards Arafat
B) When he reaches Arafat before zawal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah
C) When he reaches Arafat after zawal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah and performs wuquf
D) Only if he explicitly states his intention to abandon Umrah

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, a qarin does not abandon his Umrah by merely heading to Arafat; only actual wuquf after zawal on the 9th of Dhul-Hijjah does so.
